حرمت نہیں ہے۔ الغرض زنا اگر چه من حيث الزنا منوع اور حرام ہے، مگر جب یہ ولد کا قائم مقام بن گیا تو اس کی حرمت ساقط زنا ہوگئی ، اور حرمت مصاہرت ثابت کرنے کے حق میں یہ حرام و ممنوع نہیں رہا، لہذا حرام و ممنوع چیز کو حکم شرعی کا سبب بنانے کا اعتراض احناف پر لازم نہ ہوگا۔
Will occur, then the establishment of ownership is a legal ruling. How is it attributed to usurpation? While usurpation is prohibited and inherently ugly, it should not be a cause for any legal ruling. He answers this: Although usurpation is a cause for the establishment of ownership, it is not in the sense that ownership is intended from usurpation, but in the sense that the ownership of the usurper is a condition for a legal ruling, and that legal ruling is the obligation of compensation. The ownership is a condition for the obligation of compensation because the compensation that becomes obligatory upon the usurper is for the compensation of the owner's right. When he compensates, his giving compensation necessitates that the ownership of the owner over the usurped property terminates, because compensation has gone to him; otherwise, the collection of both the substitute and the substituted would be necessary for the owner, which is invalid. When the ownership of the owner expires, the usurped property becomes the ownership of the usurper. So, as if the ownership of the usurper is a condition for the obligation of compensation. Then the ownership of the usurper is established as a condition for a legal ruling, i.e., the obligation of compensation. And whatever is a condition for a ruling is dependent on that ruling. Therefore, here the ownership of the usurper, which is the condition, will be dependent on the ruling, which is the legal ruling. And compensation is good (hasan), so that which is dependent on it, i.e., the ownership of the usurper, will also be good due to its ruling being good. In summary, the establishment of ownership from usurpation is not because usurpation is beneficial for ownership, but rather usurpation is inherently ugly, but because usurpation entails compensation upon the usurper, and for the obligation of compensation the ownership of the usurper is a condition. If the ownership of the usurper is not established, then the owner of the usurped property would own both the original and the substitute, which is not correct. Therefore, by paying compensation, the ownership of the usurper over the usurped property is established. So, in principle, because usurpation is inherently ugly, the ownership should also be inherently ugly, but since ownership is a condition for a legal ruling and the condition is dependent on the ruling, and the ruling, i.e., compensation, is unanimously good, therefore the condition, i.e., ownership, also becomes good. Similarly, zina does not necessitate: This phrase is also an answer to an objection. Its explanation is that you stated a principle: When prohibition applies to a physical act, the prohibited thing becomes inherently ugly, remaining completely unlegislated. Yet zina is a physical act, and the prohibition "Do not approach zina" came upon it, so zina is inherently ugly. How do you derive from it the prohibition of marriage relations (hurmat al-musahara), which is a legal ruling and a blessing of Allah, counted among His favors: "And He made it lineage and marriage"? From the Hanafi side, the author answers: We do not directly derive the prohibition of marriage relations from zina. Rather, zina is a cause for the sperm, and the sperm is a cause for the child. That is, from zina the sperm appears, then from the sperm the child comes into existence. In establishing prohibitions and honors, it is the child that is the origin. First, the prohibition is established in the child, i.e., the child's ancestors and descendants are forbidden to the man and woman. Then from the child, this prohibition extends to his two sides, i.e., the man and the woman: the man's ancestors and descendants become forbidden to the woman, and the woman's ancestors and descendants become forbidden to the man. Then similarly, this obligation of prohibition extends from the child to the causes of the child: just as the prohibition of marriage relations is established from the child, so too from the causes of the child, i.e., intercourse, touching with desire, looking at the private parts, etc., the prohibition is established. In short, the prohibition of marriage relations is not directly established from zina, but through the intermediary of the child. And in the child, there is no sin, excess, or prohibition. Zina is one cause for it, just as permissible marriage is a cause for a child, so too is the prohibited one a cause for a child. And when something stands in place of another: Someone might say that zina is indeed prohibited, even if the prohibition is through the intermediary of the child, but the act of zina, which is prohibited, is the cause. So he says: The prohibition of marriage relations is not directly established from zina; rather, zina acts in place of the child. And when something acts in place of another, the attributes of the substitute are not considered; rather, the attribute of the original for which it substitutes is considered. For example, in tayammum, earth is made a substitute for water. So the attribute of earth is not considered; the attribute of earth is filthiness, soiling – it would make things dirty instead of purifying. But its attribute of filthiness is not considered; rather, the attribute of the original, i.e., water, which is its being a purifier, is considered. Similarly, here when zina becomes in place of the child, the attribute of zina, which is prohibition, is dropped; it is not considered. Rather, the attribute of the original, i.e., the child, is considered, and in the child there is no prohibition. In short, although zina as zina is prohibited and forbidden, when it becomes in place of the child, its prohibition is dropped, and in terms of establishing the prohibition of marriage relations, it is no longer prohibited and forbidden. Thus the objection that a prohibited and forbidden thing cannot be a cause for a legal ruling does not apply to the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 148

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi response to two objections regarding the ability of prohibited acts to serve as causes for legal rulings. The first objection concerns usurpation (ghasp): how can the forbidden act of usurpation result in the transfer of ownership, which is a lawful ruling? The Hanafi answer is that the ownership is not directly from the usurpation; rather, the usurper's payment of compensation (daman) necessitates that the usurper become owner to avoid the owner holding both the property and its substitute. The compensation is a good ruling, and the ownership is merely a condition for it, deriving its goodness from the ruling. The second objection concerns fornication (zina): how can the forbidden act of zina cause the prohibition of marriage relations (hurmat al-musahara), which is a blessing? The Hanafi answer is that zina does not directly cause the prohibition; instead, zina produces sperm, which produces a child, and the child is the cause of the prohibition. The child's relationship with the parents and their relatives creates the prohibition. Moreover, zina acts in place of the child (qiyam maqam al-walad) when establishing the prohibition, so the prohibition attaches by way of substitution. Just as tayammum uses earth as a substitute for water, ignoring the earth's natural property, here the prohibition of zina is ignored when it substitutes for the child. Thus, the prohibited act becomes a cause for a ruling not by its own nature but by being a condition or a substitute for a permissible element. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that a prohibited act can have indirect legal effects through necessity or substitution.

Key Terms
حکم شرعی (hukm shari'): A ruling from the Lawgiver concerning the actions of the responsible persons, such as obligation, prohibition, etc.
قائم مقام (qa'im maqam): Standing in place of another; acting as a substitute where the attribute of the substitute is ignored and the attribute of the original is considered.
ضمان (daman): Compensation or guarantee; the obligation to pay compensation for a lost or damaged property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why does the ownership of the usurper become good (hasan) despite the usurpation being prohibited?
A) Because usurpation itself is not inherently ugly.
B) Because ownership is a condition for compensation, which is a good ruling.
C) Because the owner agrees to the transfer.
D) Because the usurper repents from the sin.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school demonstrates that prohibited acts can indirectly cause lawful rulings through the mechanisms of condition (shart) and substitution (qa'im maqam), preserving the integrity of the prohibition while fulfilling legal necessities.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
intermediate
6 min
Qasr al-Salat: Rukhsah as Pure Isqat without Choice
Establishing that qasr for a traveler is obligatory, not optional

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rationale for why qasr is obligatory, using the concepts of isqat mahd and the condition of yusr in rukhsah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument from qiyas to fasting.

Core Idea
Qasr for a traveler is not optional — it is pure isqat of the full obligation, and choice exists only when both rukhsah and 'azimat offer ease.

In this passage, the author establishes that a traveler must shorten the four-rak'ah prayers and has no choice to pray full. He bases this on two key principles: (1) qasr is a 'pure dropping' (isqat mahd) like forgiving a right, and (2) a rukhsah is only optional when the alternative ('azimat) also offers some ease (yusr). Since completing four rak'ahs offers no ease, the rukhsah becomes obligatory. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and contrasts it with the Shafi'i position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal dispute
Determine the ikhtilaf between Hanafis and Shafi'is: Is qasr for a traveler obligatory or optional? Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
Hanafi: qasr is lazim; Shafi'i: traveler may choose.
2
Understand isqat mahd
Analyze the author's claim that qasr is pure isqat (isqat mahd) by analogy to forgiving qisas. Explain why this precludes the traveler from rejecting the rukhsah.
Isqat mahd = no possibility of radd; contrast with sadaqah involving tamlik.
3
Apply the condition of yusr
Explore the first proof from the meaning of rukhsah: when only the rukhsah has yusr (ease), the rukhsah becomes obligatory. Why is there no yusr in completing four rak'ahs?
The author argues no reward or ease in completing; thus qasr is determined.
4
Consider the second proof from servitude
Understand the argument that giving choice without yusr in the 'azimat contradicts 'ubudiyyah (servitude), since a servant's acts always have purpose.
Only Allah's acts are free of purpose (gharad).
5
Refute the opposing qiyas
Examine the Shafi'i analogy to a traveler's fasting and the Hanafi rebuttal: fasting involves ta'khir (postponement), not isqat, and yusr exists on both sides.
Also distinguish: Jumu'ah vs. Zuhr is not analogous.

صدقہ جس میں تملیک کا احتمال نہ ہو اسقاط محض ہوتا ہے، یعنی جس چیز کا مالک بنانا ممکن نہ ہو اس کا صدقہ اسقاط ہوتا ہے، لہذا مسافر سے عزیمت کو ساقط کر دیا گیا، اور جو چیز اسقاط کے قبیل سے ہو اس میں رد کا احتمال نہیں ہوتا ہے ، یعنی بندہ کی طرف سے رد نہیں ہو سکتی ، چاہے وہ قبول کرے یا نہ کرے جیسے قصاص کو معاف کرنا یہ اسقاط ہے، لہذا اس میں رد کا احتمال نہ ہوگا ، صاحب حق نے جب قصاص معاف کر دیا تو قصاص ساقط ہو گیا ، چاہے قاتل قبول کرے یا نہ کرے بلکہ رد بھی کرے گا تو رد نہ ہوگا۔ الغرض قصر صلوۃ اسقاط محض ہے تو اس میں رد کا احتمال نہ ہوگا، بلکہ مسافر پر قصر لازم اور عزیمت ساقط ہو جائے گی، کیونکہ نماز کو صدقہ کہا اور اس میں تملیک نہیں ہوسکتی ہے، ہاں جہاں تملیک ہوسکتی ہو یعنی مالک بنانا ممکن ہو تو ایسی چیز کا صدقہ رد کرنے سے رد ہو جائے گا، جیسے قرض خواہ نے مدیون سے قرض معاف کر دیا، یوں کہا کہ میں نے قرض کا صدقہ کر دیا تو مدیون اس کو رد کر سکتا ہے، کیونکہ قرض تملیک کے قبیل سے ہے۔
قصر صلوۃ کو اسقاط محض ثابت کرنے پر دوسرا استدلال معنی رخصت سے ہے ، معنی رخصت سے مصنف اللہ نے دو طرح سے استدلال کیا ہے۔
پہلا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ جب رخصت حقیقیہ ثابت ہوتی ہے تو بندے کو رخصت اور عزیمت دونوں پر عمل کا اختیار حاصل ہوتا ہے، کیونکہ جیسے رخصت میں یسر ہے، ایسے ہی عزیمت میں بھی یسر ہوتا ہے، یا ثواب اور بلندی درجات کے اعتبار سے یسر ہوتا ہے جیسے کلمہ کفر پر اکراہ کیا گیا، تو عزیمت تو یہ ہے کہ نہ کہے، چاہے جان چلی جائے ، اور رخصت یہ ہے کہ زبان سے کہنے کی اجازت ہے، یہاں بندے کے لئے رخصت اور عزیمت دونوں میں یسر ہے، رخصت میں تو یسر یہ ہے کہ جان بچ جائے گی، اور عزیمت میں یسر یہ ہے کہ نہ کہنے پر قتل کیا گیا تو شہادت کا درجہ ملے گا یہ بھی یسر ہے، کام کو آسان بنا دیتا ہے، آدمی ثواب اور بلندی درجات کے لئے بڑی بڑی قربانیاں دیتا ہے، یا تو عزیمت میں اور طرح سے یسر ہوتا ہے، جیسے مسافرو مریض کو رمضان میں روزہ نہ رکھنے کی رخصت ہے تو رخصت میں تو یسر یہ ہے کہ وہ روزے نہ رکھے گا تو اس کے لئے آسانی ہوگی، اور عزیمت میں یسر یہ ہے کہ ابھی روزہ کا ماحول ہے، مسلمانوں کی موافقت میں روزہ رکھنا آسان ہے، بعد میں قضاء شوار ہوگی۔ تو دونوں میں یسر ہے اس لئے اس کو اختیار دیا گیا۔ اب اگر کسی جگہ عزیمت میں کوئی یسر نہ ہو، صرف رخصت میں ہی یسر ہو، تو وہاں بندے کو اختیار نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ یسر رخصت میں متعین ہے، لہذا رخصت لازم اور عزیمت ساقط ہو جائے گی، یہاں قصر صلوۃ میں یہی صورتِ حال ہے کہ قصر میں یسر متعین ہے، عزیمت یعنی چار رکعت پڑھنے میں کوئی یسر نہیں، نہ ثواب زیادہ ہے نہ کوئی اور یسر ہے، لہذا رخصت لازم ہو جائے گی اور عزیمت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
معنی رخصت سے دوسرا طریق استدلال یہ ہے کہ اگر بندہ کو قصر اور اکمال میں اختیار دیا جائے جب کہ عزیمت میں کسی طرح سے یسر نہیں ہے، تو یہ شان عبدیت کے خلاف ہے، کیونکہ بندہ کا کوئی فعل غرض اور نفع سے خالی نہیں ہوتا، یہ تو صرف اللہ کی شان ہے کہ اس کے کسی کام میں غرض ونفع وابستہ نہیں ہوتا، لہذا اختیار نہ ہوگا، قصر متعین ہوگا ، اور پوری نماز پڑھنا درست نہ ہوگا۔ بخلاف الصوم : - امام شافعی اللہ نے قصر صلوۃ کو مسافر کے روزے پر قیاس کیا تھا، مصنف اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ مسافر کے روزے میں رخصت کی جو نص وارد ہوئی ہے وہ روزے کی ادائیگی کے مؤخر ہونے کو بتلا رہی ہے، یعنی مسافر ا بھی روزہ نہ رکھے بعد میں قضا کر لے، کیونکہ فعدة من ايام اخر کہا گیا، روزہ کو صدقہ نہیں کہا گیا، لہذا روزے میں عزیمت ساقط نہ ہوگی، بلکہ عزیمت بھی باقی رہے گی، کیونکہ روزے کو مؤخر کیا گیا ہے، اور بھی مؤخر کو معجل کیا جاسکتا ہے، جیسے دین مؤجل مدت سے پہلے دیا جا سکتا ہے، اور زکوۃ حولان حول سے پہلے ادا ہو سکتی ہے، برخلاف قصرِ صلوۃ کے کہ اس کو تو صدقہ قرار دیا گیا جس سے عزیمت بالکل ساقط ہو جاتی ہے، لہذا یہ قیاس درست نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ دونوں میں فرق ہے، مسافر کے روزے میں یسر متعارض ہے، یسر کا تعارض ہے یعنی یسر دونوں طرف ہے، رخصت میں بھی ہے اور موافقت مسلمین کی وجہ سے عزیمت میں بھی یسر ہے، لہذا یسر اور رفق کی طلب کے لئے مسافر کو اختیار دیا جائے گا، اور قصر صلوۃ میں یسر دونوں طرف نہیں ہے، صرف قصر میں یسر ہے لہذا یہاں قصر متعین ہوگا۔ وَلَا يَلْزَمُ الْعَبْدَ الْمَأْذُونَ فِي الْجُمْعَةِ لِاَنَّ الْجُمْعَةَ غَيْرُ الظُّهْرِ وَلِهَذَا لَا يَجُوْزُ بِنَاءً أَحَدِهِمَا عَلَى الْأَخَرِ وَعِنْدَ الْمُغَايَرَةِ لَا يَتَعَيَّنُ الزِفْقُ فِي الْأَقَلِ عَدَدًا وَأَمَّا ظُهْرُ الْمُسَافِرِ وَالْمُقِيمِ وَاحِدٌ فَبِالتَّخْبِيْرِ بَيْنَ الْقَلِيْلِ وَالْكَثِيرِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ شَيْ مِنْ مَعْنَى الرفق
ترجمہ :۔ اور اعتراض لازم نہیں آئے گا اس غلام کا جس کو جمعہ کی اجازت دی گئی ، اس لئے کہ جمعہ ظہر کے علاوہ ہے، اور اسی وجہ سے جائز نہیں ہے ان دونوں میں سے ایک کی بنا دوسرے پر اور مغایرت کے وقت رفق متعین نہیں ہوتا ہے کم عدد والے میں، اور بہر حال مسافر اور مقیم کی ظہر ایک ہے تو قلیل اور کثیر کے درمیان اختیار دینے سے رفق کا کچھ بھی معنی متحقق نہ ہوگا۔
A sadaqah in which there is no possibility of tamlik (transfer of ownership) is pure isqat (dropping). That is, the sadaqah of something which cannot be made owned is isqat. Therefore, the 'azimat (full obligation) is dropped from the traveler. And something that is of the category of isqat, there is no possibility of rejection (radd) from the servant; it cannot be rejected, whether he accepts or not. For example, forgiving qisas (retaliation) is isqat, so there is no possibility of rejection. When the rightful claimant forgives qisas, the qisas is dropped, whether the killer accepts or rejects; even if he rejects, it will not be rejected. In short, the shortening of prayer is pure isqat, so there is no possibility of rejection; rather, shortening is binding upon the traveler and the 'azimat is dropped, because prayer is called sadaqah and tamlik cannot occur in it. But where tamlik is possible, i.e., ownership can be transferred, then the sadaqah of such a thing can be rejected. For example, a creditor forgives a debt from the debtor, saying 'I have given the debt as sadaqah', the debtor can reject it, because debt is from the category of tamlik.
The second proof for establishing that qasr al-salat is pure isqat is from the meaning of rukhsah. The author infers from the meaning of rukhsah in two ways.
The first method: When a genuine rukhsah is established, the servant has the option to act upon either the rukhsah or the 'azimat, because just as there is yusr (ease) in the rukhsah, similarly there is also yusr in the 'azimat — either in terms of reward and elevation of ranks, as when one is coerced into uttering words of kufr; the 'azimat is not to utter it even if life is lost, and the rukhsah is to allow uttering it to save life. Here there is yusr in both: in the rukhsah, yusr is that life is saved; in the 'azimat, yusr is that if killed for not uttering, one attains martyrdom. This also is yusr, making the matter easy — people make great sacrifices for reward and high ranks. Or there is yusr in the 'azimat in another way, as a traveler or sick person has rukhsah not to fast in Ramadan. In that rukhsah, yusr is that he does not fast, giving him ease; in the 'azimat, yusr is that the fasting atmosphere is present — fasting in conformity with Muslims is easy, and making it up later will be difficult. So there is yusr in both, hence he is given choice. Now if in some matter there is no yusr in the 'azimat, only in the rukhsah, then the servant has no choice, because yusr is confined to the rukhsah. Thus the rukhsah becomes obligatory and the 'azimat is dropped. Here, in qasr al-salat, the situation is that yusr is confined to shortening; in the 'azimat, i.e., praying four rak'ahs, there is no yusr — neither greater reward nor any other ease. Hence the rukhsah becomes obligatory and the 'azimat is dropped.
The second method of inference from the meaning of rukhsah: If the servant were given a choice between shortening and completing when there is no yusr in the 'azimat at all, this would be contrary to the dignity of servitude, because no action of a servant is devoid of purpose and benefit — that is only the attribute of Allah, that His actions are not associated with purpose and benefit. Therefore, there will be no choice; shortening will be determined, and praying the full prayer will not be correct. Contrary to siyam (fasting): Imam al-Shafi'i analogized qasr al-salat to a traveler's fasting. The author is replying that the text regarding the traveler's rukhsah indicates postponement of the fast — i.e., the traveler should not fast now and make it up later, because it is said 'a number of other days' — fasting is not called sadaqah. So in fasting, the 'azimat is not dropped; rather the 'azimat remains, because the fast is postponed, and something postponed can be brought forward, like a deferred debt can be paid before the term, and zakat can be paid before the year completes. Unlike qasr al-salat, which is deemed sadaqah, causing the 'azimat to be completely dropped. Hence this analogy is not correct, because there is a difference. In the traveler's fasting, yusr is conflicting — there is yusr on both sides: in the rukhsah and, due to conformity with Muslims, also in the 'azimat. So for the sake of yusr and facility, the traveler is given choice. But in qasr al-salat, yusr is not on both sides; only in shortening is yusr. Therefore shortening is determined. And it is not binding upon the slave given permission to attend Jumu'ah, because Jumu'ah is other than Zuhr, and therefore one cannot be built upon the other. And when there is difference, facility is not determined in the lesser number. But the Zuhr of a traveler and a resident is one, so giving a choice between the lesser and greater does not realize any meaning of facility.
Translation: The objection concerning the slave given permission for Jumu'ah is not binding, because Jumu'ah is other than Zuhr, and therefore it is not permissible to base one upon the other. And when there is difference, facility is not determined in the lesser number. But the Zuhr of traveler and resident is one, so giving a choice between the lesser and greater does not realize any meaning of facility.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the Hanafi position that a traveler must shorten the four-rak'ah prayers (qasr) and has no choice to pray the full four rak'ahs. The author first establishes that qasr is a 'pure isqat' — it is like a sadaqah that drops the obligation entirely, with no possibility of rejection by the servant. He contrasts this with acts that involve tamlik (transfer of ownership), like forgiving a debt, which can be rejected. Then he provides two proofs from the meaning of rukhsah (concession). The first proof: In genuine concessions where both the rukhsah and the 'azimat have some ease (yusr), the servant may choose. But if only the rukhsah has ease (as in qasr, where no benefit is seen in praying four rak'ahs), then the rukhsah is obligatory. The second proof: If there is no ease in the 'azimat, giving a choice would be contrary to the nature of a servant, whose actions always have some purpose; only Allah's acts are purposeless. Thus choice is eliminated. Finally, the author refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's analogy between qasr and a traveler's fasting. The difference is that fasting involves postponement (ta'khir), not isqat, so the 'azimat remains and the servant may choose to fast or postpone. In qasr, the obligation is dropped entirely. Additionally, in fasting there is ease on both sides, so choice is given; in qasr, ease is only in shortening. The author also addresses a potential objection regarding a slave given permission for Jumu'ah: since Jumu'ah is a different prayer from Zuhr, the principle does not apply; but for qasr, the prayer is the same (Zuhr), so the choice would be between a lesser and greater number, which negates the very meaning of facility.

Key Terms
إسقاط محض (isqat mahd): A pure dropping of an obligation with no possibility of rejection or transfer of ownership.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession granted by the Lawgiver due to necessity or hardship, which may be either optional or obligatory depending on the presence of ease (yusr) in the alternative.
عزيمة (azimat): The original, complete obligation, which may be dropped partially or fully by a rukhsah.
يُسْر (yusr): Ease, facility, or benefit. In this context, a factor that makes an option acceptable or preferable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the Hanafi arguments for qasr being obligatory as presented in the passage?
A) Qasr is called sadaqah, which is pure isqat.
B) There is no ease (yusr) in completing four rak'ahs.
C) The Quranic verse 'wa idha darabtum fi al-ardi' explicitly commands shortening.
D) Giving a choice would be contrary to the dignity of servitude.

Key Takeaway
Qasr for a traveler is obligatory because it is pure isqat of the full obligation, and a rukhsah becomes binding when only it offers ease.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
advanced
8 min
Ease Designation When Obligations Differ in Kind
Applies rule of ease designation to slave's Jumu'ah and vow of fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when two obligations differ in legal kind (mukhtalifan hukman), ease in the lesser does not make it binding, and identify the practical consequence (ikhtiyar vs ta'yin).

Core Idea
When obligations differ in kind, ease in one does not force it—choice remains.

This passage from Al-Husami's commentary explores a key nuance in the principle of ease (rufq) in Hanafi usul. While a general rule suggests that if only one obligation contains ease, it becomes binding, the text clarifies that this only applies when the obligations are of the same legal kind. When they differ (e.g., Jumu'ah vs Zuhr, or kaffarah vs nazr), the mukallaf retains a choice.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle of ease
The text begins by stating: if both obligations have ease, choice is given; if only one has ease, it becomes determined. This is the baseline rule.
2
Recognize the objection to the rule
The objector points to the case of a slave permitted for Jumu'ah: Jumu'ah is easier (2 rak'ahs) than Zuhr (4 rak'ahs), so the principle should make Jumu'ah mandatory, yet the Hanafi school gives choice.
The objection is based on an apparent inconsistency.
3
Identify the Hanafi response: difference in kind
The Hanafi answer is that Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different legal kinds (mukhtalifan hukman). Therefore, ease in the lesser is not determinative because the greater may also have ease (e.g., Zuhr has no sermon, no travel). Hence choice remains.
The key distinction: same kind vs. different kind.
4
Apply the same reasoning to the nazr/kaffarah case
A destitute person who broke a vow has a choice between fasting three days (kaffarah) and a year (nazr). Although three days is easier, the two obligations are different in kind (one is expiation, the other worship), so choice is given.
This is derived on the same basis, supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.
5
Note the alternative view that removes the objection
If one adopts the opinion that a slave permitted for Jumu'ah is obligated to pray Jumu'ah (no choice), then the objection disappears entirely. The commentator cites this as a possible resolution.
This shows multiple valid positions within the Hanafi school.

عزیمت دونوں میں یسر ہو تو اختیار دیا جائے گا، اور اگر ایک میں یسر ہو تو اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا، بلکہ یسر والی چیز پر عمل کرنا متعین ہو جائے گا، حالانکہ اس مسئلہ میں آپ اصول توڑ رہے ہیں، کہ جب غلام کو آقا نے جمعہ پڑھنے کی اجازت دی، تو آپ کہتے ہیں کہ غلام کو جمعہ اور ظہر پڑھنے میں اختیار ہوگا، چاہے جمعہ پڑھے، چاہے ظہر پڑھے، حالانکہ یہاں جمعہ میں رفق ویسر متعین ہے، ظہر میں یسر نہیں ہے، کیونکہ یہ چار رکعت ہے اور جمعہ دو رکعت ہے، تو جمعہ متعین ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ جمعہ میں ہی رفق ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حضرت والا ! جمعہ اور ظہر دو الگ الگ چیزیں ہیں، اسی لئے جمعہ ظہر کی نیت سے ادا نہیں ہوتا، اور نہ ظہر جمعہ کی نیت سے، اسی طرح جمعہ پڑھنے والا ظہر پڑھنے والے کی اقتدا نہیں کر سکتا، اور نہ اس کا برعکس، پس جب دونوں میں مغایرت ہے تو رفق قلیل میں متعین نہیں ہوسکتا، ہو سکتا ہے کثیر میں بھی رفق ہو، ہاں جب دونوں ایک ہی جنس ہوں تو تقلیل میں کثیر کے مقابلہ میں رفق ہو سکتا ہے، جیسے مسافر کی چار رکعت، اور دو رکعت، لیکن جب دونوں چیزیں الگ الگ ہوں تو قلیل میں رفق کا تعین نہیں ہو سکتا، کثیر میں بھی ہو سکتا ہے جیسے یہاں جمعہ میں رفق قلیل ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے کہ یہ دو ہی رکعت ہے، اور ظہر میں جو کثیر ہے اس میں بھی رفق ہے، اس طرح کہ ظہر میں خطبہ نہیں ہے، سعی الی الجمعہ نہیں ہے، لہذا جب رفق دونوں میں ہے، تو غلام کو جمعہ اور ظہر کا اختیار دیا اور ہمارا زیر بحث مسئلہ یعنی مسافر کی ظہر قصر اور مقیم کی چار رکعت یہ دونوں ایک ہی ہیں، اسی لئے مقیم و مسافر دونوں ایک دوسرے کی اقتدا کر سکتے ہیں، جب دونوں ایک ہی ہیں تو قلیل میں یعنی دو رکعت میں رفق متعین ہوگا، چار رکعت میں کوئی رفق نہیں ہے، تو مسافر کو دو رکعت پڑھنا متعین ہو جائے گا، قصر اور اکمال میں اختیار نہ ہوگا۔ یہ ساری تقریر تو اس صورت میں ہے جب عبد ماذون فی الجمعہ کو جمعہ اور ظہر میں اختیار حاصل ہو۔۔ لیکن صاحب نامی شارح حسامی نے غایۃ التحقیق کے حوالہ سے لکھا ہے کہ عبد ماذون فی الجمعہ پر جمعہ لازم ہے، اس کو اختیار نہیں ہے، اگر ایسی صورت ہے تو پھر کوئی اعتراض ہی نہیں ہے۔
وَعَلَى هَذَا يُخَرَّجُ مَنْ نَذَرَ بِصَوْمٍ سَنَةٍ إِنْ فَعَلَ كَذَا وَهُوَ مُعْسِرٌ يُخَيَّرُ بَيْنَ صَوْمِ ثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ وَبَيْنَ سَنَةٍ فِي قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ وَهُوَ رِوَايَةٌ عَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ قَبْلَ مَوْتِهِ بِثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ لِأَنَّهُمَا مُخْتَلِفَانِ حُكْمًا أَحَدُهُمَا قُرْبَةٌ مَقْصُودَةٌ وَالثَّانِي كَفَّارَةٌ وَفِي مَسْأَلَتِنَا هُمَا سَوَاءٌ فَصَارَ كَالْمُدَبَّرِ إِذَا جَنَى لَزِمَ مَوْلَاهُ الْأَقَلُّ مِنَ الْأَرْشِ وَمِنَ الْقِيمَةِ بِخِلَافِ الْعَبْدِ لِمَا قُلْنَا.
ترجمہ: اور اسی اصول پر ( کہ مغایرت کے وقت قلیل میں رفق متعین نہیں ہوتا) تخریج کیجائے گی، اس مسئلہ کی کہ کسی نے نذر مانی ایک سال کے روزے کی اگر اس نے فلاں کام کیا، پس اس نے وہ کام کر لیا، اور شخص تنگدست ہے تو اس کو اختیار دیا جائے گا تین دن کے روزوں اور ایک سال کے روزوں کے درمیان امام محمد کے قول میں، اور یہی امام ابو حنیفہ کی روایت ہے، امام ابو حنیفہ نے اس قول کی طرف رجوع کر لیا تھا اپنی وفات سے تین دن پہلے، اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں ( تین دن کے روزے اور ایک سال کے روزے) مختلف ہیں حکماً، ان میں سے ایک عبادت مقصودہ ہے، اور دوسرا کفارہ ہے، اور ہمارے مسئلہ میں دونوں برابر ہیں، پس یہ مدبر کی طرح ہو گیا جب اس نے کوئی جنایت کی تو اس کے مولی پر لازم ہوگا ارش اور قیمت میں سے جو قلیل ہوگا، برخلاف غلام کے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی۔ تشریح : ۔ مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ ماقبل میں ایک مسئلہ پر جو اعتراض ہوا ایسا ہی ایک مسئلہ اور ہے، جس سے ہمارے اوپر اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے لیکن اس کا جواب بھی ایسا ہی ہے جو ماقبل کے مسئلہ میں ہم نے دیا۔ اعتراض کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ آپ کا اصول ہے کہ دو چیزوں میں سے ایک میں رفق متعین ہو، دوسرے میں رفق نہ ہو، تو بندہ کو اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا بلکہ رفق والی چیز متعین ہو جائے گی حالانکہ آپ اس مسئلہ میں اختیار دیتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی نے نذر مانی کہ اگر میں نے فلاں کام کیا تو میرے ذمہ ایک سال کے روزے ہیں، اب اس نے فلاں کام کر لیا، یعنی قسم میں حانث ہوگیا، اور یہ شخص تنگدست ہے مالی کفارہ، یعنی غلام آزاد کرنا یا دس مساکین کو کھانا، کپڑا دینے پر قادر نہیں ہے، تو امام محمد اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے قول کے مطابق اس شخص کو اختیار ہے کہ قسم کے کفارے کے تین روزے رکھ لے، یا نذر کے لحاظ سے ایک سال کے روزے رکھے، تو تین دن کے روزے اور ایک سال کے روزوں میں کیا جوڑ ہے، جو آپ نے اختیار دیا، تین دن کے روزے جو قلیل ہیں اس میں یسر ورفق ہے، اور ایک سال کے روزے جو کثیر ہیں اس میں کوئی رفق نہیں ہے، تو آپ کے اصول کے مطابق قلیل یعنی تین دن کے روزے متعین ہونے چاہئیں نہ کہ اختیار دیا جائے۔ یہاں بھی وہی جواب دیں گے جو ہم پہلے دے آئے کہ تین دن کے روزے اور ایک سال کے روزے اگر چہ صورتاً ایک ہیں مگر حکماً الگ الگ ہیں، کیونکہ ایک سال کے روزے نذر کے روزے ہیں جو عبادت مقصودہ ہے، اور تین دن کے روزے کفارے کے ہیں، جو حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے بطور عقوبت کے ہیں، تو دونوں میں مغایرت ہے، اور پہلے ہم نے بتایا کہ دو چیزیں جب الگ الگ جنس کی ہوں تو قلیل میں رفق متعین نہیں ہوتا، کثیر میں بھی کسی جہت سے رفق ہو سکتا ہے، ہاں جب دونوں ایک جنس ہوں تو قلیل میں رفق متعین ہوگا، اور یہاں دونوں چیزوں میں مغایرت ہے، لہذا قلیل میں رفق متعین نہ ہوگا بلکہ دونوں میں رفق ہوسکتا ہے، پس تین دن
If both have ease, choice is given; if only one has ease, no choice is given, rather the one with ease becomes determined. However, in this issue you break the principle: when a slave is given permission by his master to pray Jumu'ah, you say the slave has choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr, whether he prays Jumu'ah or Zuhr, even though here ease and leniency are determined in Jumu'ah, and there is no ease in Zuhr because it is four rak'ahs and Jumu'ah is two rak'ahs, so Jumu'ah should be determined because ease is only in Jumu'ah. The answer is: O sir! Jumu'ah and Zuhr are two different things; therefore Jumu'ah is not performed with the intention of Zuhr, nor Zuhr with the intention of Jumu'ah; similarly, the one praying Jumu'ah cannot follow the one praying Zuhr, nor vice versa. So when there is difference (mukhalafah) between them, ease in the lesser cannot be determined; there may also be ease in the greater. Yes, when both are of the same kind, then ease in the lesser can be in comparison to the greater, like the traveler's four rak'ahs and two rak'ahs. But when the two things are separate, ease in the lesser cannot be determined; there may also be ease in the greater, like here Jumu'ah has ease because it is only two rak'ahs, and Zuhr which is greater also has ease because Zuhr has no sermon, no going to Jumu'ah. So when there is ease in both, the slave is given choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr. And our issue under discussion, i.e., the traveler's shortened Zuhr and the resident's four rak'ahs, are the same; therefore resident and traveler can follow each other. When both are the same, then ease in the lesser, i.e., two rak'ahs, becomes determined; there is no ease in four rak'ahs, so the traveler must pray two rak'ahs; there is no choice between shortening and completing. This entire discussion is when the slave permitted for Jumu'ah has choice between Jumu'ah and Zuhr. But the author of the commentary on Al-Husami, citing Ghayat al-Tahqiq, wrote that Jumu'ah is obligatory on a slave permitted for Jumu'ah; he has no choice; if that is the case, there is no objection at all. And on this basis is derived the case of one who vowed to fast a year if he does such-and-such, and he is destitute: he is given a choice between fasting three days and a year in the opinion of Muhammad, and it is a narration from Abu Hanifa that he returned to it three days before his death, because the two are different in legal ruling: one is an intended act of worship, the other is expiation; and in our issue they are equal, so it becomes like the mudabbar who commits a crime: his master is liable for the lesser of the blood-wit or the value, contrary to the slave, for what we said. Translation: And on this same principle (that at the time of difference, ease in the lesser is not determined) is derived this issue: someone vowed to fast a year if he did a certain thing, then he did that thing, and the person is destitute; so he is given a choice between fasting three days and a year according to Imam Muhammad, and this is a narration from Abu Hanifa that he returned to this opinion three days before his death, because these two (three days of fasting and a year) are different in ruling: one is an intended act of worship, the other is expiation; and in our issue they are equal, so it becomes like the mudabbar who commits a crime: his master is liable for the lesser of the blood-wit or the value, contrary to the slave, for the reason we stated. Explanation: The author says that just as there was an objection on the previous issue, similarly there is another issue on which an objection arises against us, but its answer is the same as we gave in the previous issue. The objection is: your principle is that when ease is determined in one of two things and not in the other, the person is not given choice; rather the thing with ease becomes determined. Yet in this issue you give choice: a man vowed that if he did a certain thing, he would fast a year; he did that thing, i.e., he broke his oath, and this person is destitute, unable to pay financial expiation (freeing a slave or feeding/clothing ten poor people). So according to Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa, this person has a choice: he may fast three days as expiation for the oath, or fast a year for the vow. What connection do three days of fasting have with a year that you give choice? Three days of fasting are few and have ease and leniency, while a year is much and has no ease; so according to your principle, the lesser, i.e., three days of fasting, should be determined, not choice given. Here too we will give the same answer we gave before: that three days of fasting and a year, although similar in form, are different in legal ruling, because one year of fasting is a vowed fast which is an intended act of worship, while three days of fasting are expiatory, which are a punishment for breaking an oath. So there is difference (mukhalafah) between them, and we previously explained that when two things are of different kinds, ease in the lesser is not determined; there may be ease in the greater as well from some perspective. But when both are of the same kind, then ease in the lesser becomes determined. Here there is difference between the two things, so ease in the lesser is not determined; rather ease may be in both. So three days...

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on Al-Husami's matn in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, expanding on the principle of determining the easier option when two obligations conflict. The passage presents a rule: if two obligations both contain ease (rufq), the mukallaf is given choice; if only one contains ease, that one becomes binding (ta'yin). However, the principle is refined: when the two obligations are of different legal kinds (mukhtalifan hukman), ease in the lesser does not force its selection, because the greater may also possess ease from another perspective. This is illustrated with two cases. The first case: a slave given permission by his master to attend Jumu'ah. According to the Hanafi position (as presented here), the slave has a choice between praying Jumu'ah (2 rak'ahs) and Zuhr (4 rak'ahs), even though Jumu'ah appears easier (fewer rak'ahs). The critic objects that this violates the rule that the easier option should become mandatory. The commentator answers that Jumu'ah and Zuhr are different types of obligations (one is Jumu'ah, the other is a regular Zuhr), so the lesser ease in Jumu'ah does not negate the presence of ease in Zuhr (Zuhr does not require a sermon, traveling to the mosque, etc.). Hence choice remains. In contrast, when the obligations are of the same kind, like a traveler's shortened prayer (2 rak'ahs) and a resident's full prayer (4 rak'ahs), both are Zuhr, so ease in the lesser (2 rak'ahs) is determined and the traveler must shorten. The second case involves a destitute person (mu'sir) who vowed to fast a year if he does a certain act, and then he does it (breaking his oath). According to a narration from Imam Muhammad and a later return by Abu Hanifa, he has a choice between fasting three days (as kaffarah for the oath) or fasting a year (as fulfillment of the nazr). The critic objects that three days is easier, so it should be mandatory. The answer is that the three days are kaffarah (a punishment) while the year is an act of worship ('ibadah maqsudah); they are different in legal nature, so the ease in the lesser does not force its selection; both may contain ease from their respective perspectives. The passage also notes an alternative view that a slave permitted for Jumu'ah is obliged to attend Jumu'ah with no choice, which would resolve the objection entirely. Throughout, the commentary follows a dialectical style: raising an objection based on a perceived inconsistency, then providing a nuanced response that upholds the madhhab's consistency.

Key Terms
رفق (rufq): Ease, leniency, or reduced burden in performing an obligation; a factor in determining whether the easier option becomes binding
مغایرت (mukhalafah): Difference in legal kind or category between two obligations (e.g., Jumu'ah vs. Zuhr, or nazr vs. kaffarah)
اختیار (ikhtiyar): Choice granted to a mukallaf between two valid options when both contain ease and are of different legal kinds

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi principle discussed in the passage, when may a mukallaf be given a choice between two obligations even though one is apparently easier?
A) When the easier obligation is shorter in duration or less effort
B) When the two obligations are legally different in kind (e.g., Jumu'ah vs. Zuhr)
C) When the mukallaf is a slave
D) When the harder obligation is an expiation

Key Takeaway
When obligations differ in legal kind, ease in the lesser does not force its selection; the mukallaf is given choice because both may contain ease from different perspectives.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
intermediate
10 min
The Hanafi Principle of Rafq: Leniency Between Obligations of Different Kinds
Applying the usul principle of rafq to a nazr case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of rafq (leniency) to determine whether a mukallaf is given a choice between two obligations or the smaller one is obligatory, based on whether the obligations are of the same legal kind or different.

Core Idea
When obligations differ in legal kind, leniency is not forced in the smaller; when same kind, the smaller is mandatory.

In Hanafi usul, leniency (rafq) is a key consideration when a person faces two alternative obligations. The principle distinguishes between obligations of the same legal kind (jins wāḥid) and those of different kinds (mukhtalif). This lesson explores the rule through a case of nazr (vow) and kaffarah (expiation), where a poor man vowed to fast one year if he broke an oath. The passage applies the principle to determine whether he must choose the smaller obligation (three days of fasting) or has a choice between the two.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
Extract the usul rule from the passage: when two obligations are of the same kind, leniency is determined in the smaller, making it obligatory. When they differ in kind, leniency is not determined in either, so the person is given a choice.
The principle applies to any pair of obligations, e.g., in prayer, fasting, or compensation.
2
Classify the Obligations in the Nazr Case
Determine the legal kind of each obligation: the three-day fast is kaffarah (penalty for breaking an oath), the one-year fast is a vowed worship (ibādah maqṣūdah). They are different kinds.
Even though both involve fasting, their legal nature differs – one is punishment, the other is devotion.
3
Apply the Principle
Since they differ, the smaller (three days) is not automatically obligatory. Both have a form of leniency: three days are few, one year has great reward. Hence the person is given a choice.
This is the position of Imam Muhammad and the later view of Imam Abu Hanifa.
4
Contrast with the Same-Kind Scenario
Compare with the traveler’s prayer: qasr (shortening) and ikmal (completing) are the same kind (both are ṣalāh). Therefore, the smaller (qasr) is obligatory, and the traveler has no choice.
Also compare with the mudabbar case: paying value vs compensation is same kind ⇒ lesser is obligatory; handing over the slave vs compensation is different kind ⇒ choice.
5
Note the Conditions
The choice in the nazr case applies only if: (i) the vow was attached to a condition the person does not desire, and (ii) the person is financially constrained (mu‘sir).
If the person is wealthy, financial expiation is due, and the fasting option disappears.

تنگدست ہے تو اس کو اختیار دیا جائے گا تین دن کے روزوں اور ایک سال کے روزوں کے درمیان امام محمد کے قول میں ، اور یہی امام ابو حنیفہ کی روایت ہے، امام ابو حنیفہ علیہ نے اس قول کی طرف رجوع کر لیا تھا اپنی وفات سے تین دن پہلے ، اس لئے کہ یہ دونوں ( تین دن کے روزے اور ایک سال کے روزے) مختلف ہیں حکما ، ان میں سے ایک عبادت مقصودہ ہے، اور دوسرا کفارہ ہے، اور ہمارے مسئلہ میں دونوں برابر ہیں ، پس یہ مدبر کی طرح ہو گیا جب اس نے کوئی جنایت کی تو اس کے مولی پر لازم ہوگا ارزش اور قیمت میں سے جو قلیل ہوگا، برخلاف غلام کے اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم ۔ بیان کی۔ تشریح : ۔ مصنف اللہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ماقبل میں ایک مسئلہ پر جو اعتراض ہوا ایسا ہی ایک مسئلہ اور ہے، جس سے ہوا ہمارے اوپر اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے لیکن اس کا جواب بھی ایسا ہی ہے جو ماقبل کے مسئلہ میں ہم نے دیا۔ اعتراض کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ آپ کا اصول ہے کہ دو چیزوں میں سے ایک میں رفق متعین ہو، دوسرے میں رفق نہ ہو، تو بندہ کو اختیار نہیں دیا جائے گا بلکہ رفق والی چیز متعین ہو جائے گی حالانکہ آپ اس مسئلہ میں اختیار دیتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی نے نذر مانی کہ اگر میں نے فلاں کام کیا تو میرے ذمہ ایک سال کے روزے ہیں، اب اس نے فلاں کام کر لیا، یعنی قسم میں حانث ہوگیا، اور یہ شخص تنگدست ہے مالی کفارہ ، یعنی غلام آزادکرنا یا دس مساکین کوکھانا، کپڑا ادینے پر قادر نہیں ہے، تو امام محمد اور امام ابو حنیفہ عاللہ کے قول کے مطابق اس شخص کو اختیار ہے کہ قسم کے کفارے کے تین روزے رکھ لے، یا نذر کے لحاظ سے ایک سال کے روزے رکھے، تو تین دن کے روزے اور ایک سال کے روزوں میں کیا جوڑ ہے، جو آپ نے اختیار دیا ، تین دن کے روزے جو قلیل ہیں اس میں ٹیسر ورفق ہے، اور ایک سال کے روزے جو کثیر ہیں اس میں کوئی رفق نہیں ہے، تو آپ کے اصول کے مطابق قلیل یعنی تین دن کے روزے متعین ہونے چاہئیں نہ کہ اختیار دیا جائے۔ یہاں بھی وہی جواب دینگے جو ہم پہلے دیگر آئے کہ تین دن کے روزے اور ایک سال کے روزے اگر چہ صورۃ ایک ہیں مگر حکما الگ الگ ہیں، کیونکہ ایک سال کے روزے نذر کے روزے ہیں جو عبادت مقصودہ ہے، اور تین دن کے روزے کفارے کے ہیں، جو حانث ہونے کی وجہ سے بطور عقوبت کے ہیں، تو دونوں میں مغایرت ہے، اور پہلے ہم نے بتایا کہ دو چیزیں جب الگ الگ جنس کی ہوں تو قلیل میں رفق متعین نہیں ہوتا، کثیر میں بھی کسی جہت سے رفق ہو سکتا ہے، ہاں جب دونوں ایک جنس ہوں تو قلیل میں رفق متعین ہوگا، اور یہاں دونوں چیزوں میں مغایرت ہے، لہذا اقلیل میں رفق متعین نہ ہو گا بلکہ دونوں میں رفق ہوسکتا ہے، پس تین دن کے روزوں میں تو یہ رفق ہے کہ قلیل ہیں ، صرف تین دن ہیں، اور ایک سال کے روزوں میں اس لحاظ سے رفق ہے کہ یہ عبادت مقصودہ ہیں، جس میں عقوبت کا کوئی معنی نہیں ہے، اس کی فضیلت اور ثواب زیادہ ہے، درجات اور فضیلت کے سبب بڑی بڑی قربانیاں آدمی پر آسان ہو جاتی ہیں، لہذا جب دونوں میں رفق موجود ہے تو بندہ کو اختیار دیا جائے گا۔۔ اور ہمارے زیر بحث مسئلہ میں قصرِ صلوۃ اور اکمال صلوۃ دونوں ایک ہی ہیں، لہذا یہاں قلیل میں رفق متعین ہوگا، تو مسافر کو اختیار نہ ہوگا بلکہ قصر کرنالازم ہوگا۔ مصنف اللہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس کی ایک اور نظیر دے رہے ہیں کہ کسی مد بر غلام نے کوئی جنایت کی ، یعنی کسی کا مال ہلاک کر دیا تو مولی پر اس کا تاوان آئے گا، تاوان میں غلام کی قیمت اور اُرش یعنی ( جنایت کا جرمانہ ) دونوں میں سے جو کم ہوگا وہ واجب ہوگا، کیونکہ غلام کی قیمت اور جرمانہ دونوں ایک ہی جنس ہیں، لہذا اقل میں رفق متعین ہے، جیسے غلام کی قیمت پانچ ہزار ہے، اور ارش (جرمانہ ) چار ہزار ہے تو مولی پر چار ہزار لازم ہوں گے، اور اگر غلام نے جو نقصان کیا ہے اس کا ارش چھ ہزار ہے، تو مولی پر غلام کی قیمت یعنی پانچ ہزار لازم ہونگے ، کیونکہ قیمت اور ارش ایک ہی جنس ہیں تو رفق قلیل میں متعین ہے، اسی طرح قصر صلوۃ اور اکمال صلوۃ ایک ہی جنس ہیں تو قلیل میں یعنی قصر میں رفق متعین ہے، لہذا قصر لازم ہو گا۔ ہاں اگر آقا غلام کی قیمت نہیں دے رہا ہے بلکہ نفس غلام کو دے رہا ہے تو پھر آقا کو اختیار ہوگا کہ غلام اور ارش (جرمانہ ) میں سے جو چاہے دے، چاہے غلام کی قیمت ارش سے کم ہو یا زیادہ ، کیونکہ یہاں دونوں چیزیں یعنی غلام اور ارش الگ جنس ہیں، دونوں میں مغایرت ہوگئی ، تو اب قلیل میں رفق متعین نہ ہوگا بلکہ دونوں میں ہوسکتا ہے، جیسے غلام کی قیمت پانچ ہزار ہے اور جرمانہ چار ہزار ہے، تو یہاں دونوں میں رفق ہوسکتا ہے کیونکہ دونوں چیزیں الگ الگ ہیں، ارش میں تو رفق یہ ہے کہ وہ کم ہے چار ہزار ہے، اور غلام دینے میں بھی رفق ہے باوجود یہ کہ اس کی قیمت زیادہ ہے، اس لحاظ سے کہ آقا اس سے تنگ آ گیا ہے تو غلام کو دینا آسان ہے۔ مَنْ نَذَرَ - مصنف نے کہا کہ اختیار ہے تین دن کے اور ایک سال کے روزوں میں تو یہ اختیار اس تو صورت میں ہے جب وہ ایسی شرط سے معلق کرے جس کے وقوع کو وہ نہ چاہتا ہو، اگر ایسی شرط ہے جس کے وقوع کو چاہتا ہے تو اختیار نہ ہوگا بلکہ ایک سال کے روزے یعنی نذر پورا کرنا ضروری ہوگا، جیسے نذر مانی کہ اگر اللہ نے مجھے شفا دی تو ایک سال کے روزے رکھوں گا، تو شفا سے معلق کیا اور شفا ایسی چیز ہے جس کے وقوع کو آدمی چاہتا ہے، لہذا یہاں نذر پورا کرنا ضروری ہے۔ وهو معسر : - اگر وہ مالدار ہے تو اس کو کفارہ مالی دینا ہے پھر وہ تین دن کے روزے سے کفارہ نہ دے گا، لہذا تین دن اور ایک سال کے درمیان اختیار نہ ہوگا۔
Translation: And upon this principle (that when there is difference, leniency is not determined in the smaller) is to be derived the ruling of the case: someone vowed to fast one year if he does a certain act, then he did that act, and he is financially constrained, so he will be given a choice between three days of fasting and one year of fasting according to the statement of Imam Muhammad, and this is also the narration of Imam Abu Hanifa; Imam Abu Hanifa returned to this statement three days before his death, because these two (three days of fasting and one year of fasting) are different in legal nature: one is a worship intended for itself, and the other is an expiation. And in our case, both are equal. So this became like the mudabbar when he committed a crime, then upon his master is incumbent the lesser of the value or the compensation, unlike the slave, due to the evidence we mentioned. Explanation: The author says that in the previous topic, an objection was raised; similarly there is another case which causes an objection to arise against us, but its answer is also like the one we gave in the previous topic. The objection is: Your principle is that if of two things one has leniency and the other has no leniency, then the servant will not be given a choice, but rather the thing with leniency is determined. Yet in this case you give a choice to a person who vowed: if I do such-and-such, upon me is one year of fasting; then he did that act, i.e., he broke his oath, and he is financially constrained, unable to pay financial expiation (freeing a slave or feeding ten poor people or clothing them). According to Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Hanifa, this person has a choice: either fast three days as expiation for the oath, or fast one year as vow. What connection is there between three days of fasting and one year of fasting that you gave a choice? Three days of fasting are small, they have ease and leniency, while one year of fasting has no leniency. So according to your principle, the small, i.e., three days of fasting should be determined, not that a choice is given. Here also we will give the same answer we gave before: that three days of fasting and one year of fasting, although in form they are the same, but in legal nature they are separate, because one year of fasting is a vow fasting, which is an intended worship, and three days of fasting are expiation, which are a penalty due to breaking the oath. So there is difference between them, and we previously explained that when two things are of different kinds, leniency is not determined in the smaller; the larger may also have leniency in some respect. Yes, when both are of the same kind, leniency is determined in the smaller. And here there is difference between the two things, therefore leniency is not determined in the smaller; rather, both may have leniency. So the three days of fasting have leniency because they are few, only three days, and the one year of fasting has leniency because it is an intended worship, which has no sense of penalty; its virtue and reward are great, and due to virtues and ranks, great sacrifices become easy for a person. Therefore, when both have leniency, the servant will be given a choice. And in the case under discussion, shortening prayer (qasr) and completing prayer (ikmal) are the same kind, hence leniency is determined in the smaller, so the traveler has no choice but must shorten. The author says: He gives another analogy: if a mudabbar slave commits a crime, i.e., destroys someone's property, then upon the master is its compensation; from the slave's value and the compensation (the fine for the crime), whichever is less becomes obligatory. Because the slave's value and the compensation are of the same kind, leniency is determined in the lesser. For example, if the slave's value is five thousand and the compensation is four thousand, then four thousand are due on the master. And if the crime's compensation is six thousand, then the master must pay the slave's value, i.e., five thousand, because the value and compensation are the same kind, so leniency is determined in the smaller. Similarly, qasr and ikmal are the same kind, so leniency is determined in the smaller, i.e., qasr, thus qasr is obligatory. However, if the master is not paying the slave's value but is handing over the slave himself, then the master has a choice: he may give whichever he wishes between the slave and the compensation, whether the slave's value is less or more than the compensation, because here the two things, i.e., the slave and the compensation, are of different kinds; there is difference (mugheyara). Therefore, leniency is not determined in the smaller; rather, both may have leniency. For example, if the slave's value is five thousand and the compensation is four thousand, here both may have leniency because they are separate things: the compensation has leniency in being less (four thousand), and giving the slave also has leniency, even though his value is greater, because the master has become weary of him, so giving the slave is easy. "Whoever vows...": The author said that there is a choice between three days and one year of fasting only when he attaches it with a condition whose occurrence he does not desire. If it is a condition whose occurrence he desires, then there is no choice, but rather fulfilling the one-year vow is obligatory. For example, he vowed: if Allah gives me cure, I will fast one year. He attached it to cure, and cure is something a person desires, so here fulfilling the vow is obligatory. "And he is constrained": If he is wealthy, then he must give financial expiation; he will not expiate with three days of fasting, so there is no choice between three days and one year.
Source pages p. 174

Commentary
This passage is a detailed application of an usul principle concerning the determination of leniency (rafq) when a person has a choice between two obligations. The principle states: if two obligations are of the same kind (jins), the smaller (aqall) one becomes obligatory because leniency is determined in it; if they are of different kinds, leniency is not determined in either, so the person is given a choice. The author provides a case: someone vows to fast one year if he does a certain act, then does it. If he is unable to pay the financial expiation for breaking the oath (because he is in financial difficulty), according to Imam Muhammad and the later view of Imam Abu Hanifa (who reverted to this opinion three days before his death), he has a choice between fasting three days as expiation and fasting one year as his vow. An objector argues that since three days of fasting are clearly more lenient (fewer days), they should be automatically required, not left to choice. The answer is that although both involve fasting, they are different in legal nature: the one-year fast is an intended worship (ibadah maqsudah), while the three-day fast is a penalty (kaffarah). Therefore, they are of different kinds, and each has its own form of leniency: the three days are short, the one-year has great reward and virtue. Hence a choice is given. The author then compares this to the case of a traveler's prayer: qasr (shortening) and ikmal (completing) are the same kind, so qasr is obligatory. Another analogy is the mudabbar slave who commits a crime: if the master pays the value or compensation, whichever is less is due because both are monetary; but if the master can hand over the slave himself, the master has choice because the slave and the compensation are different kinds. Finally, conditions are mentioned: the choice only applies if the vow is attached to a condition the person does not desire (e.g., 'if I go to that place' which he dislikes) and if he is financially constrained. If he is wealthy, he must pay financial expiation and cannot substitute fasting.

Key Terms
رفق (rafq): Leniency or ease; the consideration of which of two options is easier for the obliged person.
مغایرت (mugheyarat): Difference in kind or legal nature between two things.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who will be freed upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does a traveler not have a choice between qasr (shortening) and ikmal (completing) prayer?
A) Because qasr is always easier than ikmal.
B) Because both are of the same kind, so leniency is determined in the smaller (qasr).
C) Because the traveler must always shorten.
D) Because ikmal has no leniency.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of rafq (leniency) distinguishes between obligations of the same kind (where the smaller is obligatory) and different kinds (where a choice is given), ensuring that ease is not automatically forced when obligations differ in legal nature.

The Mastur's Report on Najasah: Like a Fasiq
Settling an intra-madhhab dispute on mastur's report in najasah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi positions on the reliability of a mastur's report regarding najasah, identify the relied-upon view, and apply the istihsan-based rule in a purity scenario.

Core Idea
The mastur's report on najasah is treated like a fasiq's — rejected until probity is proven.

This passage from Kitab al-Istihsan addresses a disagreement among the Hanafi imams about how to treat the report of a person of unknown moral character (mastur) when he claims water is impure. Imam Muhammad holds that such a report is not accepted, likening the mastur to an open sinner (fasiq); a conflicting view from Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad considers the mastur like an upright person (adil). The correct, relied-upon position is that of Imam Muhammad, meaning the water is treated as pure until proven otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed case
Determine the specific issue: whether a mastur's report of najasah (impurity) in water is accepted or rejected in Hanafi law.
The mastur's moral character is unknown, unlike adil (known just) or fasiq (known sinner).
2
State the conflicting positions
Identify the two views: Imam Muhammad's position (from Kitab al-Istihsan) that the mastur is like a fasiq, and the narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that he is like an adil.
The opposing view is weaker and not relied upon.
3
Examine the reliance (tarjih)
The text explicitly says 'wa huwa al-sahih' (and it is the correct), indicating that Imam Muhammad's view is the mufta bihi position.
The principle of ihtiyat (caution) in ritual purity supports rejecting the report of an unknown person.
4
Apply the practical consequence
If a mastur reports that water is najis, what is the ruling? According to the relied-upon view, the water is considered pure (since the report is not accepted), so wudu with it is valid and tayammum is not required.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical difference between the two opinions.
5
Reflect on the usul principle
This rule is derived from istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides strict analogy (qiyas) that might otherwise treat the mastur as credible by default.
Istihsan here prioritizes caution in matters of purity over the general principle of accepting reports from unknown persons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فِي كِتَابِ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّهُ مِثْلُ الْفَاسِقُ فِيهِ وَهُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
In Kitab al-Istihsan: that he (the mastur) is like the fasiq in it, and that is the correct (position).
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf regarding the status of a mastur (a person whose moral character is unknown) who reports najasah (impurity) of water. The text quotes Imam Muhammad (al-Shaybani) in his Kitab al-Istihsan: the mastur is like a fasiq (open sinner) in this matter, and this is the correct view. The Urdu commentary explains that there is a conflicting narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa that the mastur is like an adil (just person). However, the author sides with Imam Muhammad, meaning the mastur's testimony is not accepted until his probity becomes evident, so one can perform wudu with the water (assuming it is pure) and need not do tayammum. The lesson type is a usul rule about the conditions of khabar (report) acceptance.

Key Terms
المستور (al-mastūr): A person whose moral probity (adālah) is unknown; neither known to be upright nor openly sinful.
الفاسق (al-fāsiq): An open sinner whose testimony is rejected in religious matters.
الاستحسان (al-istiḥsān): Preferring a ruling based on public interest or necessity over strict analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in this passage, how is a mastur treated when he reports najasah of water?
A) Like an adil, his report is accepted without investigation.
B) Like a fasiq, his report is rejected and the water is considered pure.
C) Like a child, his report is only accepted with a witness.
D) Like a kafir, his report is accepted if he is dhimmi.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that a mastur's report regarding najasah is rejected like a fasiq's, due to the principle of caution (ihtiyat) and istihsan.

Ruling on Reports from Fasiq, Kafir, Child, and Insane
Explaining the effect of extreme reports: fasiq requires taharrī, while kafir/child/insane are ignored.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reports from a fasiq versus a kafir/child/insane regarding najasah of water, and explain the underlying principle of legal competence (taklif) and probity (adalah).

Core Idea
A fasiq's report can justify tayammum through taharrī; a kafir, child, or insane person's report has zero legal weight for tayammum.

In this passage, Imam Muhammad clarifies a key usul principle: the legal impact of a report depends on the reporter's credibility and legal capacity. A fasiq (open sinner) lacks probity (adalah) but can still be believed through taharrī, whereas a kafir, child, or insane person lacks legal competence (taklif) entirely. This distinction affects whether one may perform tayammum based on their report. Let's examine the precise ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of reporters
The passage distinguishes between a fasiq and three others: kafir, child, and insane. Notice the different language used for each.
2
Understand the consequence for each category
For the fasiq: the listener performs taharrī; if convinced, tayammum allowed without spilling water (spilling is extra precaution). For the others: even if convinced, wudu must be performed with the water; spilling then tayammum is only afdal (better) but not required.
The word 'afdal' (أفضل) indicates a non-obligatory recommendation.
3
Analyze the underlying usul principle
The difference lies in the conditions for testimony: a fasiq lacks 'adalah but has taklif, so his report can be weighed; a kafir lacks both 'adalah and taklif in religious matters, a child and insane lack taklif and hence their reports are null evidence.
This is derived from the general rule that testimony requires probity and legal competence.
4
Apply the rule to derive the practical outcome
When a fasiq reports najasah, one must investigate and if convinced, tayammum is valid. For the other three, the report is ignored; only if the water is physically removed (by spilling) can tayammum be performed as a last resort.
Spilling the water creates a situation of genuine water absence, allowing tayammum regardless of the reporter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ فِى الْفَاسِقِ يُخْبِرُ بِنِجَاسَةِ الْمَاءِ أَنَّهُ يُحَكِّمُ السَّامِعُ رَايَهُ فَإِن وَقَعَ فِي قَلْبِهِ أَنَّهُ صَادِقُ يَتَيَمَّمُ مِنْ غَيْرِ إِرَاقَةِ الْمَاءِ فَإِنْ أَرَاقَ وَتَيَمَّمَ فَهُوَ اَحْوَطُ لِلتَّيَمُمِ وَفِي خَبْرِ الْكَافِرِ وَالصَّبِيِّ وَالْمُعْتُوْهِ إِذَا وَقَعَ فِي قَلْبِ السَّامِعِ صِدْقُهُمْ بِنِجَاسَةِ الْمَاءِ يَتَوَضَّاءُ وَلَا يَتَيَمَّمْ فَإِنْ أَرَاقَ الْمَائَ ثُمَّ تَيَمَّمَ فَهُوَ أَفْضَلُ
And Muhammad said concerning the fasiq who reports najasah of water: that the listener makes his opinion the judge; if it occurs in his heart that he (the fasiq) is truthful, he performs tayammum without spilling the water. If he spills and performs tayammum, it is more precautionary for tayammum. And concerning the report of the kafir, the child, and the insane person: when the truthfulness of them becomes established in the heart of the listener regarding najasah of water, he performs wudu and does not perform tayammum. If he spills the water then performs tayammum, it is better.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage expands on the ruling for reports from different categories of people in the context of najasah of water. Imam Muhammad states that when a fasiq (open sinner) reports that water is najis, the listener must engage in taharrī (personal investigation/reflection). If he becomes convinced in his heart that the fasiq is truthful, he may perform tayammum without spilling the water, as the conviction makes the water effectively nonexistent for purification. However, it is more precautionary (ahwat) to spill the water and then do tayammum to remove all doubt. For a kafir (unbeliever), a child (sabī), or an insane person (ma'tūh), even if the listener is convinced of their truthfulness, he must still perform wudu with the water and cannot perform tayammum based on their report. The reason is that these three categories are not legally competent witnesses in Sharīʿah; their reports carry no evidentiary weight. However, if the listener spills the water (thereby making it unavailable) and then does tayammum, it is considered afdal (better) because then he genuinely has no water. So the difference is: the fasiq's report can lead to tayammum through taharrī, while the other three cannot. This lesson illustrates a usul rule about the conditions of testimony and the concept of taharrī.

Key Terms
التحري (al-taḥarrī): Personal investigation and reflection to reach a dominant opinion (ghalabat al-zann) about a matter.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or cannot be used.
المعتوه (al-ma'tūh): A person with a mental deficiency who lacks full legal capacity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a fasiq reports that water is najis, what must the listener do according to Imam Muhammad?
A) Immediately spill the water and perform tayammum.
B) Perform taharrī; if convinced of truthfulness, tayammum is permissible.
C) Ignore the fasiq and perform wudu with the water.
D) Repeat the wudu after the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The legal weight of a report depends on the reporter's probity and capacity: a fasiq's report requires taharrī, while a kafir, child, or insane person's report has no weight for tayammum.

Acceptance of Reports in Non-Binding Transactions (Usul Rule)
Explaining the acceptance of reports from any discerning person in non-binding transactions due to necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that in non-binding transactions, the report of any discerning person (mumayyiz) is accepted, and distinguish it from the strict conditions required in binding matters.

Core Idea
In non-binding transactions, necessity overrides strict conditions; any discerning person's report suffices.

This passage from Al-Husami articulates a key Hanafi usul principle: the relaxation of conditions for accepting reports in transactions that do not involve compulsion (ilzam). The author explains that due to general public need (umum al-darurah), the requirement that the reporter be upright, Muslim, or adult is dropped. Only discernment (tamyiz) is required. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and scope of this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of transaction
Recognize that the rule applies to 'transactions free from compulsion' such as wakalah, mudarabah, and permission to trade.
These are mu'amalat ghayr mulzima.
2
State the rule
The report of any discerning person (mumayyiz) is accepted in these transactions.
Mumayyiz: one with tamyiz, able to distinguish.
3
Analyze the rationale (talil)
The reason is general necessity (umum al-darurah) and the difficulty of finding someone who meets all conditions.
Darurah justifies dropping strict conditions.
4
Distinguish from binding matters
In matters of religion (e.g., testimony for hadd or marriage), strict conditions (adalah, Islam) are required because the report is binding.
Al-umur al-din require stricter proof.
5
Note the condition of tamyiz
Tamyiz means the ability to distinguish; it does not require adulthood or Islam.
A non-Muslim child with tamyiz qualifies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِي الْمُعَامَلَاتِ الَّتِي تَنْفَكَ عَنْ مَعْنَى الْإِلْزَامِ كَا لُوَ كَالَاتِ وَالْمُضَارَبَاتِ وَالْإِذْنِ فِي النِّجَارَةِ يُعْتَبَرُ خَبَرُ كُلِ مُمَيَذٍ لِعُمُوْمِ الضَّرْوَةِ الدَّاعِيَةِ إِلَى سُقُوطِ سَائِرِ الشَّرَائِطِ فَاِنَ الْإِنْسَانَ قَلَمَا يَجِدُ الْمُسْتَجْمِعَ لِتِلْكَ الشَّرَائِطِ يَبْعَثُهُ إِلَى وَكِيْلِهِ أَوْ غُلَامِهِ وَلَا دَلِيْلَ مَعَ السَّامِعِ يَعْمَلُ بِهِ سِوَى هَذَا الْخَبَرِ وَلَانَ اعْتَبَارَ هَذِهِ الشَّرَائِطِ لِيَتَرَ خَجَ جِهَةُ الصِّدْقِ فِى الْخَبَرِ فَيَصْلَحْ أَنْ يَكُونَ مُلْزِمًا وَذَلِكَ فِيْمَا يَتَعَلَّقَ بِهِ اللُّزُوْمُ فَشَرَطْنَاهَا فِي أُمُورِ الذِيْنِ دُوْنَ مَا لَا يَتَعَلَّقُ بِهِ اللُّزُوْمُ مِنَ الْمُعَامَلَاتِ
And in transactions that are free from the meaning of compulsion, such as wakalas, mudarabas, and permission for trade, the report of any discerning person is considered valid due to the generality of necessity, which requires dropping all other conditions. For a person rarely finds someone who meets those conditions to send as his agent or servant, and there is no evidence for the listener to act upon except this report. And (this is) because the consideration of these conditions is to make the truthfulness side preponderant in the report, so that it may be suitable to be binding. And that is in matters in which binding is relevant, so we made them conditions in matters of religion, not in what does not involve binding from among the transactions.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage states a usul rule about the acceptance of reports in transactions that are non-binding (i.e., do not require a binding outcome on the listener). Examples include wakala (agency), mudaraba (partnership), and idhn fit-tijara (permission to trade). In such cases, any discerning person (mumayyiz) — regardless of his probity, religion, or age — his report is accepted. The reason is general necessity (umum al-darurah): people often need to send agents or informants and cannot always find fully qualified witnesses. Moreover, in these transactions, there is no requirement for the report to be binding (ilzam) on the listener; the listener acts on the report for his own benefit or interest. Therefore, strict conditions like adālah and Islam are dropped, unlike in matters of religion (umur al-din) where binding is relevant (e.g., testimony about hadd punishments or marriage). The passage uses talil (legal reasoning) to justify the exception: the objective of conditions is to ensure truthfulness, but since these transactions do not involve compulsion, the risk is tolerable, and the need outweighs the risk.

Key Terms
المعاملات غير الملزمة (al-muʿāmalāt ghayr al-mulzima): Transactions where the person receiving the report is not bound or compelled by it; he can choose to accept or reject.
الضرورة العامة (al-ḍarūra al-ʿāmma): A widespread need that makes strict enforcement of conditions impractical.
التمييز (al-tamyīz): The ability to distinguish between things; legal discernment that enables a person to act rationally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the text accept the report of any 'mumayyiz' in wakala and mudaraba?
A) Because these are religious matters requiring leniency.
B) Because of the general necessity and difficulty of finding qualified reporters.
C) Because the reporter must be a Muslim.
D) Because the listener is bound by the report.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, general necessity (umum al-darurah) justifies accepting reports from any discerning person in non-binding transactions, dropping conditions of 'adalah, Islam, and bulugh.

The Three Categories of Negation in Conflicting Reports
Explaining three cases of negation and when it equals affirmation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a report's negation into one of three types (based on dalīl, ambiguous, or istiṣḥāb) and apply the Hanafi rule to determine if it contradicts an affirming report.

Core Idea
Negation based on evidence equals affirmation; negation based on istiṣḥāb is weak and does not conflict.

In Hanafi usul, when a report that negates a ruling conflicts with one that affirms, we do not automatically prefer affirmation. Instead, we examine the basis of the negation. This passage introduces a threefold classification that determines whether a real contradiction exists or the affirming report simply prevails. Understanding this framework is essential for correctly resolving apparent conflicts in hadith and legal evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of negation
The passage lists three categories: (1) negation based on clear evidence (dalīl), (2) negation whose basis is ambiguous (could be dalīl or istiṣḥāb), and (3) negation based solely on istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity).
Istiṣḥāb is not a valid proof (ḥujja) in the Hanafi school.
2
Assess strength relative to affirmation
For type 1, negation equals affirmation in strength → genuine contradiction requiring tarjīḥ. For type 3, negation is weak; affirmation takes precedence without contradiction. For type 2, investigate the reporter: if he used istiṣḥāb, his report is unreliable; if he used evidence, it is strong.
Affirmation is always based on evidence (by nature).
3
Apply to the hadith of Barira
The negation that Barira's husband was a slave is based on istiṣḥāb (original state). Hence it is weak and does not contradict the affirming report that he was free. The affirming report prevails, giving Barira the option upon emancipation.
This is type 3 negation.
4
Apply to the hadith of Maymuna
Both the negation (Prophet married in iḥrām) and affirmation (he was ḥalāl) are based on evidence. This is type 1 — contradiction occurs. The Hanafis resolve it by tarjīḥ: preferring Ibn Abbas's narration over Yazid ibn al-Asam due to superior reliability.
Contradiction requires a ground for preference (tarjīḥ).
5
Takeaway for third type (ambiguous)
If the basis of negation is unknown, examine the reporter's methodology. If he relied on istiṣḥāb, disregard his report; if on evidence, treat as type 1. The passage gives the example of water purity and food permissibility as falling under this category.
Details for this category are cut off in the source.
