گا، یہاں نفی کی مذکورہ تین صورتوں میں تیسری صورت ہے۔ اور حدیث میمونہ میں بھی دو روایتیں ہیں ایک نافی اور ایک مثبت ، جو نافی روایت ہے کہ رسول اللہ نے حضرت میمونہ سے نکاح کیا، اس وقت آپ محرم تھے یہ دلیل پر مبنی ہے، وہ دلیل [آپ سانی یا پیہم؟] کی جیت ہے کہ آپ کی حالت محرم جیسی تھی ، آپ سلے ہوئے کپڑوں میں نہ تھے ، حلق و قصر نہ ہوا تھا، یہ سب دلیل ہے کہ آپ محرم تھے، لہذا یہ اس دوسری روایت کے معارض ہوگی جو مثبت ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی یا پیام اس وقت حلال تھے یہ اثبات بھی دلیل پر مبنی ہے کیونکہ اثبات کسی نہ کسی دلیل سے ہوتا ہے، لہذافی اور اثبات دونوں جب دلیل پر مبنی ہیں تو تعارض ہوگا، اور اس کو دور کرنے کے لئے وجہ ترجیح کی ضرورت ہوگی، لہذا احناف نے ابن عباس کی روایت کو جو نافی ہے ترجیح دی یزید بن اصم کی روایت پر جو نافی ہے، کیونکہ ضبط واتقان میں ابن عباس کو ترجیح حاصل ہے، یہ فی کی مذکورہ تین صورتوں میں پہلی صورت ہے۔ جب نفی مشتبہ الحال ہو یعنی نفی کی دوسری صورت ، اس کی مثال طہارت ماء اور طعام وشراب کی حلت ہے تفصیل
So the contradiction occurred, and the narration of Ibn Abbas that he married her while in iḥrām was given precedence over the narration of Yazid ibn al-Asam because he is not equal to him in precision and reliability. And the purity of water and the permissibility of food and drink are from the genus of that which is known by its evidence, like impurity and prohibition. Thus conflict occurs between the two reports in these matters. And in that case, acting upon the original rule becomes obligatory. Translation: The rule in this regard is that when negation is from the genus of that which is known by its evidence, or from that whose state is ambiguous, but it becomes known that the reporter relied on evidence for knowledge, then negation is like affirmation; otherwise not. Thus the negation in the hadith of Barira is from those things known only by apparent state, so that negation does not contradict affirmation. And in the hadith of Maymuna, the negation is from those things known by evidence, and that is the state of iḥrām, so contradiction occurred. And the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet [ṣallā llāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam?] married Maymuna while he was in iḥrām was given precedence over the narration of Yazid ibn al-Asam, because Yazid ibn al-Asam is not equal to Ibn Abbas in precision and reliability. And the purity of water and the permissibility of food and drink are from the genus of that which is known by its evidence, like impurity and prohibition. So in both these matters, contradiction occurs between the two reports, and at the time of contradiction, acting upon the original principle is obligatory. Elaboration: Since the Hanafis sometimes act upon the affirming report and sometimes upon the negating report, there must be a general rule to know where to act upon affirmation and where upon negation. So the author states the rule: negation is of three types: (1) Negation from the genus of that which is known by its evidence, i.e., the negation is based on evidence, not on istiṣḥāb of the present state which is not a proof in our view. (2) Negation from the genus of that whose state is ambiguous, i.e., it is possible that this negation is based on evidence or on istiṣḥāb. (3) Negation from the genus of that which is not known by its evidence, i.e., the negation is not based on evidence but on istiṣḥāb of the present state, i.e., the opposite of the first case. These are the three cases. Now if it is the first case, i.e., the negation is based on evidence, then negation is like affirmation, i.e., both have equal strength because negation is based on evidence and affirmation is also based on evidence. When both have equal strength, there will be contradiction, and to resolve it a ground for preference (tarjīḥ) is needed. And if the negation is not based on any evidence but on istiṣḥāb, i.e., the third case, then negation and affirmation do not have equal strength, rather affirmation is stronger because it is based on evidence, and negation is weak because it is not based on evidence. Therefore there will be no contradiction; rather affirmation will take precedence over negation. And if the state of negation is ambiguous, i.e., it is unknown whether it is based on evidence or istiṣḥāb, then we will examine the state of the reporter. If it is proven that he used istiṣḥāb as evidence, then his report is not reliable. And if his report is based on evidential knowledge, i.e., he relied on evidence that is the cause of knowing the negation, then the negation becomes strong like affirmation due to being based on evidence, so there will be contradiction, and to resolve it a ground for preference is needed. After this general rule, the author says: In the issue of khiyār al-ʿitq (option of emancipation), the negation in the hadith of Barira that the Prophet [ṣallā llāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam?] gave Barira the option while her husband was a slave — in this the negation of freedom is not based on evidence but on istiṣḥāb, i.e., originally they were slaves so they are still slaves, and istiṣḥāb is not a proof in our view. Therefore this hadith will not contradict the other hadith which is affirmative that Barira's husband was free, because affirmation is based on evidence while negation is based on istiṣḥāb without evidence. So we take the affirming report and leave the negating one. Hence the female slave married to a slave gets the option of emancipation in every case. Here the negation is of the third type among the three mentioned. And in the hadith of Maymuna, there are two reports, one negating and one affirming. The negating report that the Messenger of Allah married Maymuna while he was in iḥrām is based on evidence; that evidence is the state of the Prophet [ṣallā llāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam?] that his condition was like that of a muḥrim — he was not wearing sewn clothes, he had not shaved or shortened his hair — all this is evidence that he was in iḥrām. So this report will contradict the other report which is affirmative that the Messenger of Allah was ḥalāl (not in iḥrām) at that time. This affirmation is also based on evidence because affirmation always comes from some evidence. Therefore, when both negation and affirmation are based on evidence, there will be contradiction, and to remove it a ground for preference is needed. Hence the Hanafis gave precedence to the report of Ibn Abbas which is negating over the report of Yazid ibn al-Asam which is negating, because Ibn Abbas has precedence in precision and reliability. This is the first case among the three. When negation is ambiguous (the second case), its example is the purity of water and the permissibility of food and drink — details...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage presents a key Ḥanafī uṣūl principle for resolving conflicts between reports that negate (nāfī) and reports that affirm (muthbit). The author, commenting on a matn, explains a threefold classification of negation based on the foundation of the report. The first type is where the negation is based on clear evidence (dalīl); here it carries equal weight with affirmation, leading to a genuine contradiction (taʿāruḍ) that requires tarjīḥ (preference). The second type is where the basis of negation is ambiguous — we must investigate the reporter's methodology: if he relied on istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity), his report is invalid; if on evidence, it is strong. The third type is where negation rests solely on istiṣḥāb, which the Ḥanafī school does not consider a valid proof (ḥujja). In this case, affirmation takes precedence without contradiction. The passage illustrates these cases with two famous ḥadīth examples. The first is the ḥadīth of Barira (khiyār al-ʿitq): the negation that her husband was a slave is based on istiṣḥāb, thus it is overruled by the affirming report that he was free. The second is the ḥadīth of Maymuna: both the negation (that the Prophet married her while in iḥrām) and the affirmation (that he was ḥalāl) are based on evidence, so a contradiction occurs; the Ḥanafīs prefer Ibn ʿAbbās's narration over Yazīd ibn al-Aṣam due to the former's superior reliability. The passage also mentions a third category (ambiguous negation) with the example of water purity and food permissibility, but the text cuts off. The ruling on such cases follows the same principle: investigate the reporter's basis.

Key Terms
نفي (nafy): A report that negates a certain legal attribute or state, e.g., 'the water is not pure' or 'the marriage was not valid'.
اثبات (ithbāt): A report that affirms a certain legal attribute or state, e.g., 'the water is pure' or 'the marriage was valid'.
تعارض (taʿāruḍ): A conflict between two equally strong pieces of evidence that cannot be reconciled without preference (tarjīḥ).
استصحاب (istiṣḥāb): Presumption of continuity of a previous state; considered a weak proof (ḥujja ḍaʿīfa) by Ḥanafīs, not sufficient to base negation on.
ترجیح (tarjīḥ): The process of giving preference to one piece of evidence over another based on factors such as narrator reliability, textual strength, or contextual clues.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ḥanafī uṣūl rule explained in this passage, what is the status of a negation that is based solely on istiṣḥāb (presumption of continuity)?
A) It is equal in strength to affirmation and causes a contradiction.
B) It is weaker than affirmation and does not cause a contradiction.
C) It is stronger than affirmation because it relies on a prior state.
D) It is considered a proof but requires tarjīḥ.

Key Takeaway
Negation based on evidence equals affirmation; negation based on istiṣḥāb is weak and does not create a genuine conflict.

The Hanafi Response to Shafi'i Objections on Ta'lil Not Changing Nass
Hanafi responses to three Shafi'i objections about ta'lil altering nass rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis argue that ta'lil does not alter the ruling of the nass, and apply this principle to the three cases of washing impurities, takbir in prayer, and kaffarah for breaking fast.

Core Idea
Ta'lil does not change the nass; the nass itself indicates the broader cause beyond the specific example.

This passage presents the Hanafi defense against the Shafi'i claim that causal reasoning (ta'lil) improperly expands the scope of explicit texts. Through three objections and responses, the Hanafi scholar demonstrates that the nass itself supports the broader interpretation because the specific mention is a tool, not the intended limit. Understanding this defense is crucial for grasping the Hanafi methodology of deriving rulings from revealed texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i objection
State the objection in each case: the nass mentions water/takbir/intercourse, so the ruling should be limited to those specific instances.
The Shafi'is argue that ta'lil changes the ruling by expanding beyond the literal text.
2
State the Hanafi response
The objective is not the specific tool but the underlying purpose: removal of impurity, glorification of Allah, expiation for intentional fast-breaking.
The Hanafis argue that the nass itself points to the broader 'illah.
3
Analyze the ta'lil reasoning
Note that the Hanafi 'illah is derived from the nass itself, not imposed externally. The specific mention is due to commonality, not exclusivity.
The ta'lil merely clarifies what the nass already implies.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
Consider a hypothetical: if someone uses vinegar to remove impurity, the ruling should still be purity, consistent with the 'illah.
This shows how ta'lil extends the ruling without contradicting the nass.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis allow all liquids that remove impurity; Shafi'is require water.
This difference has implications for daily practice.

Source Text

اسی حالت پر جو تعلیل سے پہلے تھی ۔
تشریح:- اس عبارت میں شوافع کی طرف سے احناف پر چند اعتراضات کے جوابات ہیں۔
پہلا سوال : یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں ہے کہ ناپاک کپڑے کو پانی سے دھویا جائے جیسے فرمایا اغسليه بالماء مگر آپ نے علت نکالی کہ ہر رقیق اور نجاست کو زائل کرنے والی چیز سے کپڑا پاک ہو جائے گا، جیسے گلاب ، سر کہ وغیرہ، تو تعلیل سے آپ نے نص کے حکم کو متغیر کر دیا کیونکہ نص میں صراحۃ پانی کا ذکر ہے۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ تبدیلی تعلیل سے نہیں ہوئی بلکہ نص سے ہی ثابت ہے کیونکہ مقصود پانی کا استعمال نہیں ہے بلکہ نجاست کو زائل کرنا مقصود ہے اور پانی بھی نجاست کے ازالہ کا آلہ ہے اس لئے پانی کا ذکر خصوصا کر دیا گیا۔ دوسرا سوال:- یہ ہے کہ حدیث شریف میں ہے تکبیر سے نماز شروع کرو جیسے فرمایا - وتحريمها التكبير مگر آپ نے علت نکالی کہ مقصد اللہ کی تعظیم اور ثنا ہے، اور یہ جس لفظ سے بھی ادا ہو اس کا کہنا صحیح ہے جیسے اللہ اجل “ اللہ اعظم “ وغیرہ، تو اس تعلیل سے آپ نے نص کا حکم بدل دیا کیونکہ نص میں صراحی تکبیر کا ذکر ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ یہاں نص میں تکبیر مقصود نہیں ہے، بلکہ مقصود بدن کے ہر ہر جز ء سے اللہ کی تعظیم کرنا ہے، اور نص میں خاص تکبیر کا ذکر اس لئے کیا گیا کہ وہ بھی ایک ایسا آلہ ہے جو زبان کے فعل کو تعظیم قرار دینے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے، لہذا نص کے حکم کو تعلیل سے ہم نے نہیں بدلا بلکہ خود نص سے ہی تغیر ہوا ہے۔ تیسرا سوال:- یہ ہے کہ حدیث میں کفارہ صرف جماع سے وارد ہوا ہے جیسے وہ اعرابی کا واقعہ جنہوں نے رمضان میں اپنی بیوی سے جماع کر لیا تو حضور نے فرمایا اعتق رقبه الحدیث ، اور آپ نے علت نکالی کہ روزہ توڑنا علت ہے لہذا کھانے پینے سے روزہ توڑے گا تو بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا، تو آپ نے نص کے حکم کو بدل دیا کیونکہ نص میں خاص جماع کے ساتھ کفارہ کا ورود ہے۔ جواب یہاں بھی وہی ہے جو پہلے دیا کہ اصل کفارہ کا سبب عمداً افطار ہے، جان بوجھ کر بغیر عذر کے روزہ توڑ دینا ہے، لہذا کھانے پینے سے بھی کفارہ آئے گا، اور جماع بھی اس کا ایک فرد ہے، یہ مقصد نہیں ہے کہ صرف جماع سے کفارہ لازم ہوگا، لہذا یہاں بھی تعلیل سے نص کا حکم متغیر نہیں ہوا۔
·
وبعد التعليل : - اس عبارت کا تعلق انما خصصنا سے یہاں تک جتنے سوالات شوافع کی طرف سے ہوئے ہیں سب کے ساتھ ہے، یعنی ان تمام جگہوں میں تعلیل کے بعد احکام اسی طرح صلاحیت رکھتے ہیں جس طرح تعلیل سے پہلے رکھتے تھے جیسے جماع تعلیل سے پہلے ہی افطار کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے، پانی نجاست کو زائل کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے، شاۃ ادا ئیگی زکوۃ کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہے ، غرض مذکورہ نصوص میں تعلیل سے تغیر نہیں ہوا جیسا کے ہر سوال کے تحت آپ نے دیکھ لیا، بلکہ تعلیل سے پہلے ہی نص سے تغیر ہوا ہے، لہذا ان سب جگہوں پر شرط رابع کے فوت ہونے کا اعتراض نہیں ہو سکتا۔
On the same condition that existed before the ta'lil. Explanation: This passage contains responses to several objections from the Shafi'is against the Hanafis. The first objection: It is that the hadith says that impure cloth should be washed with water, as He said: 'Wash it with water', but you derived the 'illah that the cloth will become pure with any liquid that removes impurity, like rose water, vinegar, etc. So by your ta'lil you changed the ruling of the nass because the nass explicitly mentions water. The answer: This change did not occur due to ta'lil but is established from the nass itself because the objective is not the use of water but the removal of impurity, and water is merely a tool for removing impurity; therefore water was mentioned specifically. The second objection: It is that the noble hadith says: 'Begin the prayer with takbir', as He said: 'And its prohibition is the takbir', but you derived the 'illah that the purpose is the glorification and praise of Allah, and whatever word expresses that is correct, such as 'Allahu Ajal', 'Allahu A'zam', etc. So by this ta'lil you changed the ruling of the nass because the nass explicitly mentions takbir. The answer: Here the nass does not intend takbir itself, but the intention is to glorify Allah with every part of the body, and the specific mention of takbir in the nass is because it is a tool that has the capacity to make the action of the tongue a glorification. Therefore we did not change the ruling of the nass by ta'lil; rather the change occurred from the nass itself. The third objection: It is that in the hadith, expiation (kaffarah) is reported only from intercourse, like the incident of the Bedouin who had intercourse with his wife in Ramadan, and the Prophet said: 'Free a slave,' etc., but you derived the 'illah that breaking the fast is the cause, so if one breaks the fast by eating or drinking, expiation will also be obligatory. So you changed the ruling of the nass because the nass mentions expiation specifically with intercourse. The answer here is the same as given before: the real cause of expiation is intentionally breaking the fast, i.e., deliberately breaking the fast without excuse, therefore expiation will also apply to eating and drinking, and intercourse is merely one instance of it. The intention is not that expiation is due only from intercourse. Therefore here too the ruling of the nass is not changed by ta'lil. And after ta'lil: This phrase is connected to all the objections raised by the Shafi'is from 'innama khasasna' up to here, i.e., in all these instances, after ta'lil the rulings possess the same capacity as before ta'lil. For example, intercourse had the capacity to break the fast before ta'lil, water had the capacity to remove impurity, a sheep had the capacity to fulfill zakat. In short, in the mentioned texts, change did not occur due to ta'lil, as you saw under each objection; rather the change occurred from the nass itself before ta'lil. Therefore in all these places the objection that the fourth condition is missing cannot be raised.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a Hanafi response to three Shafi'i objections concerning the use of ta'lil (causal reasoning) in deriving rulings. The Shafi'is argue that by applying ta'lil, the Hanafis change the explicit ruling of the nass (text). The Hanafi response explains that the ta'lil does not change the ruling; rather, the nass itself indicates that the specific example is not the intended limitation but a tool to achieve a broader objective. For example, in the hadith about washing impurity with water, the objective is removal of impurity, not water specifically. Similarly, takbir is a tool for glorification, and intercourse is a type of intentional fast-breaking. Therefore, the ta'lil merely clarifies the underlying cause, and the rulings remain consistent with the nass. The passage emphasizes that the Shafi'i objection regarding the fourth condition (that ta'lil should not change the text) is invalid.

Key Terms
تعلیل (ta'lil): The process of identifying the 'illah (cause) for a ruling and applying it to new cases.
نص (nass): A clear textual ruling from the Qur'an or Hadith that is explicit in its meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, what is the real purpose behind the hadith commanding washing with water?
A) To specify that only water can purify
B) To ensure the use of a specific liquid
C) To achieve the removal of impurity
D) To limit purification to a single method

Key Takeaway
Ta'lil in Hanafi usul does not override the nass; it reveals the underlying cause that the nass itself points to.

Istihsan as Hidden Qiyas: The Hanafi Rule of Precedence
Defining istihsan as qiyas khafi and explaining when it takes precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish istihsan from apparent qiyas and apply the Hanafi rule that precedence is based on strength of effect (ta'thir).

Core Idea
Istihsan is hidden qiyas, not a fifth proof; precedence depends on strength of effect, not appearance.

This lesson explores the Hanafi doctrine of istihsan (juristic preference). The author defines istihsan as a form of hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi) and defends it against the charge that it is an illegitimate proof. Through the analogy of the world and the Hereafter, and the example of sajdah in prayer, the text establishes the rule: the stronger effect determines which analogy is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Define istihsan and its relation to qiyas
Read the opening: 'Istihsan is called hidden qiyas'. Understand that Hanafis treat istihsan not as an independent proof but as a type of analogy.
2
Identify the objection and the Hanafi response
The objector claims only four proofs exist. The response: istihsan is a type of qiyas, not a new proof. Focus on the argument that both are qiyas, differing only in clarity.
3
Apply the rule of precedence
The rule: precedence goes to whichever qiyas (jali or khafi) has the stronger effect. Use the analogy of the world (apparent but weak effect) vs. Hereafter (hidden but strong effect) to internalize the concept.
4
Analyze the sajdah example
The passage presents a case: a person recites a sajdah verse in prayer. Qiyas says bowing suffices (based on Quranic phrase 'wa kharru ru'ka'an'), while apparent qiyas (or istihsan) says it does not. The text argues that qiyas is preferred here because its hidden effect (achieving humility) is stronger.
This is a rare case where apparent qiyas is preferred; usually istihsan is preferred.
5
Summarize the epistemological basis
The author concludes that an attribute's being an 'illa is based solely on its effect and effectiveness, not on whether it is manifest or hidden.

Source Text

ولما صارت العلة : - استحسان کہتے ہیں قیاس مخفی کو ، امام ابو حنیفہ ان استحسان کے قائل ہیں، اسی لئے احناف کبھی قیاس کو چھوڑ دیتے ہیں ، اور استحسان پر عمل کرتے ہیں، معترض اعتراض کرتا ہے کہ ادلۂ شرع تو چار ہیں، یہ پانچویں دلیل استحسان آپ کہاں سے لائے؟ دوسری بات یہ کہ آپ استحسان کے مقابلہ میں قیاس کو چھوڑ دیتے ہیں ، اس کا مطلب ہوا دلیل شرعی کو چھوڑ کر غیر شرعی دلیل پر عمل کرنا یہ کیسے درست ہو گا ؟ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ استحسان کوئی نئی چیز نہیں ، قیاس ہی کی قسم ہے، بس اتنا فرق ہے کہ قیاس ، جلی ہے اور استحسان قیاس خفی ہے، جب دونوں قیاس ہی کی قسمیں ہیں تو رہا یہ سوال کہ کہاں کس کو ترجیح ہوگی تو اس میں ضابطہ یہ ہے کہ جہاں جس کی تاثیر قوی اور مضبوط ہوگی وہاں اس کو ترجیح دیں گے ، لہذا جہاں استحسان کی تاثیر قوی ہوگی وہاں استحسان مقدم ہوگا ، اور جہاں قیاس کی تاثیر قوی ہوگی وہاں قیاس مقدم ہوگا، کیونکہ اثر کی قوت وصحت کا اعتبار ہے نہ کہ اس کے ظہور کا ، یعنی اثر کے ظاہر اور خفی ہونے کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، بلکہ اثر کے قوی اور مضبوط ہونے کا اعتبار ہے، کیونکہ بعض دفعہ ایک چیز ظاہر ہوتی ہے مگر اس کا اثر ضعیف ہوتا ہے، اور ایک چیز مخفی ہوتی ہے مگر اس کا اثر قوی ہوتا ہے، جیسے دنیا اگر چہ ظاہر ہے مگر اس کا اثر فنا ہونا ہے جو ضعیف ہے، اور آخرت مخفی ہے باطن ہے، مگر اس کا اثر بقا ہے جو قوی ہے، لہذا قوی کو ضعیف پر ترجیح دیں گے، ظاہر اور خفی ہونا نہ دیکھیں گے، کیونکہ علت کا علت ہونا اثر اور تاثیر ہی کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے۔ وَبَيَانُ الثَّانِي فِي مَنْ تَلَا آيَةَ السَّجْدَةِ فِي صَلوتِهِ أَنَّهُ يَرْكَعُ بِهَا قِيَاسًا لِاَنَّ النَّصَّ قَدْ وَرَدَ بِهِ قَالَ الله تَعَالَى وَخَرُّوا رُكَّعًا وَفِي الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ لَا يُجْزِيْهِ لِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ أَمَرَنا بِالسَّجُودِ وَالرُّكُوعُ خِلَافَة كَسْجُودِ الصَّلوةِ فَهُذَا أَثَرٌ ظَاهِرٌ فَا مَا وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ فَمَجَازٌ مَحْضٌ لَكِنَّ الْقِيَاسَ اَوْلى بِاَثَرِهِ الْبَاطِنِ بَيَانُهُ أَنَّ السُّجُوْدَ عِنْدَ التَّلَاوَةِ لَمْ يُشْرَعُ قُرْبَةً مَقْصُوْدَةٌ حَتَّى لَا يَلْزَمَ بِالنَّذْرِ وَإِنَّمَا الْمَقْصُودُ مُجَرَّدُ مَا يَصْلَحْ تَوَاضُعًا وَالرُّكُوعُ فِي الصَّلوة يَعْمَلُ هَذَا الْعَمَلَ بِخِلَافِ سُجُودِ الصَّلوةِ وَالرُّكُوعِ فِي غَيْرِهَا فَصَارَ الْآثَرَ الْخَفِيُّ مَعَ الْفَسَادَ الظَّاهِرِ اَوْلٰى مِنَ الْأَثَرِ الظَّاهِرِ مَعَ الْفَسَادَ الْخَفِي وَهَذَا قِسْمٌ عَزِيزُ الْوُجُودِ وَأَمَّا الْقِسْمَ الْأَوَّلُ فَأَكْثَرُ مِنْ أَنْ يُحْصَى
And when the 'illa became [effective]: Istihsan is called hidden qiyas. Imam Abu Hanifa believed in istihsan, therefore the Hanafis sometimes abandon qiyas and act upon istihsan. The objector objects: 'The proofs of Shari'ah are only four; where did you bring this fifth proof, istihsan? Moreover, you abandon qiyas in favor of istihsan; this means abandoning a legal proof and acting upon an illegal proof; how can this be correct?' The answer is that istihsan is not a new thing; it is a type of qiyas. The only difference is that qiyas is jali (apparent) and istihsan is qiyas khafi (hidden). Since both are types of qiyas, as for the question of which takes precedence, the rule is: precedence is given to whichever has stronger and more powerful effect. So where istihsan's effect is stronger, istihsan is preferred; and where qiyas's effect is stronger, qiyas is preferred. Because consideration is given to the strength and soundness of the effect, not to its manifestation. That is, not its manifestness or hiddenness, but its strength and robustness. Because sometimes a thing is manifest but its effect is weak, and a thing is hidden but its effect is strong. For example, the world, although manifest, its effect is annihilation (fana), which is weak; and the Hereafter is hidden and inward, but its effect is permanence (baqa), which is strong. Therefore, we give preference to the strong over the weak; we do not consider manifestness or hiddenness. Because an attribute's being an 'illa is solely due to its effect and effectiveness. And the explanation of the second [case where qiyas is preferred] concerns a person who recites a verse of sajdah in his prayer: by qiyas, he can bow (ruku') with it, because the text has come with that: Allah says, 'And they fell down in ruku'' (wa kharru ru'ka'an). And according to istihsan, it does not suffice him, because the Shari'ah commanded us to prostrate, and bowing is contrary to that, like the prostration of prayer. So this is an apparent effect. As for the basis of qiyas, it is pure metaphor. However, qiyas is more appropriate due to its hidden effect. Its explanation is that the prostration of tilawah was not legislated as an intended act of worship such that it would be binding by vow; rather, the purpose is merely what constitutes humility. And bowing in prayer fulfills this purpose, unlike the prostration of prayer and bowing in other contexts. So the hidden effect despite apparent defect is preferable to the apparent effect with hidden defect. And this is a type that is rare in occurrence. As for the first type [where istihsan is preferred], it is more numerous than can be counted.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage addresses the Hanafi concept of istihsan (juristic preference) and defends it against the charge of being a fifth proof. It begins by defining istihsan as hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi). The objector argues that the Shari'ah has only four proofs (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), so istihsan is an innovation. The response is that istihsan is not an independent proof but a type of qiyas. The difference is that qiyas is apparent (jali) while istihsan is hidden (khafi). The rule for precedence is based on the strength of the effect (ta'thir), not on whether the effect is apparent or hidden. The author uses the analogy of the world (apparent but weak effect of annihilation) vs. the Hereafter (hidden but strong effect of permanence). Therefore, if the hidden effect of istihsan is stronger, it is preferred over the apparent qiyas. The second part provides an example: a person recites a verse of sajdah in his prayer. By qiyas, he can substitute bowing (ruku') for prostration because the Quranic phrase 'wa kharru ru'ka'an' uses the word 'ru'ka''. But istihsan says bowing does not suffice because the command is specifically to prostrate. However, the passage argues that qiyas is preferred in this case because its hidden effect (achieving humility) is stronger, even though the apparent effect (the command of sujud) is overridden. This is a rare type where qiyas is preferred; in most cases, istihsan is preferred.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi) that is preferred over apparent qiyas when its effect is stronger.
قیاس جلی (qiyās jaliy): Apparent analogy whose effect is evident; may be weak in effect compared to istihsan.
قیاس خفی (qiyās khafiy): Hidden analogy; also called istihsan. Its effect may be less apparent but stronger.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what determines whether istihsan or qiyas jali is given precedence?
A) The number of scholars who support each.
B) Whether the effect is apparent or hidden.
C) The strength of the effect (ta'thir).
D) The ease of implementation.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan is not a departure from qiyas but a hidden qiyas; precedence is determined by the strength of the legal effect, not by the apparentness of the analogy.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference

When Qiyas Overrides Istihsan: Sajdah in Prayer
Second type of Qiyas-Istihsan preference: Qiyas preferred

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul rule that Qiyas is preferred over Istihsan when its hidden effect is stronger, using the sajdah tilawah example.

Core Idea
Qiyas can outweigh Istihsan when its hidden effect serves the law's purpose better than literal adherence.

In Hanafi usul, Istihsan often overrides Qiyas, but there is a rare second type where Qiyas takes precedence. This passage unpacks that exception through the case of a worshipper who recites a sajdah verse during prayer. Does bowing (ruku) fulfill the obligation of sajdah tilawah? By Qiyas, yes; by Istihsan, no. The commentary explains why the hidden benefit of Qiyas outweighs the apparent literal strength of Istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling positions
Find the two positions stated: Qiyas says bowing suffices (يركع بها قياسا); Istihsan says it does not (لا يجزيه في الاستحسان).
These correspond to the two methods being compared.
2
Examine the textual evidence
Locate the Quranic verse (وخر راكعا وأناب) used for Qiyas. Note that the word 'raki'an' (bowing) is used in the context of prostration.
This is a metaphorical usage (majaz) – a key point.
3
Analyze the apparent weakness of Qiyas
The passage states that the face of Qiyas is 'pure metaphor' (مجان محض). Literally, the command is to prostrate, not bow. So Qiyas appears weak.
This is why Istihsan seems stronger on the surface.
4
Uncover the hidden effect (athar khafi)
Contrast the purposes: sajdah tilawah is not an independent act of worship (قربة مقصودة) but merely an act of humility (تواضع). Bowing in prayer already achieves that purpose, unlike prostration or bowing outside prayer.
Thus, Qiyas fulfills the law's intent better.
5
Apply the preference rule
Conclude that the hidden effect of Qiyas (achieving humility) outweighs the apparent corruption of metaphor. Hence, Qiyas is preferred over Istihsan here.
This type (second) is rare; the first type (Istihsan preferred) is common.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَبَيَانُ الثَّانِي فِي مَنْ تَلَا آيَةَ السَّجْدَةِ فِي صَلوتِهِ أَنَّهُ يَرْكَعُ بِهَا قِيَاسًا لِاَنَّ النَّصَّ قَدْ وَرَدَ بِهِ قَالَ الله تَعَالَى وَخَزَرَاكِعَاوَاَنَابَ وَفِي الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ لَا يُجْزِيْهِ لِأَنَّ الشَّرْعَ أَمَرَنا بِالسَّجُودِ وَالرُّكُوعُ خِلَافَة كَسْجُودِ الصَّلوةِ فَهُذَا أَثَرْظَاهِرْ فَا مَا وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ فَمَجَانٌ مَحْضٌ لَكِنَّ الْقِيَاسَ اَوْلى بِاَثَرِهِ الْبَاطِنِ بَيَانُهُ أَنَّ السُّجُوْدَ عِنْدَ التَّلَاوَةِ لَمْ يُشْرَعُ قُرْبَةً مَقْصُوْدَةٌ حَتَّى لَا يَلْزَمَ بِالنَّذْرِ وَإِنَّمَا الْمَقْصودُ مُجَرَّدُ مَا يَصْلَحْ تَوَاضُعًا وَالرُّكُوعُ فِي الصَّلوة يَعْمَلُ هَذَا الْعَمَلَ بِخِلَافِ سُجُودِ الصَّلوةِ وَالرُّكُوعِ فِي غَيْرِهَا فَصَارَ الْآثَرَ الْخَفِيُّ مَعَ الْفَسَادَ الظَّاهِرِ اَوْلٰى مِنَ الْأَثَرِ الظَّاهِرِ مَعَ الْفَسَادَ الْخَفِي وَهَذَا قِسْمْ عَزَوْجُودَهُ وَأَمَّا الْقِسْمَ الْأَوَّلُ فَأَكْثَرُ مِنْ أَنْ يُحْصَى
And the explanation of the second (type) is concerning the one who recites the verse of prostration in his prayer: that he bows with it by analogy, because the text has come with it. Allah said: 'And he fell down bowing and repented.' And in istihsan, it does not suffice him, because the Law commanded us to prostrate, and bowing is contrary to it, like the prostration of prayer. So this is an apparent effect. As for the face of analogy, it is pure metaphor, but analogy is more worthy due to its hidden effect. Its explanation: that prostration at the time of recitation is not legislated as an intended act of worship such that it is binding by oath; rather the intended purpose is merely that which serves as humility. And bowing in prayer performs this action, unlike the prostration of prayer and bowing outside of it. So the hidden effect with apparent corruption is more worthy than the apparent effect with hidden corruption. And this type is rare in occurrence; as for the first type, it is too numerous to count.
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of precedence between Qiyas and Istihsan, where Qiyas is preferred despite its apparent weakness. The example: a person recites an ayah of sajdah (like in Surah Sad) during his prayer. According to Qiyas, he can fulfill the sajdah by bowing (ruku) because the Qur'an uses 'ruku' to refer to sujud in the verse 'wa kharra raaki'an wa anaab'. This is a Qiyas based on common meaning (khushu'/humility). According to Istihsan, bowing does not suffice because the Law commands sujud (literal prostration), and ruku is a different act; just as prayer-sujud is not fulfilled by ruku, so too sajdah tilawah. The commentary then explains that Qiyas appears weak because it relies on metaphor (majaz: using 'ruku' to mean 'sujud'), but its hidden effect is stronger: sajdah tilawah is not an intended act of worship (qurbah maqsudah) but merely an act of humility, and ruku in prayer already achieves that purpose. Thus, the hidden benefit of Qiyas (achieving the purpose with less effort) outweighs the apparent literal inconsistency. Istihsan's apparent strength (literal correspondence) hides a corruption: requiring a separate prostration when the common purpose is served. Therefore, the rule is: when the hidden effect of one argument is stronger, even if its face is weak, it can be preferred. This type is rare; the first type (Istihsan preferred over Qiyas) is common.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (istihsan): Legal preference of a ruling over another due to a stronger hidden effect, even if Qiyas is more apparent.
القياس (qiyas): Analogical extension of a ruling from an original case to a new case based on shared effective cause.
الأثر (athar): The effect or consequence of a legal argument; its strength determines preference.
المجاز (majaz): Metaphorical usage of a word for a similar meaning; here, using 'ruku' for 'sujud' due to shared concept of humility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage conclude that Qiyas is preferred over Istihsan in the sajdah tilawah example?
A) Because the Quranic verse explicitly commands bowing instead of prostration.
B) Because the hidden effect of Qiyas (achieving humility) outweighs the apparent effect of Istihsan (literal sujud).
C) Because Istihsan is invalid in Hanafi usul.
D) Because prostration is not required at all during prayer.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas can be preferred over Istihsan when its hidden effect achieves the law's purpose more efficiently, even if its face is metaphorically weak.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference

When Qiyas Overrides Istihsan: Sajdah Tilawah in Ruku'
Analyzing preference of qiyas over istihsan via a case of sajdah tilawah in ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of preferring qiyas over istihsan by analyzing apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin) effects of legal reasoning, using the case of sajdah tilawah in ruku'.

Core Idea
Qiyas is preferred over istihsan when its hidden effect fulfills the purpose of the act, even if its apparent foundation is weak.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced case from Hanafi usul where qiyas overrides istihsan. The scenario involves performing sajdah tilawah in ruku' during prayer. The commentary shows that although istihsan appears stronger on the surface, qiyas wins when we consider the deeper purpose of the act. You will learn to evaluate both the apparent and hidden effects of proofs and apply the principle of tarjih to determine the preferred ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case
The scenario: a person recites a verse of sajdah during prayer and intends to perform sajdah tilawah in ruku'. Qiyas says it is valid; istihsan says it is not. Understand what each method claims.
The case is specific: the sajdah tilawah is intended within the ruku' movement of the same prayer.
2
Understand the Apparent Effects
Qiyas appears weak because it relies on the metaphorical use of 'ruku'' for sajdah in Qur'an 38:24. Istihsan appears strong because it adheres to the literal distinction between ruku' and sajdah.
The apparent effect is what is immediately observable from the text or reality.
3
Dig into the Hidden Effects
Qiyas's hidden effect: sajdah tilawah is qurbat ghayr maqsudah (purpose is humility), which is achieved by ruku'. Istihsan's hidden effect: it analogizes sajdah tilawah to the prostration of prayer (qurbat maqsudah), making the analogy invalid because the two types differ in legal nature.
Hidden effect considers the underlying purpose and correct application of analogy.
4
Apply the Tarjih Principle
Compare hidden effects: qiyas's hidden effect is strong (purpose achieved), istihsan's hidden effect is weak (faulty analogy). Thus, qiyas is preferred despite its weak apparent foundation.
The stronger hidden effect outweighs the weaker apparent effect.
5
Note the Rarity
This type of preference (qiyas over istihsan) is rare compared to the opposite. Default rule is istihsan over qiyas; this is an exception when the hidden effect of qiyas is clearly stronger.
Recognize the default and the exceptional nature of this case.

شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
قربت مقصودہ بن کر مشروع نہیں ہوا ہے، یہاں تک کہ وہ نذر سے لازم نہیں ہوتا ہے، اور مقصود محض وہ چیز ہے جو تو اضع کی صلاحیت رکھے، اور نماز کا رکوع یہ کام کرتا ہے برخلاف نماز کے سجدہ کے، اور نماز کے علاوہ کے رکوع کے، پس اثر حفی فساد ظاہر کے ساتھ اس اثر ظاہر سے اولی ہے جو فساد فی کے ساتھ ہے، اور یہ قسم ایسی ہے جس کا وجود کم ہے، اور بہر حال پہلی قسم تو وہ شمار سے زیادہ ہے۔ یح : ماقبل میں استحسان کو قیاس پر مقدم کرنا بیان کر چکے ، یہاں قسم ثانی یعنی قیاس کو استحسان پر مقدم کرنا بیان کر رہے ہیں، جس کی تقریر یہ ہے کہ کسی نے نماز میں آیت سجدہ تلاوت کی اور رکوع میں سجدہ تلاوت ادا کرنے کی نیت کی، تو قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ رکوع میں سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو جائے گا اور استحسان کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ ادانہ ہوگا ، قیاس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکوع اور سجدہ دونوں خضوع کے معنی میں ایک دوسرے کے مشابہ ہیں، یعنی دونوں میں خضوع اور تواضع کے معنی ہیں، اسی لئے قرآن میں سجدہ کو رکوع سے تعبیر کیا گیا ہے جیسے وخرراکھا واناب ۔ یہاں داؤد کے سجدہ کو رکوع سے تعبیر کیا، خر کے معنی زمین پر گرنا، یہ دلیل ہے کہ رکوع سے مراد سجدہ ہے، لہذا جب رکوع اور سجدہ دونوں ایک دوسرے کے مشابہ ہیں ، تو رکوع میں بھی سجدہ تلاوت ادا ہو جائے گا اور استحسان کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ شریعت نے ہم کو آیت سجدہ کی تلاوت کے وقت سجدہ کا حکم دیا ہے، اور سجدہ کی حقیقت اور ہے، رکوع کی حقیقت اور ہے، لہذا رکوع سجدہ کے قائم مقام نہیں ہو سکتا ہے، اسی لئے نماز کا سجدہ رکوع سے اور نماز کا رکوع سجدہ سے ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے، حالانکہ نماز کا سجدہ رکوع سے زیادہ قریب ہے بہ نسبت سجدہ تلاوت کے، پس جب نماز کے رکوع سے نماز کا سجدہ ادا نہیں ہوتا تو سجدہ تلاوت بھی رکوع سے ادا نہ ہوگا۔
السلام
-
فهذا اثر ظاهر- یہ قیاس اور استحسان کا ظاہری اثر ہے، استحسان میں جو بتایا کہ رکوع اور سجدہ دونوں الگ الگ چیزیں ہیں، لہذا دونوں ایک دوسرے کے قائم مقام نہیں ہو سکتے یہ ظاہر نظر کے اعتبار سے بہت عمدہ معلوم ہورہا ہے مگر اس کا باطنی اثر اس میں فساد ہے، پس استحسان میں ظاہر کے عمدہ اور باطن میں فساد کی وجہ سے اس کو قیاس کے مقابلہ میں مرجوح قرار دیا، کیونکہ قیاس ظاہری نظر میں ضعیف ہے۔ وہ اس طرح کہ قیاس کی بنیاد مجاز پر رکھی گئی ہے، کیونکہ قران میں سجدہ کو رکوع جو کہا ہے وہ مجازاً کہا ہے، اور مجاز حقیقت کے مقابلہ میں ضعیف ہوتا ہے، تو قیاس کی بناء مجاز پر ہے ،اس لئے ظاہر یہ ضعیف ہے اور استحسان کی بنا حقیقت پر ہے اس لئے استحسان ظاہراً عمدہ ہے ۔۔ لیکن دقیق نظر سے باطنی اثر دیکھیں گے تو قیاس عمدہ اور استحسان ضعیف ہے وہ کس طرح ؟ اس کو اگلی عبارت میں بیان کر رہے ہیں۔ بيانه ان السجود - قیاس کے باطنی اثر کو بیان کر رہے ہیں کہ سجدہ تلاوت قربت غیر مقصودہ ہے، جس

الفيضُ الحجازي
۲۷۲
شرح اردو المنحها الى امى
کا مقصد تعظیم ہے، اس لئے نذر ماننے سے سجدہ تلاوت لازم نہیں ہوتا ہے، اگر قربت مقصودہ ہوتا تو نذر سے لازم ہو جاتا ، معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ تلاوت قربت مقصودہ نہیں ہے، پھر اس کی مشروعیت کیوں ہوئی ؟ سجدہ تلاوت سے مقصود تعظیم اور تواضع کا اظہار ہے تاکہ مطیع، فرمانبردار کا سرکش ، نافرمان سے امتیاز ہو جائے ، جیسے قرآن میں بہت سی آیات سجدہ کی ہیں جیسے والله يسجد من فی السموات والارض طوعاً وكرها وغیرہ یہاں تواضع ہی مقصود ہے لہذا جب سجدہ تلاوت کا مقصد تعظیم و تواضع ہے تو یہ کام نماز کے رکوع سے بھی ہو جائے گا۔ یہ قیاس کا باطنی اثر ہے جو بہت قوی ہے۔
استحسان کا باطنی اثر یہ ہے کہ اس میں سجدہ تلاوت کو سجدہ نماز پر قیاس کر کے یوں کہا گیا ہے کہ جس طرح نماز کا سجدہ رکوع سے ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے، سجدہ تلاوت بھی رکوع سے ادا نہ ہوگا ، اسی طرح نماز کے باہر کے رکوع سے سجدہ تلاوت ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو نماز کے رکوع سے بھی ادا نہ ہوگا، یہ استحسان کا باطنی اثر ہے مگر یہ ضعیف اور فاسد ہے کیونکہ نماز کا سجدہ قربت مقصودہ ہے، اور سجدہ تلاوت قربت غیر مقصودہ ہے، تو قیاس صحیح نہیں ہے کہ نماز کا سجدہ جیسے رکوع سے ادا نہیں ہوتا، سجدہ تلاوت بھی ادا نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح نماز کا رکوع عبادت ہے اور نماز کے باہر کا رکوع عبادت نہیں ہے، اور سجدہ تلاوت جس رکوع سے ادا ہو گا اس کا عبادت ہونا شرط ہے پس یہ قیاس بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ قیاس کا ظاہری اثر ( بناء علی القیاس ) اگر چہ ضعیف ہے۔۔ مگر اس کا باطنی اثر ( یعنی تعظیم و تواضع کا مقصود ہونا اور اس کا رکوع سے حاصل ہونا ) قوی اور مضبوط ہے، اور استحسان کا ظاہری اثر (حقیقت پر عمل ) اگر چہ قوی ہے۔ مگر اس کا باطنی اثر ( قربت غیر مقصودہ مثل سجدہ تلاوت کو قربت مقصوده مثل سجدة صلوۃ پر قیاس ) ضعیف اور فاسد ہے پس قیاس پر عمل کرنا جس کا مخفی اور باطنی اثر قوی ہے اگر چہ ظاہری اثر میں فساد ہے یہ زیادہ اولی ہے اس استحسان پر عمل کرنے سے جس کا ظاہری اثر قوی ہے، اور باطنی اثر ضعیف اور فاسد ہے، لہذا یہاں قیاس کو استحسان پر ترجیح دی۔ عمال کہتے ہیں کہ یہ قسم جو ابھی بیان ہوئی یعنی قیاس کو استحسان پر مقدم کرنا بہ نسبت پہلی قسم (استحسان کو قیاس پر مقدم کرنے ) کے قلیل الوجود ہیں، اور قسم اول کی مثالیں انگنت ہیں۔ ثُمَّ الْمُسْتَحْسَنُ بِالْقِيَاسِ الْخَفِي يَصِحُ تَعْدِيَتُهُ بِخِلَافِ الْمُسْتَحْسَنِ بِالْأَثَرِ أَوِ الْإِجْمَاعِ أَوْ الضَّرُورَةِ كَالسَّلَم وَالْاِسْتِصْنَاعِ وَتَطْهِيرِ الْحِيَاضِ وَالْأَبَارِ وَالْأَوَانِئ أَلَا تَرى أَنَّ الْاِخْتِلَافَ فِي الثَمَنِ قَبْلَ قَبْضِ الْمَبِيعِ لَا يُؤْجِبْ يَمِيْنَ
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi. 271. Urdu commentary of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. It is not legislated as an intended act of worship, to the extent that it is not made obligatory by a vow. And the solely intended thing is that which has the capacity for humility. The bowing of prayer does this, unlike the prostration of prayer and unlike bowing outside prayer. So a hidden effect with apparent corruption is more worthy than an apparent effect with hidden corruption. And this type is rare, whereas the first type is countless. Explanation: Previously, it was explained that istihsan is given precedence over qiyas. Here, the second type, i.e., giving precedence to qiyas over istihsan, is being explained. Its exposition is that someone recited a verse of sajdah in prayer and intended to perform sajdah tilawah in ruku'. Qiyas requires that sajdah tilawah is performed in ruku', and istihsan requires that it is not performed. The proof of qiyas is that ruku' and sajdah are similar in the meaning of humility, i.e., both have the meanings of humility and lowliness. Therefore, in the Qur'an, sajdah is expressed as ruku', such as 'wakharra raki'an wa anaba'. Here, David's sajdah is expressed as ruku'; 'kharra' means to fall to the ground. This is proof that by ruku' is meant sajdah. Hence, when ruku' and sajdah are similar to each other, then sajdah tilawah will also be performed in ruku'. And the proof of istihsan is that the Shariah has commanded us to prostrate at the time of reciting a verse of sajdah, and the reality of sajdah is something else, and the reality of ruku' is something else. Therefore, ruku' cannot stand in place of sajdah. For this reason, the prostration of prayer is not performed by bowing, and the bowing of prayer is not performed by prostration, even though the prostration of prayer is closer to bowing than sajdah tilawah. So when the prostration of prayer is not performed by bowing, then sajdah tilawah will also not be performed by bowing. So this is the apparent effect— this is the apparent effect of qiyas and istihsan. In istihsan, it was stated that ruku' and sajdah are two separate things, therefore they cannot stand in place of each other. This seems very good from the perspective of outer appearance, but its inner effect has corruption in it. So istihsan was deemed preponderated over qiyas due to the goodness of its apparent and corruption in its inner, because qiyas is weak in outer appearance. That is, the basis of qiyas is placed on metaphor, because in the Qur'an, sajdah is called ruku' metaphorically, and metaphor is weak compared to reality. So the basis of qiyas is on metaphor, therefore it is weak in appearance, and the basis of istihsan is on reality, therefore istihsan is good in appearance. But if we look with a precise eye at the inner effect, then qiyas is good and istihsan is weak. How is that? They are explaining it in the next phrase. 'Bayaanuhu anna al-sujood'— they are explaining the inner effect of qiyas: that sajdah tilawah is a non-intended act of worship, the purpose of which is glorification. Therefore, it does not become obligatory by a vow. If it were an intended act of worship, it would become obligatory by a vow. So it is known that sajdah tilawah is not an intended act of worship. Then why was it legislated? The purpose of sajdah tilawah is to express glorification and humility so that the obedient and submissive are distinguished from the rebellious and disobedient, as in the Qur'an many verses of sajdah, such as 'wa lillahi yasjudu man fi al-samawati wa al-ardi taw'an wa karhan' etc. Here, humility is the only purpose. Therefore, when the purpose of sajdah tilawah is glorification and humility, then this action will also be achieved by the bowing of prayer. This is the inner effect of qiyas, which is very strong. The inner effect of istihsan is that in it, sajdah tilawah is analogized to the prostration of prayer, saying: just as the prostration of prayer is not performed by bowing, sajdah tilawah will also not be performed by bowing. Similarly, sajdah tilawah is not performed by bowing outside prayer, so it will also not be performed by bowing in prayer. This is the inner effect of istihsan, but it is weak and corrupt, because the prostration of prayer is an intended act of worship, and sajdah tilawah is a non-intended act of worship. So the analogy is not correct that just as the prostration of prayer is not performed by bowing, sajdah tilawah will also not be performed. Similarly, the bowing of prayer is worship, and bowing outside prayer is not worship. And for the bowing by which sajdah tilawah is performed, it being worship is a condition. So this analogy is also not correct. Summary: The apparent effect of qiyas (based on qiyas) although weak, its inner effect (i.e., glorification and humility being the purpose and its being achieved by bowing) is strong and firm. And the apparent effect of istihsan (acting on reality) although strong, its inner effect (analogizing a non-intended act of worship like sajdah tilawah to an intended act of worship like the prostration of prayer) is weak and corrupt. So acting on qiyas, whose hidden inner effect is strong even though its apparent effect is corrupt, is more worthy than acting on istihsan whose apparent effect is strong and inner effect is weak and corrupt. Therefore, here qiyas is given preference over istihsan. Some say that this type that has just been mentioned, i.e., giving precedence to qiyas over istihsan, is rare compared to the first type (giving precedence to istihsan over qiyas), and examples of the first type are countless. Then, what is considered good by hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) can be extended, unlike what is considered good by tradition (athar), consensus (ijma'), or necessity (darurah), like salam [forward sale], istisna' [manufacturing contract], purification of water troughs, wells, and vessels. Do you not see that disagreement about the price before taking possession of the sold item does not require an oath?
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on a specific ruling within the Hanafi usul tradition, concerning the preference of qiyas over istihsan. The commentator first sets the context: previously, it was explained that istihsan is given precedence over qiyas; now the opposite is being addressed—cases where qiyas is given precedence over istihsan. The case under discussion is: a person recites a verse of sajdah during prayer and intends to perform the sajdah tilawah (prostration of recitation) in ruku'. The question is whether the sajdah tilawah is fulfilled by the ruku' or not. Qiyas (analogy) says yes, because both ruku' and sajdah involve humility (khushu'), and the Qur'an itself uses the word 'ruku'' to refer to sajdah (e.g., Prophet Dawud's prostration described as 'wakharra raki'an'). Istihsan, however, says no, because the Shariah has commanded a specific act of prostration for sajdah tilawah; the reality of sajdah is different from ruku', and they cannot substitute for each other. The commentator then analyzes the apparent (zahir) and hidden (batin) effects of both proofs. The apparent effect of istihsan seems strong because it is based on the reality of the acts: sajdah is sajdah, ruku' is ruku'. The apparent effect of qiyas seems weak because it relies on a metaphorical usage of 'ruku'' for sajdah. However, when one examines the hidden (deeper) effect, qiyas is actually strong: sajdah tilawah is a non-intended act of worship (qurbat ghayr maqsudah), meaning its purpose is not intrinsic worship but rather expressing humility. Since ruku' in prayer also expresses humility, the purpose is achieved. On the other hand, the hidden effect of istihsan is flawed: it analogizes sajdah tilawah to the prostration of prayer (sajdah salat), but the latter is an intended act of worship (qurbat maqsudah) where the act itself is the goal. The analogy is invalid because the two types of sajdah differ in their legal nature. Similarly, the analogy of bowing inside prayer to bowing outside prayer fails because the latter is not worship. Therefore, the ruling is that qiyas is preferred because its hidden effect is stronger, even if its apparent effect is weak. The commentator concludes by noting that such cases (where qiyas takes precedence over istihsan) are rare compared to the opposite. The passage ends with a general usul principle: what is deemed good by hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) can be extended to other cases, unlike istihsan based on text (athar), consensus (ijma'), or necessity (darurah), giving examples like salam and istisna' contracts, and purification of water containers.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): A legal method preferring what is good or based on a stronger hidden reason over an apparent analogy.
قیاس (qiyās): Analogical deduction from a known ruling to a new case based on a shared effective cause (illah).
قربت مقصودہ (qurbat maqṣūdah): An act of worship that is intended for its own sake, i.e., its performance is the primary goal.
قربت غیر مقصودہ (qurbat ghayr maqṣūdah): An act of worship whose purpose is a result rather than the act itself, e.g., sajdah tilawah's purpose is humility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator prefer qiyas over istihsan in the case of sajdah tilawah performed in ruku'?
A) Because qiyas is based on a direct Quranic command.
B) Because the hidden effect of qiyas (achieving humility) is stronger than the hidden effect of istihsan (faulty analogy).
C) Because istihsan is not a valid source in Hanafi usul.
D) Because sajdah tilawah is an intended act of worship (qurbat maqsudah).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, qiyas can be preferred over istihsan when its hidden effect (batin) is stronger and the purpose of the act is achieved, even if its apparent foundation is weak.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
advanced
8 min
Preferring Qiyas over Istihsan: The Criterion of Inner Effects
Usul rule: preferring qiyas over istihsan based on inner effect strength

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the preference between qiyas and istihsan by analyzing their inner effects (bātini asar) using the case of sajdah tilawah.

Core Idea
The strength of a legal reasoning is determined by its inner effect, not just its outer appearance.

In Hanafi usul, both qiyas and istihsan are valid methods, but when they conflict, preference is not always given to istihsan. This passage demonstrates a rare case where qiyas is preferred because its inner effect—the underlying purpose of the act—is stronger. By examining the example of sajdah tilawah, we learn to evaluate the bātini asar of each reasoning and apply a nuanced preference rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested ruling
What is the specific legal question? Here: Can sajdah tilawah be validly performed by ruku' in prayer?
Contrast with the general rule that sajdah cannot be replaced by ruku'.
2
Extract the qiyas argument
What is the qiyas (analogy) that permits performing sajdah tilawah with ruku'? Note its basis: the purpose of sajdah tilawah is ta'zim and tawadu', which ruku' also fulfills.
This is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on maqsad.
3
Extract the istihsan argument
What is the istihsan that forbids it? It analogizes sajdah tilawah to sajdah salat, arguing that since sajdah salat cannot be done by ruku', neither can sajdah tilawah.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) but the author argues it is weak.
4
Compare inner effects (bātini asar)
Identify the inner effect of each reasoning. The qiyas's inner effect is that ta'zim is achieved by ruku', which is strong. The istihsan's inner effect is comparing two acts with different purposes, which is weak and corrupt.
The outer effect (zāhiri asar) may be strong for istihsan, but inner effect is decisive.
5
Apply the preference rule
Since the qiyas has a stronger inner effect, it is preferred over istihsan. Note that this type is rare; usually istihsan is preferred.
This nuance prevents overgeneralization.

کا مقصد تعظیم ہے، اس لئے نذر ماننے سے سجدہ تلاوت لازم نہیں ہوتا ہے، اگر قربت مقصودہ ہوتا تو نذر سے لازم ہو جاتا ، معلوم ہوا کہ سجدہ تلاوت قربت مقصودہ نہیں ہے، پھر اس کی مشروعیت کیوں ہوئی ؟ سجدہ تلاوت سے مقصود تعظیم اور تواضع کا اظہار ہے تاکہ مطیع، فرمانبردار کا سرکش ، نافرمان سے امتیاز ہو جائے ، جیسے قرآن میں بہت سی آیات سجدہ کی ہیں جیسے والله يسجد من فی السموات والارض طوعاً وكرها وغیرہ یہاں تواضع ہی مقصود ہے لہذا جب سجدہ تلاوت کا مقصد تعظیم و تواضع ہے تو یہ کام نماز کے رکوع سے بھی ہو جائے گا۔ یہ قیاس کا باطنی اثر ہے جو بہت قوی ہے۔ استحسان کا باطنی اثر یہ ہے کہ اس میں سجدہ تلاوت کو سجدہ نماز پر قیاس کر کے یوں کہا گیا ہے کہ جس طرح نماز کا سجدہ رکوع سے ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے، سجدہ تلاوت بھی رکوع سے ادا نہ ہوگا ، اسی طرح نماز کے باہر کے رکوع سے سجدہ تلاوت ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے، تو نماز کے رکوع سے بھی ادا نہ ہوگا، یہ استحسان کا باطنی اثر ہے مگر یہ ضعیف اور فاسد ہے کیونکہ نماز کا سجدہ قربت مقصودہ ہے، اور سجدہ تلاوت قربت غیر مقصودہ ہے، تو قیاس صحیح نہیں ہے کہ نماز کا سجدہ جیسے رکوع سے ادا نہیں ہوتا، سجدہ تلاوت بھی ادا نہ ہو گا۔ اسی طرح نماز کا رکوع عبادت ہے اور نماز کے باہر کا رکوع عبادت نہیں ہے، اور سجدہ تلاوت جس رکوع سے ادا ہو گا اس کا عبادت ہونا شرط ہے پس یہ قیاس بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ خلاصہ کلام یہ کہ قیاس کا ظاہری اثر ( بناء علی القیاس ) اگر چہ ضعیف ہے۔۔ مگر اس کا باطنی اثر ( یعنی تعظیم و تواضع کا مقصود ہونا اور اس کا رکوع سے حاصل ہونا ) قوی اور مضبوط ہے، اور استحسان کا ظاہری اثر (حقیقت پر عمل ) اگر چہ قوی ہے۔ مگر اس کا باطنی اثر ( قربت غیر مقصودہ مثل سجدہ تلاوت کو قربت مقصوده مثل سجدة صلوۃ پر قیاس ) ضعیف اور فاسد ہے پس قیاس پر عمل کرنا جس کا مخفی اور باطنی اثر قوی ہے اگر چہ ظاہری اثر میں فساد ہے یہ زیادہ اولی ہے اس استحسان پر عمل کرنے سے جس کا ظاہری اثر قوی ہے، اور باطنی اثر ضعیف اور فاسد ہے، لہذا یہاں قیاس کو استحسان پر ترجیح دی۔ عمال کہتے ہیں کہ یہ قسم جو ابھی بیان ہوئی یعنی قیاس کو استحسان پر مقدم کرنا بہ نسبت پہلی قسم (استحسان کو قیاس پر مقدم کرنے ) کے قلیل الوجود ہیں، اور قسم اول کی مثالیں انگنت ہیں۔
Its purpose is glorification, so sajdah tilawah is not necessitated by a vow; if it were an intended act of devotion, it would be necessitated by the vow. It is known that sajdah tilawah is not an intended act of devotion. So why was it legislated? The purpose of sajdah tilawah is the expression of glorification and humility, so that the obedient and compliant are distinguished from the rebellious and disobedient, just as many verses in the Quran mention prostration, such as 'And to Allah prostrates whoever is in the heavens and the earth, willingly or unwillingly,' etc. Here, only humility is intended. Therefore, since the purpose of sajdah tilawah is glorification and humility, this act can also be performed by the bowing (ruku') of prayer. This is the inner effect of qiyas, and it is very strong. The inner effect of istihsan is that in it, sajdah tilawah is compared to the prostration of prayer, saying that just as the prostration of prayer is not performed by bowing, so too sajdah tilawah will not be performed by bowing. Similarly, just as sajdah tilawah outside prayer is not performed by bowing, so it will not be performed by the bowing of prayer. This is the inner effect of istihsan, but it is weak and corrupt, because the prostration of prayer is an intended act of devotion, while sajdah tilawah is not an intended act of devotion. So the analogy is not correct: that just as the prostration of prayer is not performed by bowing, sajdah tilawah will also not be performed. Similarly, the bowing of prayer is worship, while bowing outside prayer is not worship, and for the bowing that performs sajdah tilawah, it being worship is a condition. Therefore, this analogy is also not correct. In summary, the outer effect of qiyas (based on qiyas) although weak, but its inner effect (i.e., glorification and humility being intended and being achieved by bowing) is strong and sound, and the outer effect of istihsan (acting on reality) although strong, but its inner effect (comparing an unintended act like sajdah tilawah to an intended act like prostration of prayer) is weak and corrupt. Therefore, acting upon qiyas, whose hidden and inner effect is strong, even if there is corruption in its outer effect, is more appropriate than acting upon istihsan, whose outer effect is strong but inner effect is weak and corrupt. Hence, here qiyas is preferred over istihsan. Scholars say that this type, which has just been mentioned (i.e., giving precedence to qiyas over istihsan) is rare compared to the first type (giving precedence to istihsan over qiyas), and examples of the first type are countless.
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage discusses the interaction between qiyas and istihsan using the example of sajdah tilawah. The author argues that the purpose (maqsad) of sajdah tilawah is ta'zim (glorification) and tawadu' (humility), not qurbah (nearness to Allah) as an end in itself. Therefore, it can be validly performed by ruku' (bowing) in prayer, contrary to the general rule that sajdah cannot be replaced by ruku'. The qiyas (analogy) that leads to this conclusion is called qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) and its inner effect (bātini asar) is strong because it aligns with the underlying purpose. The istihsan, on the other hand, draws an analogy between sajdah tilawah and sajdah salat (prostration in prayer), treating both as qurbah maqsūdah (intended nearness), but this is weak because sajdah tilawah is not qurbah maqsūdah. The author concludes that in such cases where the inner effect of qiyas is strong and that of istihsan is weak, qiyas is preferred over istihsan, although instances of this type are rare compared to cases where istihsan is preferred.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogy in legal reasoning; specifically here, qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) based on underlying purpose.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference; a method that overrides qiyas jali in favor of a stronger evidence or a hidden analogy.
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): Hidden analogy; an analogy that is not immediately apparent but is discovered by deeper consideration of the underlying cause.
باطنی اثر (bātini asar): Inner effect; the underlying purpose or rationale that gives a legal reasoning its true strength.
ظاہری اثر (zāhiri asar): Outer effect; the surface-level analogy or literal application of a rule.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the istihsan's inner effect considered weak?
A) Because it contradicts a Quranic verse.
B) Because it analogizes sajdah tilawah to sajdah salat, which have different purposes.
C) Because it is based on a weak hadith.
D) Because it is not accepted by any other school.

Key Takeaway
When qiyas and istihsan conflict, preference is given to the one with the stronger inner effect (bātini asar), even if the outer effect is weaker.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
intermediate
8 min
Types of Istihsan and Ta'diyah of Rulings
Explaining which types of istihsan produce transferable rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which types of istihsan allow analogical extension (ta'diyah) and apply this rule to classify new cases.

Core Idea
Only istihsan by hidden qiyas allows ta'diyah; text, consensus, and necessity confine rulings to their original cases.

Istihsan is a key Hanafi proof that overrides qiyas jali in certain cases. However, not all istihsan rulings can be extended to new situations by analogy. This lesson explores the classification of istihsan into four types based on its source and explains a critical difference: only rulings derived from istihsan by hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi) have a generalizable cause that permits ta'diyah. The other three types—based on explicit text, consensus, or necessity—remain specific to their context. We will examine the rule through the example of the seller's oath in a price dispute, which also reveals an intra-Hanafi difference of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of istihsan
List the four sources that can serve as the basis of istihsan: text (nass/athar), consensus (ijma'), necessity (darurah), and hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi). Recognize that each type overrides qiyas jali.
The passage uses 'athar' for text, but it includes Quran and hadith.
2
State the rule for ta'diyah
The passage explicitly states that only the ruling derived from istihsan by qiyas khafi can be transferred (ta'diyah) to other cases. Rulings from the other three types cannot be extended because they are based on specific textual evidence, consensus, or necessity that does not yield a generalizable cause.
Ta'diyah means extending the ruling by analogy using the extracted 'illah.
3
Apply the rule to the example of the seller's oath
Before delivery, if a dispute arises about the price, qiyas jali would not require an oath from the seller (he is the defendant), but istihsan by qiyas khafi requires it. This ruling can be transferred to heirs and lease contracts. After delivery, the oath is required only by text (athar), and according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, this ruling cannot be extended.
The example shows how the rule operates: the pre-delivery ruling is based on hidden qiyas and extends; the post-delivery ruling is based on text and does not.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the post-delivery oath ruling (based on text) cannot be transferred. It does not mention Imam Muhammad's view, but a difference may exist. The practical consequence is that in cases analogous to post-delivery, the oath rule is not extended according to these two imams.
This difference illustrates the importance of identifying the basis of the ruling before attempting analogical extension.

نہیں کرتا ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ مدعی ہے، اور یہ اختلاف استحسانا بائع پر قسم واجب کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ بائع مبیع کی تسلیم کا انکار کرتا ہے اس شمن کے بدلہ جس کا مشتری دعوی کرتا ہے اور یہ ایسا حکم ہے جو وارثین حکم استحسان بالنص سے ثابت ہے،۔۔ اور کبھی قیاس جلی کے معارض اجماع ہوتا ہے، تو اس کو استحسان بالا جماع کہتے ہیں ، اور کبھی ضرورت قیاس جلی کے معارض ہوتی ہے اس کو استحسان بالضرورۃ کہتے ہیں، اور کبھی قیاس Then that which is deemed preferable (mustahsan) by hidden qiyas, its transference is valid, unlike that which is deemed preferable by textual evidence (athar) or consensus (ijma') or necessity (darurah), like salam sale, istisna'a, and purification of tanks, wells, and vessels. Do you not see that a dispute about the price before delivery of the sold item does not necessitate an oath for the seller by qiyas because he is the claimant, but istihsan necessitates it because he denies delivery of the sold item in exchange for the price claimed by the buyer. And this is a ruling that transfers to heirs and to lease. But after delivery, the seller's oath is not necessitated by it except by textual evidence, contrary to qiyas according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; thus its transference is not valid. Translation: Then that which is mustahsan by qiyas khafi, its transference is valid, contrary to that ruling which is mustahsan by text or consensus or necessity, such as salam sale, istisna'a, and purification of tanks, wells, and vessels. Do you not see that dispute in the price before delivery of the sold item does not necessitate an oath for the seller by qiyas because he is the claimant, and this dispute necessitates it by istihsan because the seller denies delivery of the sold item in exchange for that price which the buyer claims. And this is a ruling that transfers to heirs and to lease. So in any case, after delivery, due to the dispute, the seller's oath is not necessitated, but contrary to qiyas only by text (athar) according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, so its transference is not valid. Explanation: Istihsan is a proof that opposes qiyas jali. The opponent to qiyas jali is sometimes text, which the author has called athar. When text opposes, the ruling established from it is said to be established by istihsan bil-nass. And sometimes the opponent to qiyas jali is consensus, so it is called istihsan bil-ijma'. And sometimes necessity opposes qiyas jali, so it is called istihsan bil-darurah. And sometimes hidden qiyas opposes, so it is called istihsan bil-qiyas. In short, just as a shar'i ruling is established by qiyas jali, similarly there are four other proofs that oppose it: (1) istihsan bil-nass, (2) istihsan bil-ijma', (3) istihsan bil-darurah, (4) istihsan bil-qiyas. Now the author intends to explain in this passage: among the rulings established by these proofs, where the ruling remains confined to its locus and where the ruling can be transferred from the original to a branch. Thus he said: if a ruling is established by istihsan bil-qiyas in opposition to qiyas jali, then its transference is valid, meaning that by extracting the cause of that ruling, the ruling can be transferred to a branch, and others can be analogized to it. And besides istihsan bil-qiyas, the remaining three types, i.e., istihsan bil-nass, istihsan bil-ijma', and istihsan bil-darurah, the ruling established from these three...
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage introduces a key rule about the scope of istihsan. Istihsan can be based on four sources: text (nass/athar), consensus (ijma'), necessity (darurah), or hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi). The author explains that only rulings derived from istihsan based on qiyas khafi can be transferred (ta'diyah) to other cases by extracting the underlying cause. Rulings from istihsan based on text, consensus, or necessity remain confined to their original context and cannot be extended analogically. An example is given: before delivery of a sold item, if a dispute arises about the price, qiyas jali would require no oath from the seller because he is the defendant, but istihsan requires an oath because the seller denies receipt of the price. This ruling can be transferred to heirs and lease contracts. However, after delivery, the rule changes and only text supports the oath, and according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, that ruling cannot be transferred.

Key Terms
الاستحسان بالقياس (al-istihsan bi al-qiyas): Istihsan based on hidden qiyas; when a hidden analogy overrides a clear analogy.
تعدية الحكم (ta'diyat al-hukm): Extension of a ruling from its original case to new cases by analogy.
الاستحسان بالأثر (al-istihsan bi al-athar): Istihsan based on a textual evidence (athar) from Quran or Hadith.
الاستحسان بالضرورة (al-istihsan bi al-darurah): Istihsan based on necessity, allowing exceptions to general rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which type of istihsan allows its ruling to be transferred (ta'diyah) to other cases?
A) Istihsan by text (athar)
B) Istihsan by consensus (ijma')
C) Istihsan by necessity (darurah)
D) Istihsan by hidden qiyas (qiyas khafi)

Key Takeaway
Only rulings from istihsan by hidden qiyas can be transferred; those from text, consensus, or necessity are confined to their original cases.
