Istihsan — Juristic Preference
intermediate
8 min
Refutation of Takhsis al-Illah in Istihsan
Defending Hanafi istihsan against charge of causing takhsis al-illah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that istihsan does not constitute takhsis al-illah, and apply the distinction between 'adam al-illah and a preventer to the case of the forgetful fasting person.

Core Idea
Istihsan does not specify the cause; it eliminates the cause itself, avoiding logical contradiction.

This passage defends the Hanafi position that istihsan is not a specification of the cause (takhsis al-illah) but rather a case where the cause itself is absent. The objector claims that when a jurist abandons qiyas jali for istihsan, the cause of the qiyas exists but is prevented. The Hanafi response distinguishes between non-existence of the cause and prevention. Understanding this distinction is essential to grasping the Hanafi theory of istihsan as a valid source of law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Define takhsis al-illah: the claim that a cause (illah) exists but its ruling is blocked by a preventer (mani'). The objector argues that istihsan does exactly this.
This is a methodological challenge to Hanafi usul.
2
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi response: when a text, consensus, necessity, or a stronger analogy (istihsan) opposes qiyas jali, the cause in qiyas jali does not remain. The ruling's absence is due to 'adam al-illah (non-existence of the cause), not a preventer.
The opponent's initial objection involving nass/ijma/darurah is refuted first, then the case of istihsan vs. qiyas jali is addressed.
3
Understand the objector's challenge
The objector concedes that nass/ijma/darurah annul the qiyas, but insists that when istihsan (another qiyas) opposes qiyas jali, the initial cause still exists but is overridden — this is takhsis.
This is the crux of the dispute.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The text argues that istihsan (qiyas khafi) is stronger in effect, so it completely abrogates qiyas jali, leaving no cause. Hence again it is 'adam al-illah, not takhsis.
The conclusion: istihsan in no respect falls under takhsis.
5
Apply to the fasting example
Forgetful eating/drinking: the opponent says the cause (loss of abstention) exists but is prevented by the hadith. The Hanafi says the cause is absent because the act is attributed to Allah, so no transgression occurred.
This example illustrates converting the opponent's proof into proof of 'adam al-illah.

الفیضُ الحجازي
۲۷۷
شرح اردو المنتخب الحسامي
شرعیہ احکام شرع کی دلیلیں اور علامات ہوتی ہیں ، لہذا جہاں بھی علت ہوگی وہ حکم کو ثابت کرے گی اور حکم کی دلیل ہوگی، اگر حکم کا علت سے تخلُّف ہوا تو مناقضہ ہوگا یعنی علت چاہے گی کہ حکم ثابت ہو اور تخلف چاہے گا کہ حکم ثابت نہ ہو حالانکہ ایک ساتھ دونوں باتیں ناممکن ہیں، اس کا نام ہے مناقضہ ، معلوم ہوا کہ مانع کی وجہ سے بھی تخلف باطل ہے۔ معترض کہتا ہے کہ آپ استحسان ( قیاس خفی ) کی وجہ سے قیاس جلی کو چھوڑ دیتے ہیں، تو یہ تخصیص علت ہی ہوا، کیونکہ قیاس جلی موجود ہے اور آپ نے اس کو چھوڑ کر استحسان پر عمل کیا، تو گویا قیاس جلی میں جو علت ہے اس کو ایک مانع استحسان کے مقابل میں آنے کی وجہ سے چھوڑ دیا، اس کا نام تخصیص علت ہے، مصنف، اللہ اسی کا جواب ( دے رہے ہیں کہ استحسان تخصیص علت کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے، یعنی ایسا نہیں ہے کہ استحسان کی وجہ سے قیاس جلی میں تخصیص ہوئی کیونکہ قیاس میں جو وصف علت ہے، جب اس کے مقابل میں نص، اجماع یا ضرورۃ آجائے گی تو قیاس کی علت وہ باقی ہی نہیں رہے گی، کیونکہ قیاس کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط ہے کہ وہ نص کے مقابلہ میں نہ ہو، جب اس کے مقابل میں نص ہوگی تو قیاس صحیح نہ ہوگا، تو اس کی علت باقی نہ رہے گی اور نص، اجماع اور ضرورۃ تینوں ایک درجہ میں ہیں، کیونکہ ضرورۃ اجماع کے درجہ میں ہے اور اجماع کتاب وسنت کے مثل ہے، لہذا جیسے نص کے مقابلہ میں قیاس صحیح نہیں ہے، ایسے ہی اجماع اور ضرورۃ کے مقابلہ میں بھی قیاس صحیح نہیں ہوا، تو اس کی علت بھی نہ رہی لہذا تخصیص علت والا اعتراض واقع نہ ہوگا۔ معترض کہتا ہے کہ ان تین چیزوں میں تو آپ کی بات سمجھ میں آگئی کہ نص اجماع اور ضرورۃ کے مقابلہ میں قیاس باقی نہیں رہتا۔ لیکن اگر قیاس جلی کے مقابل میں استحسان آجائے تو یہاں تو آپ کو تخصیص علت کا قائل ہونا پڑے گا، کیونکہ یہاں تو دو قیاسوں میں ٹکراؤ ہے ، مصنف اسی بات کو اگلی عبارت میں واضح کر رہے ہیں ۔ وكذا اذا عارضه : - اس طرح جب استحسان قیاس جلی کے معارض ہوگا تو قیاس جلی کا عدم ثابت ہوگا یعنی قیاس جلی باقی ہی نہیں رہے گا کیونکہ استحسان ( قیاس خفی ) قوی التاثیر ہے تو اس کو ترجیح ہوگی ، اور اس کے مقابلہ میں قیاس جلی باقی ہی نہ رہے گا ، نہ اس کی علت باقی رہے گی، تو عدم حکم عدم علت سے ہوا، یہ نہ کہونگے کہ علت تو باقی ہے مگر مانع کی وجہ سے حکم نہ پایا گیا، خلاصہ یہ ہوا کہ استحسان کسی بھی اعتبار سے تخصیص علت کے قبیل سے نہیں ہے۔ صاحب حسامی کہتے ہیں کہ جو بات ہم نے استحسان و قیاس میں کہی کہ عدم حکم عدم علت کی وجہ سے ہوا، تمام علل مؤشرہ میں ہم یہی بات کہتے ہیں کہ جہاں بھی حکم کا تخلف ہو گا عدم علت کی وجہ سے ہوگا۔ وبيان ذلك : - مذکورہ اختلاف پر تفریح پیش کر رہے ہیں کہ اگر کسی روزہ دار کے حلق میں زبردستی پانی ڈال دیا گیا تو اس کا روزہ ٹوٹ گیا، کیونکہ روزہ کا رکن (امساک) فوت گیا، اس پر اعتراض ہو گا ناسی کا کہ بھول کر اگر کسی نے کھا پیا تو اس کا روزہ نہیں ٹوتا ہے، حالانکہ علت پائی گئی روزہ کا رکن یعنی امساک فوت ہو گیا تو روزہ ٹوٹنا چاہیے۔ تو فریق اول جو تخصیص علت کا قائل ہے وہ تو کہتا ہے کہ یہاں علت تو پائی گئی ( یعنی فوات امساک ) مگر حکم ( فسادِصوم ) ایک مانع کی وجہ سے نہیں پایا گیا ، مانع وہ حدیث ہے جس میں فرمایا انما اطعمه الله وسقاه ، اس کو اللہ نے کھلایا پلایا ہے، ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ ناسی کے روزہ کا عدم فساد عدم علت کی وجہ سے ہے، ہمارے نزدیک علت یعنی فوات امساک ہوا ہی نہیں، کیونکہ ناسی کا فعل اللہ کی طرف منسوب ہے یعنی اللہ نے اس کو کھلایا پلایا تو گویا اس نے کھایا پیا ہی نہیں، لہذا اس سے جنایت کے معنی ساقط ہو جا ئیں گے اور اس سے جو کھانے پینے کا فعل ہوا ہے وہ معاف ہو جائے گا، تو روزہ کا رکن باقی ہے، اس لئے روزہ باقی ہے، ایسا نہیں ہے کہ روزہ کا رکن تو فوت ہو گیا مگر مانع کی وجہ سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹا۔ الغرض فریق اول نے جس چیز کو ( حدیث رسول انما اطعمه الله وسقاه ) تخصیص علت کی دلیل قراردیا، اسی چیز کو ہم نے عدم علت کی دلیل قرار دیا جس کی وضاحت تشریح میں ہو گئی۔ مصنف یہ کہتے ہیں کہ یہ یعنی تخصیص علت کی دلیل کو عدم علت کی دلیل قرار دینا، اس فصل کی بنیاد ہے، اس کو یاد کرلو،مضبوط کرلو، اس میں بہت ثاقبہ ہے اس باب کے بہت سارے مسائل اس اصل پر متفرع ہیں اور اس میں بہت سارے اعتراضات سے چھٹکارا ہے۔
اللہ
Al-Fayd al-Hijazi 277: Explanation in Urdu of al-Muntakhab al-Husami. Legal rulings have proofs and signs of the Shari'a, so wherever the cause exists it will establish the ruling and be the proof of the ruling. If the ruling deviates from the cause, then a contradiction occurs, meaning the cause wants the ruling to be established and the deviation wants the ruling not to be established, yet both things together are impossible. This is called contradiction. It is known that deviation due to a preventer is also invalid. The objector says: You abandon qiyas jali because of istihsan (qiyas khafi), so this is specification of the cause, because qiyas jali exists and you abandoned it and acted on istihsan. So it is as if the cause in qiyas jali was abandoned due to the preventer of istihsan coming in opposition. This is called specification of the cause. The author, may Allah, answers that istihsan is not of the category of specification of the cause, meaning it is not that specification occurred in qiyas jali due to istihsan, because when the attribute that is the cause in qiyas is opposed by a text, consensus, or necessity, then that cause in qiyas does not remain, because for the validity of qiyas it is a condition that it not be in opposition to a text. When it is opposed by a text, qiyas is not valid, so its cause does not remain. And text, consensus, and necessity are all at one level, because necessity is at the level of consensus, and consensus is like the Book and Sunnah. So just as qiyas is not valid in opposition to a text, similarly qiyas is not valid in opposition to consensus and necessity, so its cause also does not remain, hence the objection of specification of the cause does not occur. The objector says: In these three things your point is understood that qiyas does not remain in opposition to text, consensus, and necessity. But if istihsan opposes qiyas jali, then here you will have to accept specification of the cause, because here there is a clash between two qiyases. The author clarifies this in the next phrase: 'And likewise when it opposes it' - thus when istihsan opposes qiyas jali, the non-existence of qiyas jali is established, meaning qiyas jali does not remain, because istihsan (qiyas khafi) is stronger in effect, so it is given precedence, and in its face qiyas jali does not remain, and its cause does not remain. So the non-existence of the ruling arises from the non-existence of the cause. We do not say that the cause remains but the ruling is not found due to a preventer. The conclusion is that istihsan is in no respect from the category of specification of the cause. The author of al-Husami says: What we said about istihsan and qiyas, that non-existence of the ruling is due to non-existence of the cause, we say the same regarding all indicative causes: wherever the ruling deviates, it is due to non-existence of the cause. 'And the explanation of that' - he gives a clarification of the mentioned disagreement: if someone forcibly pours water down the throat of a fasting person, his fast is broken, because the pillar of fasting (abstention) is lost. An objection is raised: the one who forgets - if he eats or drinks forgetfully, his fast is not broken, even though the cause is found: the pillar of fasting, i.e., abstention, is lost, so the fast should break. The first party who believes in specification of the cause says: Here the cause is found (i.e., loss of abstention) but the ruling (invalidity of fast) is not found due to a preventer, and the preventer is the hadith in which the Prophet said, 'Verily, Allah fed him and gave him drink.' Our answer is that the non-invalidity of the fast of the forgetful person is due to non-existence of the cause. According to us, the cause, i.e., loss of abstention, did not occur, because the act of the forgetful person is attributed to Allah, i.e., Allah fed him and gave him drink, so it is as if he did not eat or drink. Hence the meaning of transgression falls away from it, and the act of eating and drinking is forgiven. So the pillar of fasting remains, therefore the fast remains. It is not that the pillar of fasting was lost but the fast did not break due to a preventer. In summary, what the first party took as a proof for specification of the cause (the hadith 'Verily, Allah fed him and gave him drink') we took as a proof for non-existence of the cause, as clarified in the commentary. The author says that this - i.e., taking the proof of specification of the cause as a proof for non-existence of the cause - is the foundation of this chapter. Memorize it, strengthen it; it has great sharpness. Many issues of this chapter branch off from this principle, and it brings deliverance from many objections. Allah.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a detailed disputation defending the Hanafi position that istihsan does not constitute takhsis al-illah (specification of the cause) in qiyas. The objector (mu'tarid) claims that when a Hanafi abandons qiyas jali (manifest analogy) in favor of istihsan (hidden analogy/preference), this amounts to specifying the cause of the qiyas jali, i.e., the cause exists but is prevented from operating by istihsan. The author refutes this by distinguishing between the absence of the cause ('adam al-illah) and the presence of a preventer (mani'). The author first argues that when a text (nass), consensus (ijma'), or necessity (darurah) opposes the qiyas, the qiyas itself becomes invalid, so its cause does not remain; hence there is no specification but rather complete negation of the cause. Then the objector raises the case where istihsan (qiyas khafi) opposes qiyas jali. The author responds that istihsan is stronger in effect, so it abrogates the qiyas jali entirely; again the cause is absent, not merely prevented. The author then provides a concrete example from fiqh: a fasting person who is forced to drink has his fast broken, but a person who forgetfully eats or drink does not. The proponent of takhsis says the cause (loss of abstention) exists but is prevented by the hadith 'Allah fed him and gave him drink.' The Hanafi response is that the act of the forgetful person is attributed to Allah, so the causal element (transgression) is absent; therefore the cause (loss of abstention) itself is not realized. Hence the fast remains intact. This example illustrates that what appears to be a preventer is actually evidence that the cause does not exist. The author emphasizes that this principle — converting proof of takhsis into proof of 'adam al-illah — is the foundation of the chapter and resolves many objections.

Key Terms
تخصیص علت (takhsis al-illah): Specification of the cause: claiming that a cause (illah) exists but its effect (ruling) is blocked due to a preventer (mani'), resulting in an exception.
استحسان (istihsan): A legal method where a jurist prefers an alternative ruling due to a stronger evidence (like hidden analogy, custom, or necessity), even if it contradicts a prima facie qiyas jali.
عدم علت ('adam al-illah): Non-existence of the cause: the legal cause itself is absent, so the ruling does not apply; this is different from a preventer blocking the cause's effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example of the forgetful fasting person, how does the Hanafi refutation of takhsis al-illah explain the fast not being broken?
A) The cause (loss of abstention) exists but is blocked by the hadith as a preventer.
B) The cause (loss of abstention) does not exist because the act is attributed to Allah, so the pillar of fasting remains.
C) The fast is not broken because istihsan allows an exception for forgetfulness.
D) The cause is specified only for intentional acts, not for forgetful ones.

Key Takeaway
Istihsan does not specify the cause; it negates it. The distinction between 'adam al-illah and a preventer is crucial to understanding Hanafi usul and defending istihsan as a valid source.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference

Mumānaʿah: The Four Methods of Refuting a Causal Argument
Explains mumānaʿah as a method of refuting causal arguments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four types of mumānaʿah and apply each to refute an opponent's causal argument (taʿlīl).

Core Idea
Mumānaʿah means denying a specific premise of the causal proof; it takes four forms.

In Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh, after establishing a cause (ʿilla) through ṭard and ʿaks, the opponent may still refute the argument. This passage introduces mumānaʿah, a set of refutation strategies targeting either the attribute, its suitability, the ruling, or the causal link. Understanding these four types equips you to evaluate and deconstruct legal analogies.

Guided Path
1
Define mumānaʿah
Mumānaʿah is the objector's refusal to accept a specific premise of the opponent's proof. It is a dialectical tool to break the causal argument.
It requires identifying which premise is being denied.
2
List the four divisions
The four types are: (1) denial of the attribute itself, (2) denial of the attribute's suitability for the ruling, (3) denial of the ruling itself, and (4) denial of the attribution of the ruling to the attribute.
Memorize these categories.
3
Analyze the first type: denial of the attribute itself
Study the kaffāra example: Shafi'is claim sexual intercourse is the cause; Hanafis deny that attribute, asserting instead 'intentional breaking of the fast' as the cause.
The objector need not propose an alternative attribute; denial suffices.
4
Analyze the second type: denial of suitability
Study the guardianship example: Shafi'is claim virginity as cause; Hanafis accept virginity but argue it lacks effect elsewhere (ṭard), so it is not suitable.
Suitability requires the attribute to show effect in other cases.
5
Analyze the third and fourth types: denial of ruling and attribution
In the wudu example, Hanafis either deny the ruling (triple performance as Sunnah) or deny that the attribute (pillarhood) is the cause of that ruling, showing inconsistencies.
These types often overlap; the goal is to sever the causal link.

دو طرح کی ہیں، ایک یہ کہ بندہ خود تعیین کرے جیسے نذر کا روزہ اور دوم یہ کہ شریعت تعیین کرے، رمضان کے روزے میں شریعت کی تعیین موجود ہے، لہذا مطلق نیت سے بھی رمضان کا روزہ ادا ہو جائے گا ۔۔ تو یہاں ہم نے فریق مخالف کی علت کو تسلیم کر کے حکم اس کے خلاف ثابت کیا، مطلق نیت سے روزہ کا ادا ہونا ثابت کر دیا تو ہم نے شوافع کے اس استدلال کو دفع کر دیا، اس کا نام ہے قول بموجب العلۃ ۔
وَأَمَّا الْمُمَانَعَةُ فَهِيَ أَرْبَعَةُ أَقْسَامِ مُمَانَعَةٌ فِي نَفْسِ الْوَصْفِ وَفِي صَلَاحِهِ لِلْحُكْمِ وَفِي نَفْسِ الْحُكْمِ وَفِي نِسْبَتِهِ إِلَى الْوَصْفِ ترجمہ :۔ اور بہر حال ممانعت پس وہ چار قسم پر ہے، نفس وصف کا انکار کر دینا ، وصف کا حکم کے لئے صالح ہونے سے انکار کر دینا نفس حکم کا انکار کر دینا ، وصف کی طرف حکم کے منسوب ہونے کا انکار کرنا۔ تشریح : - علت طرد یہ کو دفع کرنے کا دوسرا طریقہ ممانعت ہے، ممانعت اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ معترض مغلک کی دلیل کے تمام مقدمات کو یا بعض متعین اجزا کو قبول کرنے سے انکار کر دے۔ ممانعت کی چار قسمیں ہیں ، (۱) نفس وصف کا انکار کرنا (۲) وصف کا صالح الحکم ہونے کا انکار کرنا (۳) نفس حکم کا انکار کرنا (۴) حکم کے وصف کی طرف منسوب ہونے کا انکار کرنا۔ پہلی قسم : ممانعت في نفس الوصف یہ ہے کہ معتل نے جس وصف کو علت قرار دیا ہے، معترض اس وصف کو علت ماننے سے انکار کر دے۔ جیسے امام شافعی سے کہتے ہیں کہ رمضان کا روزہ اگر جماع سے توڑا ہے تو کفارہ واجب ہے اور اگر کھانے پینے سے توڑا ہے تو کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے، تو کفارہ کا سبب انہوں نے جماع کو قرار دیا۔ اس پر ہم احناف کہتے ہیں کہ جماع کو کفارہ کی علت ہم تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے ، بلکہ عمداً افطار ( روزہ توڑنا) کفارہ کی علت ہے، اور عمداً افطار کھانے پینے سے بھی ہوتا ہے، لہذا کھانے پینے سے بھی کفارہ واجب ہوگا، جماع اگر علت ہوتا تو بھول کر جماع سے بھی کفارہ واجب ہوتا حالانکہ بھول کر جماع سے کفارہ واجب نہیں ہے۔ غرض معلل نے جس وصف کو حکم کی علت قرار دیا معترض نے اس علت کو توڑ دیا۔ دوسری قسم: یہ ہے کہ معترض معلل کے وصف کو تو تسلیم کرے لیکن یہ تسلیم نہ کرے کہ اس وصف میں حکم کو ثابت کرنے کی صلاحیت ہے، جیسے امام شافعی اللہ نے باکرہ پر ولایت کو ثابت کرنے کی علت بکارت کو قرار دیا، اور دلیل یہ دی کہ باکرہ مردوں کے ساتھ زندگی گزارنے کا تجربہ نہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے نکاح کے مصالح سے ناواقف ہے، اس لئے باکرہ پر ولایت ثابت ہوگی۔ اس پر ہم کہتے ہیں کہ وصف بکارت تو تسلیم ہے لیکن اس میں حکم کی علت بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں ہے، کیونکہ بکارت کی تاثیر کسی اور جگہ ظاہر نہیں ہوئی ہے، بلکہ جو وصف ولایت کی صلاحیت رکھتا ہے وہ صفر ہے، کیونکہ وصف صغر کا اثر دوسری جگہ یعنی ولایت مال میں ظاہر ہو چکا ہے، لہذا وصف صغر حکم کی علت ہوگا ، غرض معترض نے معلل کے وصف کو صالح الحکم تسلیم نہیں کیا۔
تیسری قسم: یہ ہے کہ معترض وصف کو بھی تسلیم کرے، اور اس میں حکم کی صلاحیت کو بھی تسلیم کرے البتہ حکم کا انکار کر دے، اور کہے کہ حکم یہ نہیں جو آپ نے ثابت کیا، بلکہ دوسرا ہے۔ جیسے امام شافعی اللہ نے فرمایا کہ وضو میں چہرہ اور ہاتھ کو تین مرتبہ دھونا مسنون ہے، کیونکہ چہرہ کا دھونا رکن ہے، اور یہ رکنیت کی علت سر کے مسح میں بھی پائی جاتی ہے، لہذا سر کے مسح میں بھی تثلیث مسنون ہے، تو یہاں علت رکنیت اور حکم تثلیث ہے، ہم احناف نے کہا کہ ہم حکم یعنی تثلیث مسنون ہونے کو تسلیم ہی نہیں کرتے ، بلکہ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ فرض ادا ہونے کے بعد محل فرض میں کچھ زیادتی کر کے فرض کو کامل و مکمل کرنا مسنون ہے، اور چونکہ وضو میں پورا چہرہ دھونا فرض ہے، تو اس میں اکمال کی سنت حاصل کرنے کے لئے تثلیث کا حکم دیا اور سر کے مسح میں پورے سر کا مسح فرض نہیں ہے اس لئے اس میں اکمال پورے سر کے مسح سے ہو جائے گا، اس لئے مسح ایک مرتبہ مسنون ہے۔ چوتھی قسم: یہ ہے کہ معترض حکم کے اس وصف کی طرف منسوب ہونے کو تسلیم نہ کرے، یعنی معترض یوں کہے کہ حکم اس وصف کی طرف منسوب نہیں ہے، بلکہ دوسرے وصف کی طرف منسوب ہے، لہذا اوپر والے مسئلہ میں ہم کہتے ہیں کہ آپ نے حکم یعنی تثلیث کو وصف رکنیت کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے یعنی رکنیت کو تثلیث کی علت بتایا، تو پھر نماز میں قیام، رکوع ، قرآت سجدہ سب رکن ہیں، تو ان میں بھی تثلیث ہونی چاہیے حالانکہ کوئی بھی اس کا قائل نہیں ہے، نیز مضمضہ اور استنشاق میں بھی باوجود رکن نہ ہونے کے تثلیث مسنون ہے، معلوم ہوا کہ تثلیث کے مسنون ہونے کی علت رکنیت نہیں ہے۔
There are two types [of intention]: one is that the servant himself specifies, like the fast of a vow; and the second is that the Shari'ah specifies. In the fast of Ramadan, the specification of the Shari'ah is present, so even with an absolute intention the fast of Ramadan will be performed... So here we accepted the opponent's cause and established the ruling contrary to it; we established that the fast is performed with absolute intention, thus we repelled the argument of the Shafi'is. This is called 'qawl bi-mūjib al-ʿillah'. As for al-mumānaʿah, it has four types: prevention regarding the attribute itself, regarding its suitability for the ruling, regarding the ruling itself, and regarding its attribution to the attribute. Translation: And in any case, prevention is of four types: denying the attribute itself, denying the suitability of the attribute for the ruling, denying the ruling itself, and denying the attribution of the ruling to the attribute. Explanation: The second method of repelling the causal argument is mumānaʿah. Mumānaʿah is that the objector refuses to accept all or some specific premises of the proponent's argument. Mumānaʿah has four types: (1) Denying the attribute itself. (2) Denying the suitability of the attribute for the ruling. (3) Denying the ruling itself. (4) Denying the attribution of the ruling to the attribute. First type: Mumānaʿah fī nafs al-waṣf: The objector denies accepting the attribute that the proponent has made the cause. For example, the Shafi'is say that if the fast of Ramadan is broken by sexual intercourse, expiation is obligatory, but if broken by eating or drinking, expiation is not obligatory. So they made sexual intercourse the cause of expiation. We Hanafis say: We do not accept sexual intercourse as the cause of expiation; rather, intentional breaking of the fast is the cause of expiation, and intentional breaking occurs by eating and drinking as well, so expiation is obligatory for eating and drinking too. If sexual intercourse were the cause, then expiation would be obligatory even if one forgets and has intercourse, but it is not. In short, the proponent made a certain attribute the cause of the ruling; the objector refuted that cause. Second type: The objector accepts the attribute but does not accept that this attribute has the capacity to establish the ruling. For example, Imam Shafi'i made virginity the cause for establishing guardianship over a virgin, giving the reason that a virgin, not having experience of living with men, is unaware of the benefits of marriage, so guardianship is established over her. We say: We accept the attribute of virginity, but it does not have the capacity to be the cause of the ruling, because the effect of virginity has not appeared elsewhere. Rather, the attribute that has the capacity for guardianship is minority (ṣighar), because the effect of the attribute of minority has appeared elsewhere, namely in guardianship over property. Therefore, the attribute of minority is the cause of the ruling. In short, the objector did not accept the proponent's attribute as suitable for the ruling. Third type: The objector accepts both the attribute and its suitability for the ruling, but denies the ruling itself, saying that the ruling is not what you established but something else. For example, Imam Shafi'i said that washing the face and hands three times in wudu is Sunnah, because washing the face is a pillar (rukn), and this attribute of being a pillar is also found in wiping the head, so triple wiping is also Sunnah. Here the cause is pillarhood and the ruling is triple performance. We Hanafis say: We do not accept the ruling that triple performance is Sunnah; rather we say that after performing the obligatory act, adding something extra to complete and perfect the obligatory act is Sunnah. Since washing the whole face in wudu is obligatory, triple washing is prescribed to attain the Sunnah of completion. But wiping the whole head is not obligatory, so completion is achieved by wiping the whole head once, therefore wiping once is Sunnah. Fourth type: The objector does not accept that the ruling is attributed to this attribute, meaning he says the ruling is not attributed to this attribute but to another. So in the above issue, we say: You attributed the ruling (triple performance) to the attribute of pillarhood, i.e., you made pillarhood the cause of triple performance. Then in prayer, standing, bowing, recitation, and prostration are all pillars, so triple performance should also be prescribed in them, but no one holds that. Also, in rinsing the mouth and sniffing water, despite not being pillars, triple performance is Sunnah. So it is known that the cause of triple performance being Sunnah is not pillarhood.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage discusses the second method of refuting an opponent's causal argument (ta'līl) in Hanafi uṣūl al-fiqh: mumānaʿah (prevention or denial). The author first clarifies a preliminary point about intention (niyya) in fasting: if the Shari'a specifies the time (like Ramadan), a general intention suffices. This is an example of qawl bi-mūjib al-ʿillah (accepting the opponent's cause but deriving a different ruling). Then the main topic: mumānaʿah is defined as the objector's refusal to accept some or all premises of the proponent's proof. It has four types: (1) Denying the attribute (waṣf) itself that the proponent claims is the cause. The Hanafi example: Shafi'is say sexual intercourse is the cause of kaffāra for breaking a fast; Hanafis deny that attribute, asserting intentional breaking (including eating/drinking) is the cause. (2) Accepting the attribute but denying its suitability (ṣalāḥiyya) for the ruling. Example: Shafi'is claim virginity causes guardianship; Hanafis accept virginity but argue it is not effective, since minority (ṣighar) shows its effect elsewhere (guardianship over property). (3) Accepting attribute and suitability but denying the ruling itself. Example: Shafi'is claim that since washing the face (a pillar) is done three times in wudu, wiping the head (also a pillar) should also be done three times. Hanafis deny that triple performance is the ruling; instead, completion of the obligatory act is the goal. (4) Denying the attribution of the ruling to the attribute. Example: Shafi'is attribute triple performance to pillarhood; Hanafis show that pillarhood does not consistently necessitate triple performance (e.g., pillars in prayer are not done thrice, and non-pillars like rinsing are done thrice). Thus, the attribute is not the effective cause. The author follows the order of definition, enumeration, and detailed examples for each type, adhering strictly to Hanafi positions.

Key Terms
الممانعة (al-mumānaʿah): Refusing to accept a premise of the opponent's proof in dialectical argument.
الوصف (al-waṣf): The attribute claimed as the cause of a ruling in a qiyās argument.
صلاحية (ṣalāḥiyya): The fitness of an attribute to serve as the effective cause for a ruling, verified by ṭard and ʿaks.
الإضافة/النسبة (al-iḍāfa/al-nisba): The attribution of the ruling to the attribute; denying this means claiming the ruling is caused by a different attribute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the four types of mumānaʿah as described in the passage?
A) Denial of the attribute, denial of its suitability, denial of the ruling, denial of attribution
B) Denial of the cause, denial of the effect, denial of the condition, denial of the proof
C) Rejection of the text, rejection of analogy, rejection of consensus, rejection of reasoning
D) Accepting the cause, accepting the attribute, accepting the ruling, accepting the attribution

Key Takeaway
Mumānaʿah provides a systematic method for refuting causal arguments by targeting one of four elements: the attribute, its suitability, the ruling, or the attribution.

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
intermediate
8 min
Refuting a Rejected Cause: Corruption of Placement and Contradiction
Explains two methods to refute a rejected cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between fasād al-waḍ‘ and munāqaḍa and apply them to critique a cause in qiyas.

Core Idea
A cause that contradicts the wisdom of the ruling is corrupt in placement; a cause that fails in some applications is contradictory.

This passage equips you with two powerful tools to refute a weak cause in analogical reasoning. The first, corruption of placement, targets the very suitability of the attribute as a cause. The second, contradiction, exposes inconsistencies where the cause exists but the ruling does not. Mastering these will sharpen your ability to evaluate legal arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the alleged cause and ruling
Find the ‘illa and hukm claimed by the opponent. For example, the Shafi‘i claim that Islam of one spouse causes immediate separation.
Ensure you have the exact wording of the cause.
2
Check for corruption of placement
Ask: Is the cause inherently appropriate for the ruling? Does it align with the higher objective (maqsad) of the ruling? If not, the cause is fasād al-waḍ‘.
This is the strongest objection; it leaves no room for response.
3
Check for contradiction
Examine whether the cause exists without the ruling in any instance. If so, it is munāqaḍa. Consider whether the absence is due to a preventer.
If a preventer exists, it is naqḍ, not munāqaḍa, in debate terminology.
4
Apply the Hanafi rebuttal
State the Hanafi position and show how the cause fails using either method. For example, Islam cannot be a cause for separation because it protects rights.
The Hanafi response should directly refute the opponent’s claim.
5
Assess the opponent's escape attempt
If the opponent tries to specify the cause or introduce a distinction, evaluate whether it succeeds. For wudu versus ghusl, the Shafi‘i distinction between legal and actual purification fails because both are purifications.
A successful escape must preserve the consistency of the cause.

الْتَعَبَّدُ فَهَذِهِ الْوَجُوهُ تُلْجِئُ أَصْحَابَ الطَّرْدِ إِلَى الْقَوْلِ بِالتَّاثِيرِ ترجمہ : اور بہر حال فساد وضع پس جیسے شوافع کا علت بنانا احد الزوجین کے اسلام کو فرقت ثابت کرنے کے لئے، اور زوجین میں سے ایک کے ارتداد کو نکاح باقی رکھنے کی (علت بنانا ) پس یہ تعلیل فاسد ہے وضع کے اعتبار سے ،اس لئے کہ اسلام حقوق کے لئے قاطع بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے، اور ردت عفو کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے۔ جاتی ہے، تو معلل مجبور ہوگا مسئلہ کی وجہ بیان کرنے کی طرف، اور وہ وجہ یہ ہے کہ وضو طہارت حکمی ہے، اس لئے کہ محل غسل میں کوئی نجاست سمجھ میں نہیں آتی ہے، تو وضو نیت کے شرط ہونے میں تیمم کی طرح ہوگا ، تا کہ تعبد تحقیق ہو جائے ، پس یہ چاروں قسمیں اصحاب طرد ( شوافع ) کو تاثیر کے قائل ہونے پر مجبور کریں گی۔ تشریح :- علت طردیہ کو دفع کرنے کا تیسرا طریقہ فساد وضع ہے، فساد وضع کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ علت کی بنیاد ہی فاسد ہو، معلل نے ایسے وصف کو حکم کی علت بنایا ہے جس وصف کا حکم سے کوئی جوڑ نہیں ، بلکہ یہ وصف اس حکم کی ضد کو چاہتا ہے، جیسے شوافع کہتے ہیں کہ دو میاں بیوی میں سے ایک اسلام قبول کرلے تو ایک کے اسلام لاتے ہی دونوں میں تفریق واقع ہو جائے گی ، اگر عورت غیر مدخول بہا ہے اور اگر عورت مدخول بہا ہے تو تین حیض گذرنے پر تفریق ہو جائے گی ، تفریق واقع کرنے کے لئے دوسرے پر اسلام پیش کرنے کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے،۔۔لیکن ہم احناف کہتے ہیں کہ یہ تعلیل اپنی وضع اور بنیاد ہی میں فاسد ہے، کیونکہ اسلام تو حقوق کی حفاظت کے لئے آیا ہے، یہ تفریق کی علت کیسے بن سکتا ہے ؟ ہاں تفریق جو ہوگی وہ دوسرے کے اباء اور انکار عن الاسلام سے ہوگی ، کیونکہ ایک جب مسلمان ہو گیا تو دوسرے پر اب اسلام پیش کیا جائے گا، دوسرا بھی اسلام لے آئے تو نکاح علی حالہ باقی رہے گا ، اور نہ قبول کرے تو اس کا انکار تفریق کا سبب بن جائے گا، تو اباء اور انکار عن الاسلام کو تفریق کی علت بنانا بالکل معقول ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر میاں بیوی میں سے کوئی ایک نعوذ باللہ مرتد ہو جائے اور عورت غیر مدخول بہا ہے، تو بالاتفاق فوراً فرقت واقع ہو جائے گی ، اور اگر مدخول بہا ہے تو احناف کے نزدیک اس صورت میں بھی فوراً فرقت واقع ہو جائے گی مگر امام شافعی رضی اللہ عنہ فرماتے ہیں کہ عدت کے بعد فرقت واقع ہوگی، تو انہوں نے عدت تک نکاح کو باقی رکھا، گویا ردت کو عفو کے قابل سمجھا اور ردت کو بقائے نکاح کی علت قرار دیا، تو یہ بنیادی غلطی ہوئی کیونکہ ردت منافی نکاح ہے، کیونکہ یہ منافی عصمت ہے ، ردت کی وجہ سے جان ومال کی عصمت ختم ہو جاتی ہے، اور نکاح کا مدار عصمت پر ہے۔ فساد وضع کا اعتراض معلل پر سب سے بھاری ہے، کیونکہ اس اعتراض کے بعد معلل کو جواب دینے کی کوئی گنجائش ہی نہیں رہتی ، برخلاف مناقضہ وغیرہ کے کہ اس میں معلل مختلف تو جیہات سے بچاؤ کا راستہ ڈھونڈ لیتا ہے۔ فساد وضع کی مثال ایسی ہے، جیسے شہادت میں گواہ نے دعوی کے خلاف کوئی بات کہہ کر معاملہ خراب کر دیا، تو اس کے بعد گواہ کے عادل یا صالح ہونے نہ ہونے کی تحقیق کا کوئی سوال ہی نہیں رہتا، بلکہ دعوی خود بخود ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ واما المناقضة : - علت طردیہ کے دفع کی چوتھی قسم مناقضہ ہے، مناقضہ اس کو کہتے ہیں کہ معلل نے جس وصف کو علت بنایا ہے بعض جگہوں میں حکم کا علت سے تخلف ہو یعنی علت تو ہو مگر حکم نہ پایا جائے ، یہ تخلف چاہے مانع کی وجہ سے ہو یا بغیر مانع کے۔۔ جو حضرات تخصیص علت کے جواز کے قائل ہیں ، وہ کہتے ہیں کہ اگر تخلف بغیر مانع کے ہے تو مناقضہ ہے، اور اگر کسی مانع کی وجہ سے ہے تو مناقضہ نہیں کہیں گے بلکہ فن مناظرہ میں اس کو نقض کہا جائے گا ، مناقضہ کی مثال جیسے امام شافعی پہلے فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح تیمم میں نیت فرض ہے، ایسے ہی وضو میں بھی فرض ہے، کیونکہ دونوں صنف طہارت میں شریک ہیں ۔۔ مگر ہم کہیں گے کہ غسل ثوب اور غسل بدن سے آپ کا یہ دعوی ٹوٹ جاتا ہے، کیونکہ غسل بدن اور غسل ثوب بھی طہارت ہے، مگر اس میں نیت فرض نہیں ہے ،۔۔اس مناقضہ سے بچنے کے لئے وہ مجبور ہوں گے کہ وضو اور غسل ثوب میں فرق بیان کریں ، تو انہوں نے اس طرح فرق بیان کیا کہ غسل ثوب میں نجاست حقیقی کو دور کر کے طہارت حاصل کی جاتی ہے، یہ عقل کے عین مطابق ہے اس لئے غسل ثوب میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ البتہ وضو سے طہارت حکمی حاصل ہوتی ہے، کیونکہ اعضاء وضو پر کوئی نجاست نہیں ہے ،لہذا وضو سے طہارت حکمی یہ امر تعبدی اور امر غیر معقول ہے ، اور امر غیر معقول و امر تعبدی میں نیت کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے جیسے تیمم ، کیونکہ مٹی سے طہارت حاصل کرنا امر تعبدی و غیر معقول ہے ،اس لئے اس میں نیت فرض ہے ،لہذا وضو میں بھی نیت فرض ہوگی ، کیونکہ امور تعبدیہ میں نیت فرض ہے جیسے نماز روزہ وغیرہ، گویا انہوں نے یہ ثابت کرنے کی کوشش کی کہ حکم کا علت سے متخلف نہیں ہوا ، کیونکہ نیت حکم ہے اور طہارت حکمیہ علت ہے، نہ کہ مطلق طہارت، لہذا غسل ثوب و بدن سے دعوی نہ ٹوٹے گا۔ شوافع نے جو تو جیہ اور وجہ فرق بیان کیا ، ہم اس کو اس طرح توڑیں گے کہ نجاست نکلنے سے طہارت کا زائل ہونا اور بدن کا ناپاک ہونا امر معقول ہے، کہ جس طرح منی نکلنے سے پورا بدن ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے، اسی طرح پیشاب وغیرہ کے نکلنے سے بھی پورا بدن ناپاک ہو جاتا ہے تو قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ پیشاب وغیرہ نکلنے سے بھی پورے بدن کا غسل واجب ہوتا جیسے منی نکلنے کی صورت میں۔۔ مگر چونکہ خروج منی کا تحقق کم ہوتا ہے تو پورے بدن کے غسل سے حرج و تنگی
The devotional act? So these aspects force the people of rejection (Shafi'is) to accept effectiveness. Translation: And in any case, corruption of placement: like the Shafi'is taking as cause the Islam of one spouse to establish separation, and the apostasy of one spouse to keep the marriage remaining; this reasoning is corrupt in its placement, because Islam does not have the capacity to cut rights, and apostasy does not have the capacity for pardon. And in any case, contradiction: like the Shafi'is' saying concerning wudu and tayammum that both are purification, so how can they separate in intention? So we say that this reasoning breaks in washing actual impurity from cloth and body, so the opponent will be forced to explain the reason for the issue, and that reason is that wudu is legal purification, because no impurity is perceived in the place of washing, so wudu will be like tayammum in the condition of intention, so that the devotional act is realized. So these four types will force the people of rejection to accept effectiveness. Explanation: The third method of repelling the rejected cause is corruption of placement. The meaning of corruption of placement is that the basis of the cause itself is corrupt; the opponent has made a description a cause for a ruling that has no connection to the ruling, rather this description demands the opposite of the ruling, like the Shafi'is say that when one of the two spouses accepts Islam, as soon as one accepts Islam, separation occurs between them if the woman is non-consummated, and if the woman is consummated, separation occurs after three menstruations. There is no need to present Islam to the other for separation. But we Hanafis say that this reasoning is corrupt in its very placement, because Islam came to protect rights, how can it be a cause for separation? Yes, separation that occurs will be from the other's refusal and denial of Islam, because when one becomes Muslim, Islam will be presented to the other; if the other also accepts Islam, the marriage remains as is, and if he does not accept, his denial becomes the cause of separation. So making refusal and denial of Islam the cause of separation is entirely reasonable. Similarly, if one of the spouses, God forbid, becomes an apostate and the woman is non-consummated, then by consensus immediate separation occurs, and if consummated, according to the Hanafis immediate separation also occurs, but Imam al-Shafi'i says separation occurs after the waiting period, so he kept the marriage remaining until the waiting period, as if he considered apostasy worthy of pardon and made apostasy a cause for the continuance of marriage. This is a fundamental error because apostasy is contrary to marriage, because it is contrary to inviolability; due to apostasy, the inviolability of life and property ends, and marriage is based on inviolability. The objection of corruption of placement is the heaviest on the opponent, because after this objection there is no room for the opponent to answer, unlike contradiction and others where the opponent finds a way to escape through various explanations. The example of corruption of placement is like a witness in testimony saying something against the claim and ruining the case; thereafter there is no question of investigating whether the witness is just or righteous; rather the claim itself falls. And as for contradiction: The fourth type of repelling the rejected cause is contradiction. Contradiction is when the opponent has made a description a cause, but in some places the ruling is absent despite the cause, i.e., the cause exists but the ruling is not found. This absence may be due to a preventer or without a preventer. Those who allow specification of the cause say that if the absence is without a preventer, it is contradiction, and if due to some preventer, they will not call it contradiction but in the art of debate it is called refutation. An example of contradiction is like Imam al-Shafi'i earlier saying that just as intention is obligatory in tayammum, so too in wudu it is obligatory, because both share in the category of purification. But we say that this claim is broken by washing of cloth and washing of body, because washing of body and washing of cloth are also purification, but intention is not obligatory in them. To avoid this contradiction, they will be forced to explain the difference between wudu and washing of cloth. So they explained the difference: in washing of cloth, purification is achieved by removing actual impurity; this is exactly in accordance with reason, so there is no need for intention in washing of cloth. However, wudu produces legal purification, because there is no impurity on the limbs of wudu; therefore, legal purification from wudu is a devotional and non-rational matter, and in non-rational and devotional matters, intention is needed, like tayammum, because achieving purification from soil is a devotional and non-rational matter, so intention is obligatory in it. Therefore, intention will also be obligatory in wudu, because in devotional acts, intention is obligatory, like prayer, fasting, etc. So they attempted to prove that the ruling is not absent despite the cause, because intention is the ruling and legal purification is the cause, not absolute purification; therefore, the claim will not be broken by washing of cloth and body. The Shafi'is gave this explanation and reason for difference; we will break it in this way: that removal of purification by emission of impurity and the body becoming impure is a rational matter, just as from emission of semen the whole body becomes impure, similarly from emission of urine etc. the whole body becomes impure, so analogy would require that from emission of urine etc. also washing the whole body would be obligatory like in the case of semen emission. But because the occurrence of semen emission is rare, there would be hardship and difficulty in washing the whole body.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage explains two methods of refuting a rejected cause ('illa tardiyya) in usul al-fiqh: corruption of placement (fasād al-waḍ') and contradiction (munāqaḍa). The author first discusses fasād al-waḍ', meaning the cause's foundation is inherently corrupt. For example, the Shafi'is claim that if one spouse accepts Islam, separation occurs immediately (if non-consummated) or after three menstruations (if consummated). The Hanafis reject this because Islam is meant to protect rights, not sever them. True separation results from the other spouse's refusal of Islam after being invited. Similarly, making apostasy a cause for continuation of marriage is invalid because apostasy destroys inviolability ('iṣma) upon which marriage is based. This objection is the strongest because it leaves no room for response. The second method is contradiction: the alleged cause exists but the ruling is absent. For example, the Shafi'is argue that intention is obligatory in wudu because both wudu and tayammum are purifications, and tayammum requires intention. The Hanafis counter that washing the body or cloth (ghusl al-thawb wa ghusl al-badan) is also purification but does not require intention, thus breaking the analogy. To escape this, the Shafi'is distinguish: washing removes actual impurity (rational), while wudu is legal purification (devotional, non-rational) requiring intention. The Hanafis further rebut this by pointing out that the same logic would require ghusl for minor impurities, which is not the case. The commentary thus illustrates the usul principle that a valid cause must be consistently effective; if it fails in some applications, it is contradictory unless a preventer exists.

Key Terms
فساد الوضع (fasād al-waḍ‘): A cause is corrupt in its placement because the attribute used as cause has no connection to the ruling or actually opposes it.
مناقضة (munāqaḍa): Contradiction: the cause exists in a case but the ruling is absent, either with or without a preventer.
علة طردية (‘illa ṭardiyya): A rejected cause that is invalid because it fails the conditions of effectiveness (ta’thīr).
تخلف (takhluf): The absence of the ruling despite the presence of the alleged cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, why is the Shafi'i claim that Islam causes immediate separation between spouses considered corrupt in its placement?
A) Because Islam protects rights, so it cannot be a cause for cutting them.
B) Because separation requires a court decree.
C) Because the other spouse must also convert first.
D) Because the cause applies only to non-consummated marriages.

Key Takeaway
A cause must be both suitable for the ruling and consistently effective; fasād al-waḍ‘ attacks suitability, while munāqaḍa attacks consistency.

Daf' bi al-Wasf: Denying the Attribute to Defend a Qiyas
Explains the first method of refuting an objection: denying the attribute itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the method of daf' bi al-wasf and apply it to defend a Hanafi ruling against a naqd objection in usuli reasoning.

Core Idea
Daf' bi al-wasf denies the claimed attribute's existence in the specific case.

This lesson introduces the first method of deflecting an objection (naqd) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh: daf' bi al-wasf. When an opponent argues that a claimed cause (illa) is present in a case but the ruling is not applied, the Hanafi may respond by denying that the attribute actually exists in that case. The classic example is the ruling on wudu: Hanafis hold that any najasah exiting the body breaks wudu, while Shafi'is restrict this to the two passages. The Shafi'i objects that blood from a wound does not always break wudu, even though it is najasah. The Hanafi defense is that such blood does not truly 'exit' (khuruj) – it merely appears (zuhur) – so the attribute of khuruj is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling and the claimed illa
What is the ruling that the Hanafis defend? (Wudu breaks with any exiting najasah). What is the 'illa they propose? (Khuruj al-najasah).
The 'illa is the common attribute used in the qiyas.
2
Analyze the naqd (objection)
The Shafi'i objection: why does non-flowing blood not break wudu according to Hanafis, since the 'illa of khuruj seems present?
Naqd points to an apparent inconsistency in the Hanafi's own use of the 'illa.
3
Understand daf' bi al-wasf
The Hanafi does not concede the presence of the 'illa. He argues that the blood does not truly exit; it only appears due to skin removal. The attribute of 'khuruj' is absent.
This is a denial of the existence of the attribute (wasf), not a denial of the ruling or the qiyas itself.
4
Distinguish khuruj from zuhur
Feces truly exits from the anus because it is stored internally and moves out. Blood under the skin is already there; cutting the skin merely makes it appear. Thus, the Hanafi position is consistent.
This distinction is critical: mere appearance (zuhur) is not exit (khuruj).
5
Apply the method to the i'lal structure
Frame the qiyas: asl (urine/feces from passages) – hukm (breaks wudu) – 'illa (khuruj al-najasah). Far' (blood from elsewhere). The far' lacks the 'illa in the non-flowing case, so the ruling does not apply.
This shows how daf' bi al-wasf preserves the validity of the qiyas by showing the far' does not meet the 'illa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دفع بالوصف . جیسے احناف کے نزدیک غیر سبیلین سے ناپا کی نکلے تو ناقض وضو ہے، اور شوافع کے نزدیک ناقض وضو نہیں ہے، ہم نے علت بیان کی کہ سبیلین سے نکلنے والی نجاست (پیشاب پاخانہ ) سے وضو ٹوٹ جاتا ہے تو سبیلین کے علاوہ بدن کے کسی حصہ سے بھی نجاست جیسے خون نکلے گا، تو وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا، دونوں میں علت خروج نجاست ہے۔ اس پر امام شافعی سے نقض وار کرتے ہیں کہ جب ناپاکی نکلے اور بہے نہیں تو اس سے کیوں وضو نہیں ٹوٹتا، جب که خروج نجاست کی علت یہاں بھی ہے۔ مصنف عالی کہتے ہیں کہ ہم اس نقض کو دو طرح سے دفع کریں گے ، (۱) ایک تو اس طرح کہ ہم وصف کا انکار کرینگے یعنی ہم کہیں گے کہ وصف (علت) یعنی خروج نجاست ہے ہی نہیں ، کیونکہ ہر کھال کے نیچے خون ہوتا ہے اور ہر رگ میں خون ہے، جب کھال ہٹی تو خون کا ظہور ہوا ، خروج نہیں ہوا۔ اس پر معترض اگر کہے کہ ڈبر پر پائخانہ ظاہر ہو تو اس سے کیوں وضوٹوٹ جاتا ہے، جب کہ ظہور نجاست ہے خروج یہاں بھی نہیں ہے، ہم جواب دیں گے کہ دبر پر ظہور نہیں بلکہ خروج ہے کیوں کہ پائخانہ کا اسٹاک اندر ہوتا ہے وہاں سے منتقل ہو کر ظہور ہوا جس کو خروج کہیں گے ، لہذا اس سے وضو ٹوٹ جائے گا، بہر حال یہ دفع بالوصف ہوا۔
Deflection by the attribute. For example, according to the Hanafis, if najasah comes out from other than the two passages, it breaks wudu, and according to the Shafi'is, it does not break wudu. We explained the cause: wudu is broken by najasah (urine, feces) coming out from the two passages, so if najasah like blood comes out from any part of the body other than the two passages, wudu will break; in both, the cause is the exiting of najasah. Imam al-Shafi'i objects: when najasah comes out but does not flow, why does wudu not break, even though the cause of exiting najasah is present here? The exalted author says: we will deflect this objection in two ways. (1) One is that we deny the attribute: we say the attribute (cause), i.e., exiting of najasah, is not present, because under every skin there is blood, and in every vein there is blood; when the skin is removed, the blood appears, it does not exit. If the objector says: when feces appears at the anus, why does wudu break, even though it is appearance and not exit? We will answer: at the anus it is not appearance but exit, because the stool is stored inside, and it transfers from there and appears, which is called exit; therefore wudu breaks. In any case, this is daf' bi al-wasf.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage explains the first method of deflecting an objection (naqd) in the context of i'lal (causal reasoning). The Hanafis hold that any najasah exiting from the body breaks wudu, while the Shafi'is restrict this to the two passages. The objector (Shafi'i) argues that if blood exits but does not flow, wudu does not break according to Hanafis, contradicting their claimed 'illa (cause) of khuruj al-najasah. The Hanafi responds by denying that the blood actually exits—it merely appears due to the skin being removed, it does not exit from inside the body. This distinguishes it from feces which truly exits from the anus. Thus, the attribute (khuruj) is not present in the case of non-flowing blood, so the ruling is consistent. This is daf' bi al-wasf: denying the existence of the claimed attribute.

Key Terms
دفع بالوصف (daf' bi al-wasf): Denying the existence of the attribute claimed as the cause (illa) in a specific case.
خرج (khuruj): An entity leaving its internal origin to an external place; contrasted with mere appearance (zuhur).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How do Hanafis defend the ruling that non-flowing blood from a wound does not break wudu?
A) By denying the attribute of khuruj (exit) in that case.
B) By denying the ruling of naqd entirely.
C) By citing a Quranic verse.
D) By accepting the Shafi'i position.

Key Takeaway
Daf' bi al-wasf is a precise usuli technique: when a naqd objection claims a ruling is inconsistent, the Hanafi can deny the presence of the attribute (illa) in the contested case, thereby preserving the validity of the original qiyas.

Daf' bi al-Hukm: Affirming the Ruling, Delaying Its Effect
Explains the third method of refutation: daf' bi al-hukm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define daf' bi al-hukm and apply it to cases of continuous excusing conditions, distinguishing it from denying the ruling or the cause.

Core Idea
Daf' bi al-hukm: the ruling is established by the cause but delayed due to an excuse.

In Hanafi usul, when an objection claims that a ruling contradicts its cause, one method of refutation is daf' bi al-hukm—affirming that the ruling is indeed established but its application is postponed. This is crucial for understanding how the Hanafi school handles cases like a continuously bleeding wound or chronic urinary incontinence, where wudu would break but is delayed until the end of the prayer time to allow worship without repeated ablution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's objection
The opponent (e.g., Shafi'i) argues that if the cause (exit of impurity) is present, the ruling (wudu-breaking) must apply immediately. They see a contradiction in the Hanafi delay.
The objection targets the consistency between cause and ruling.
2
State the Hanafi position
Hanafis do not deny the ruling; they affirm that wudu is broken by the cause. However, they argue that the effect is delayed due to the excuse of continuous flow.
This is daf' bi al-hukm: affirming the ruling but delaying its application.
3
Define daf' bi al-hukm
Daf' bi al-hukm means 'deflection by the ruling': the ruling is conceded as established by the cause, but its implementation is postponed until the excuse ceases (e.g., end of prayer time).
The ruling remains binding; only the timing changes.
4
Apply to the wound case
For a person with a continuously bleeding wound, the cause (exit of blood) triggers the ruling of wudu-breaking. But due to the excuse (continuous flow), the breaking is delayed until the end of the prayer time. At that point, wudu is required even if no new hadath occurs.
This is analogous to the mustahadah (chronically bleeding woman) case.
5
Distinguish from other refutations
Daf' bi al-hukm differs from musawamah (concession of the ruling while denying the cause) and mu'aradah (equivalence, countering with another cause). Here, both cause and ruling are accepted; only the consequence is deferred.
Each method addresses a different aspect of the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اس پر امام شافعی صلى الله عليه وسلم کی طرف سے دوسرا نقض و اعتراض وارد ہوتا ہے، وہ یہ ہے کہ جس شخص کا زخم برابر بہتارہتا ہو تو اس کا وضو ٹوٹ جانا چاہیے کیونکہ وصف خروج نجاست بھی پایا گیا، اور وہ معنی جو وصف سے دلالۂ ثابت ہے یعنی موضع نجاست کا دھونا یہ بھی پایا گیا ، کیونکہ اس پر نجاست کی جگہ کا دھونا واجب ہے،لہذا وضوٹوٹ جانا چاہیے حالانکہ آپ کہتے ہیں کہ بقاء وقت تک اس کا وضو باقی رہتا ہے، تو یہ علت کا حکم سے مختلف ہے۔ مصنف یہ کہتے ہیں کہ اس نقض کو بھی ہم دو طرح سے دفع کریں گے ، (۱) ایک تو دفع بالحکم یعنی ہم حکم کو ثابت مانتے ہیں یعنی ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ علت (خروج) کی وجہ سے حکم (حدث ) ثابت ہے، ہم نہیں کہتے ہیں کہ اس کا وضو نہیں ٹوٹا ، لہذا علت کی وجہ سے حکم ثابت ہو گیا، علت کا حکم سے تخلف نہیں ہوا، لیکن جو حکم ہے یعنی وضو ٹو ٹنا یہ اس کے عذر کی وجہ سے مؤخر ہو گیا ، وقت کے بقاء تک اس کو لمبا کر دیا ، اسی لئے وقت کے ختم سے اس پر وضو لا زم ہوگا ، چاہے دوسرا کوئی حدث پیش نہ آیا ہوں۔ یہ جو ہم نے نقض کو دفع کیا اس کا نام ہے دفع بالحکم ۔
Upon this, a second objection comes from Imam al-Shafi'i: a person whose wound continuously bleeds ought to have his wudu broken because the attribute of exiting najasah is found, and also the meaning established by the attribute (washing the place of najasah) is found because washing the place of najasah is obligatory for him. Therefore, wudu ought to break, yet you (Hanafis) say that his wudu remains valid until the end of time (of prayer). So the cause differs from the ruling. The author says: we will deflect this objection in two ways. (1) One is daf' bi al-hukm: we affirm the ruling; i.e., we say that due to the cause (khuruj), the ruling (hadath) is established. We do not say that his wudu did not break. Therefore, the ruling is established by the cause; the cause is not contrary to the ruling. But the ruling (breaking of wudu) is delayed due to his excuse; it is extended until the end of the time. Hence, at the end of the time, wudu becomes necessary for him even if another hadath does not occur. This deflection of the objection is called daf' bi al-hukm.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
Here, the Hanafi commentator addresses a second objection from the Shafi'i regarding a person with a continuously flowing wound. According to the Hanafi view, such a person's wudu remains intact until the end of the prayer time. The objector argues that if the illa (khuruj and place-washing) are present, wudu should break immediately, contradicting the Hanafi ruling. The Hanafi response is daf' bi al-hukm: they do not deny that the ruling (wudu-breaking) is established; rather, they assert that it is established but delayed due to an excuse (the continuous nature of the flow). The rule is that wudu becomes obligatory at the end of the time, similar to the case of a person with urinary incontinence. Thus, the cause and ruling are not in conflict; the ruling is merely postponed.

Key Terms
دفع بالحکم (daf' bi al-hukm): Affirming that the ruling is established by the cause but is delayed in application due to an excuse.
علت (illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that triggers a ruling.
حکم (hukm): The legal ruling, e.g., breaking of wudu.
عذر (udhr): The excusing condition that justifies postponement of the ruling's effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does daf' bi al-hukm mean in the context of a continuously bleeding wound?
A) The ruling of wudu-breaking is denied completely.
B) The ruling is affirmed but its application is delayed until the end of the prayer time.
C) The cause is denied.
D) The meaning is denied.

Key Takeaway
Daf' bi al-hukm is a Hanafi tool that preserves the link between cause and ruling while accommodating excusing conditions through delayed application.

The Principle of Attributing Liability: Condition vs True Cause
Explaining the principle with the slave leg iron example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a condition removes an obstacle and a free agent causes the loss, liability is not attributed to the condition.

Core Idea
A condition that removes an obstacle is not the cause when a free agent chooses the harmful act.

In Hanafi usul, the distinction between a condition (shart) and a true cause (illa) is crucial for determining liability. This lesson examines a classic example: untying a slave's leg iron. The slave's subsequent escape is his own free act, not the result of the untying. Therefore, the one who untied is not liable. We will trace the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and classify it
Recognize that untying the leg iron is a condition (shart) because it removes an obstacle to escape.
In Hanafi usul, a condition does not generate the effect itself.
2
Identify the intervening free agent
The slave's choice to run away is the act of a free agent (fā‘il mukhtār).
A free agent's act is a capable cause (illa) for the judgment.
3
Determine the true cause
The true cause of the loss is the slave's running away, not the untying.
The causally relevant act must be the one that directly brings about the effect.
4
Apply the attribution rule
Since a true cause exists that can receive the judgment, the judgment is attributed to that cause, not the condition.
Rule: If the cause is capable of receiving the judgment, the judgment is not attributed to the condition or preceding cause.
5
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the one who untied the leg iron is not liable (no daman).
Liability falls on the free agent if anyone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی، اور اس شرط پر فاعل مختار کا فعل طاری ہوا ہے، پس اول سبب محض باقی رہا، لہذا تلف فتح کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا، برخلاف کنویں میں گرنے کے کیونکہ گرنے والے کا گرنے میں کوئی اختیار نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس نے اپنے کو خود گرایا ہے تو اس کا خون رائیگاں ہوگا۔ تشریح: اسی اصول پر کہ علت اگر حکم کو قبول کرنے کی صلاحیت رکھتی ہو تو حکم شرط اور سبب کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کسی شخص نے زید کے غلام کی بیڑی کھول دی اور غلام بھاگ گیا، تو بیڑی کھولنے والے پر غلام کی قیمت کا ضمان نہ آئے گا، اس لئے کہ بیڑی کھولنا تو شرط ہے، یہ بیڑی بھاگنے سے مانع تھی تو اس نے کھول کر مانع زائل کر دیا، اور مانع کو زائل کرنے کا نام شرط ہے لیکن بھاگنے کی اصل علت تو فاعل مختار یعنی غلام کا فعل ہے، اور یہ علت ایسی ہے جس کی طرف ہلاک ہونے کا حکم منسوب ہو سکتا ہے، لہذا غلام کے ضائع ہونے کا حکم شرط یعنی بیڑی کھولنے والے کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو گا۔ لیکن بیڑی کھولنا اگر چہ شرط ہے لیکن اس میں سبیت کے معنی ہے کیونکہ سبب حقیقی علت سے پہلے ہوتا ہے جیسے شرط علت سے مؤخر ہوتی ہے، اور یہاں بیڑی کھولنے میں یہ بات ہے کیونکہ بیڑی کھولنا غلام کے بھاگنے پر مقدم ہے جو بھاگنا تلف کی علت ہے، لیکن یہ شرط سبب محض ہے، علت کے معنی اس میں نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جس شرط میں علت کے معنی ہوتے ہیں وہ علت اسی شرط سے پیدا ہوتی ہے، حالانکہ یہاں بھاگنا جو علت ہے، اور بیڑی کھولنے پر پیش آیا وہ بذات خود قائم ہے، وہ شرط سے یعنی بیڑی کھولنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا۔ غرض جب بیڑی کھولنا شرط ہے جو سبب کے معنی میں ہے، نہ کہ علت کے معنی میں، تو حکم کو اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسے جب شرط میں علت کے معنی ہو تو حکم اس شرط کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے، جیسے کنواں کھودنا جو پہلے گذرا، اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے راستہ میں چوپایہ چھوڑ دیا، پھر وہ چوپایہ دائیں بائیں گھوم کر کسی چیز کو تلف کرے، تو چھوڑنے والے پر تلف کا ضمان نہ آئے گا، کیونکہ یہاں جانور کو چھوڑنے اور سامان ہلاک کرنے کے درمیان فاعل مختار یعنی چوپایہ کا فعل ہے، اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہے لیکن یہ بات یاد رکھیں کہ اگر جانور کو جس راستہ پر چھوڑا ہے، اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی راستہ نہ ہو تو مرسل پر تلف کا ضمان آئے گا، اسی طرح اگر جانور دائیں بائیں نہیں گھوما، جس طرف چھوڑا ہے اسی طرف چل کر کوئی چیز تلف کی تو بھی مرسل پر ضمان آئے گا، ان دونوں صورتوں میں مرسل بمنزلہ سائق کے ہوگا اور پہلے پڑھ چکے ہیں کہ سائق پر ضمان آتا ہے۔ پھر ایک سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ بیڑی کھولنا اور جانور کو چھوڑنا دونوں کو آپ نے ایک درجہ میں رکھ دیا حالانکہ بیڑی کھولنا یہ شرط ہے، کیونکہ بیڑی بھاگنے سے مانع تھی تو اس کو کھول کر مانع زائل کردیا اور ازالہ مانع کا نام شرط ہے، اور جانور کو چھوڑنا سبب محض ہے، شرط نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جانور کو چھوڑنے میں ازالہ مانع نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جانور مقید نہیں تھا، تو بیڑی کھولنے کو ارسال کے ساتھ کیسے تشبیہ دی؟ الا ان المرسل سے اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ یہ تشبیہ صرف عدم ضمان میں ہے، یعنی جیسے بیڑی کھولنے والے پر ضمان نہیں ہے، ایسے ہی مرسل پر بھی ضمان نہیں، کیونکہ دونوں میں درمیان میں فاعل مختار کا فعل موجود ہے جو علت ہے، اور جب علت صالح محکم موجود ہے تو حکم سبب اور شرط کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا، غرض دونوں اگر چہ الگ الگ ہیں ایک سبب اور ایک شرط ہے مگر عدم وجوب ضمان میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔
Because of the reason we stated, and upon this condition the act of a free agent occurred, so the first pure cause remained, therefore the destroyed property will not be attributed to the one who dug [the well], unlike falling into a well because the faller has no choice in falling, to the extent that if he threw himself, his blood is wasted. Explanation: On this principle that if the cause is capable of receiving the judgment, the judgment will not be attributed to the condition or cause. We say: A person untied Zayd's slave's leg iron and the slave ran away, so the one who untied the leg iron will not be liable for the slave's value, because untying the leg iron is a condition, it was an obstacle to running away, so he removed the obstacle, and removing an obstacle is called a condition, but the real cause of running away is the act of the free agent, i.e., the slave, and this cause is such that the judgment of destruction can be attributed to it, so the judgment of the slave's loss will not be attributed to the condition, i.e., the one who untied the leg iron. However, untying the leg iron, although it is a condition, has the meaning of a cause because a cause (sabab) precedes the real cause, while a condition is subsequent to the cause. Here untying precedes the slave's running away which is the cause of destruction, but this condition is a pure cause, it does not have the meaning of cause, because when a condition has the meaning of cause, that cause arises from that condition, whereas here running away, which is the cause, occurs after untying but is self-subsisting, it did not arise from the condition of untying. In short, when untying is a condition in the meaning of a cause (sabab), not in the meaning of the real cause, then the judgment will not be attributed to this condition, just as when the condition has the meaning of cause, the judgment is attributed to that condition, like digging a well which passed earlier. Its example is exactly like someone who left an animal loose on the road, then that animal wanders left and right and destroys something, so the one who let it loose will not be liable for the destruction, because here between the releasing of the animal and the destruction of property is the act of a free agent, i.e., the animal. Similarly here. But remember: if the animal is left on a road with no other path, then the releasor will be liable; similarly if the animal does not wander left and right but goes straight and destroys something, then the releasor will also be liable. In both these cases, the releasor is like a driver, and we have already read that the driver is liable. Then a question arises: You have placed untying the leg iron and releasing the animal on the same level, whereas untying the leg iron is a condition because the leg iron was an obstacle to running away, so by untying he removed the obstacle, and removing an obstacle is called a condition, while releasing the animal is a pure cause, not a condition, because releasing the animal does not involve removing an obstacle, since the animal was not tied. So how can untying be analogized to releasing? The answer from 'illa al-mursal is that this analogy is only regarding the absence of liability, i.e., just as the one who untied the leg iron is not liable, similarly the releasor is not liable, because in both cases there is an act of a free agent in between which is the cause, and when a valid, strong cause exists, the judgment will not be attributed to the cause or condition. In short, although one is a cause and the other a condition, they are equal regarding the non-obligation of liability.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage explains a core Hanafi rule in causation: when an action is merely a condition (shart) that removes an obstacle, and the actual destruction is caused by a free agent, liability does not attach to the one who performed the condition. The example: untying a slave's leg iron. The untying is a condition because it removes an obstacle to running away. However, the running away is the act of the slave, a free agent. Since the slave is a free agent, his act is a valid cause to which the loss can be attributed. Therefore, the untying is not considered the cause, and the one who untied is not liable. The text distinguishes between a condition that is in the meaning of a sabab (preceding cause) and a condition that is in the meaning of an illa (true cause). In this case, the condition (untying) precedes the slave's act but does not generate it, so it is a sabab. The true illa is the slave's free choice. The same principle applies to letting an animal loose. The releasor is not liable if the animal wanders and destroys something because the animal's own act is the intervening free agent. However, if the damage is inevitable (e.g., only one road) or the animal goes straight, the releasor becomes like a driver and is liable. A question arises: how can untying (a condition of removing an obstacle) be analogized to releasing (a pure cause)? The answer: the analogy is only in the result of non-liability. Both have an intervening free agent's act. Therefore, despite their conceptual difference, both result in no liability.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition; an action that removes an obstacle (māni‘) to something else, e.g., untying the leg iron which prevented escape.
سبب (sabab): A cause that precedes the true cause but does not generate it; a 'pure cause' (sabab mahḍ) that is not the direct efficient cause.
علت (‘illa): The real cause that directly brings about the effect; here the act of the free agent (fā‘il mukhtār) that causes the loss.
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability for compensation or guarantee; the obligation to pay the value of what is destroyed.
فاعل مختار (fā‘il mukhtār): A free agent capable of choice; an actor whose actions are voluntary and attributable to him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rule explained in this lesson, if a person unties a slave's leg iron and the slave runs away and is lost, who is liable for the loss?
A) The person who untied the leg iron
B) The slave himself
C) The slave's owner
D) No one is liable

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, when a condition removes an obstacle and a free agent causes the loss, liability is on the free agent, not the one who performed the condition.

The Animal Analogy and Exceptions to Non-Liability
Analysing the animal analogy and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a releasor is liable for an animal's destruction and explain the exceptions to non-liability.

Core Idea
Releasing an animal is analogous to untying a slave: non-liability due to intervening free agent, except when damage is inevitable.

This lesson continues the discussion by analogizing untying a slave's leg iron to releasing an animal. The author addresses a question: how can a condition (untying) be analogized to a cause (releasing)? The answer is that the analogy is only in the result of non-liability, because both involve an intervening free agent. However, exceptions exist: if the animal has no alternative path or goes straight, the releasor becomes like a driver and is liable. We will examine these rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two actions being compared
Untying a slave's leg iron (condition) and releasing an animal (pure cause) are compared.
They differ in nature but produce the same legal result in the case of non-liability.
2
Note the question raised
How can a condition be analogized to a cause? The answer: only in the consequence of non-liability.
The intervening free agent's act is present in both.
3
Identify the exceptions
Two exceptions: (a) if the animal is released on a road with no other path, or (b) if the animal goes straight without wandering.
In those cases, the releasor is liable like a driver (sā’iq).
4
Explain why exceptions create liability
In those cases, the animal's act is not a true free choice; it is effectively compelled by the releasor's action.
The rule of intervening free agent does not apply when the damage is inevitable.
5
Apply the rule to the exceptions
If the animal has only one path, the releasor is considered a driver and is liable. Similarly, if the animal goes straight, it is as if the releasor directed it.
The key is whether the animal's movement was free or constrained.

Source Text

کر دیا، اور مانع کو زائل کرنے کا نام شرط ہے لیکن بھاگنے کی اصل علت تو فاعل مختار یعنی غلام کا فعل ہے، اور یہ علت ایسی ہے جس کی طرف ہلاک ہونے کا حکم منسوب ہو سکتا ہے، لہذا غلام کے ضائع ہونے کا حکم شرط یعنی بیڑی کھولنے والے کی طرف منسوب نہ ہو گا۔ لیکن بیڑی کھولنا اگر چہ شرط ہے لیکن اس میں سبیت کے معنی ہے کیونکہ سبب حقیقی علت سے پہلے ہوتا ہے جیسے شرط علت سے مؤخر ہوتی ہے، اور یہاں بیڑی کھولنے میں یہ بات ہے کیونکہ بیڑی کھولنا غلام کے بھاگنے پر مقدم ہے جو بھاگنا تلف کی علت ہے، لیکن یہ شرط سبب محض ہے، علت کے معنی اس میں نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جس شرط میں علت کے معنی ہوتے ہیں وہ علت اسی شرط سے پیدا ہوتی ہے، حالانکہ یہاں بھاگنا جو علت ہے، اور بیڑی کھولنے پر پیش آیا وہ بذات خود قائم ہے، وہ شرط سے یعنی بیڑی کھولنے سے پیدا نہیں ہوا۔ غرض جب بیڑی کھولنا شرط ہے جو سبب کے معنی میں ہے، نہ کہ علت کے معنی میں، تو حکم کو اس شرط کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا جائے گا جیسے جب شرط میں علت کے معنی ہو تو حکم اس شرط کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے، جیسے کنواں کھودنا جو پہلے گذرا، اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے جیسے کسی نے راستہ میں چوپایہ چھوڑ دیا، پھر وہ چوپایہ دائیں بائیں گھوم کر کسی چیز کو تلف کرے، تو چھوڑنے والے پر تلف کا ضمان نہ آئے گا، کیونکہ یہاں جانور کو چھوڑنے اور سامان ہلاک کرنے کے درمیان فاعل مختار یعنی چوپایہ کا فعل ہے، اسی طرح یہاں بھی ہے لیکن یہ بات یاد رکھیں کہ اگر جانور کو جس راستہ پر چھوڑا ہے، اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی راستہ نہ ہو تو مرسل پر تلف کا ضمان آئے گا، اسی طرح اگر جانور دائیں بائیں نہیں گھوما، جس طرف چھوڑا ہے اسی طرف چل کر کوئی چیز تلف کی تو بھی مرسل پر ضمان آئے گا، ان دونوں صورتوں میں مرسل بمنزلہ سائق کے ہوگا اور پہلے پڑھ چکے ہیں کہ سائق پر ضمان آتا ہے۔ پھر ایک سوال پیدا ہوتا ہے کہ بیڑی کھولنا اور جانور کو چھوڑنا دونوں کو آپ نے ایک درجہ میں رکھ دیا حالانکہ بیڑی کھولنا یہ شرط ہے، کیونکہ بیڑی بھاگنے سے مانع تھی تو اس کو کھول کر مانع زائل کردیا اور ازالہ مانع کا نام شرط ہے، اور جانور کو چھوڑنا سبب محض ہے، شرط نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جانور کو چھوڑنے میں ازالہ مانع نہیں ہے، کیونکہ جانور مقید نہیں تھا، تو بیڑی کھولنے کو ارسال کے ساتھ کیسے تشبیہ دی؟ الا ان المرسل سے اس کا جواب دے رہے ہیں کہ یہ تشبیہ صرف عدم ضمان میں ہے، یعنی جیسے بیڑی کھولنے والے پر ضمان نہیں ہے، ایسے ہی مرسل پر بھی ضمان نہیں، کیونکہ دونوں میں درمیان میں فاعل مختار کا فعل موجود ہے جو علت ہے، اور جب علت صالح محکم موجود ہے تو حکم سبب اور شرط کی طرف منسوب نہ ہوگا، غرض دونوں اگر چہ الگ الگ ہیں ایک سبب اور ایک شرط ہے مگر عدم وجوب ضمان میں دونوں برابر ہیں۔
Because of the reason we stated, and upon this condition the act of a free agent occurred, so the first pure cause remained, therefore the destroyed property will not be attributed to the one who dug [the well], unlike falling into a well because the faller has no choice in falling, to the extent that if he threw himself, his blood is wasted. Explanation: On this principle that if the cause is capable of receiving the judgment, the judgment will not be attributed to the condition or cause. We say: A person untied Zayd's slave's leg iron and the slave ran away, so the one who untied the leg iron will not be liable for the slave's value, because untying the leg iron is a condition, it was an obstacle to running away, so he removed the obstacle, and removing an obstacle is called a condition, but the real cause of running away is the act of the free agent, i.e., the slave, and this cause is such that the judgment of destruction can be attributed to it, so the judgment of the slave's loss will not be attributed to the condition, i.e., the one who untied the leg iron. However, untying the leg iron, although it is a condition, has the meaning of a cause because a cause (sabab) precedes the real cause, while a condition is subsequent to the cause. Here untying precedes the slave's running away which is the cause of destruction, but this condition is a pure cause, it does not have the meaning of cause, because when a condition has the meaning of cause, that cause arises from that condition, whereas here running away, which is the cause, occurs after untying but is self-subsisting, it did not arise from the condition of untying. In short, when untying is a condition in the meaning of a cause (sabab), not in the meaning of the real cause, then the judgment will not be attributed to this condition, just as when the condition has the meaning of cause, the judgment is attributed to that condition, like digging a well which passed earlier. Its example is exactly like someone who left an animal loose on the road, then that animal wanders left and right and destroys something, so the one who let it loose will not be liable for the destruction, because here between the releasing of the animal and the destruction of property is the act of a free agent, i.e., the animal. Similarly here. But remember: if the animal is left on a road with no other path, then the releasor will be liable; similarly if the animal does not wander left and right but goes straight and destroys something, then the releasor will also be liable. In both these cases, the releasor is like a driver, and we have already read that the driver is liable. Then a question arises: You have placed untying the leg iron and releasing the animal on the same level, whereas untying the leg iron is a condition because the leg iron was an obstacle to running away, so by untying he removed the obstacle, and removing an obstacle is called a condition, while releasing the animal is a pure cause, not a condition, because releasing the animal does not involve removing an obstacle, since the animal was not tied. So how can untying be analogized to releasing? The answer from 'illa al-mursal is that this analogy is only regarding the absence of liability, i.e., just as the one who untied the leg iron is not liable, similarly the releasor is not liable, because in both cases there is an act of a free agent in between which is the cause, and when a valid, strong cause exists, the judgment will not be attributed to the cause or condition. In short, although one is a cause and the other a condition, they are equal regarding the non-obligation of liability.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage explains a core Hanafi rule in causation: when an action is merely a condition (shart) that removes an obstacle, and the actual destruction is caused by a free agent, liability does not attach to the one who performed the condition. The example: untying a slave's leg iron. The untying is a condition because it removes an obstacle to running away. However, the running away is the act of the slave, a free agent. Since the slave is a free agent, his act is a valid cause to which the loss can be attributed. Therefore, the untying is not considered the cause, and the one who untied is not liable. The text distinguishes between a condition that is in the meaning of a sabab (preceding cause) and a condition that is in the meaning of an illa (true cause). In this case, the condition (untying) precedes the slave's act but does not generate it, so it is a sabab. The true illa is the slave's free choice. The same principle applies to letting an animal loose. The releasor is not liable if the animal wanders and destroys something because the animal's own act is the intervening free agent. However, if the damage is inevitable (e.g., only one road) or the animal goes straight, the releasor becomes like a driver and is liable. A question arises: how can untying (a condition of removing an obstacle) be analogized to releasing (a pure cause)? The answer: the analogy is only in the result of non-liability. Both have an intervening free agent's act. Therefore, despite their conceptual difference, both result in no liability.

Key Terms
سائق (sā’iq): A driver; in fiqh, one who drives an animal and is liable for its destruction if it causes damage.
مرسل (mursil): One who releases an animal; the releasor.
ازالہ مانع (izālat māni‘): Removal of an obstacle; the defining characteristic of a condition (shart).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which scenario is a person who releases an animal NOT liable for damage caused by the animal according to the Hanafi rule?
A) The animal is released on a road with no other path and goes straight
B) The animal wanders left and right on a road with many paths
C) The animal is released on a narrow bridge and goes straight
D) The animal is released in a confined space with only one exit

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule on animal release: no liability if an intervening free agent exists, unless the damage is inevitable (no alternative path or direct movement).

Istihsan — Juristic Preference
